- **Tests.** 119 new tests across four files: `tests/test_hvac_schedule_extraction.py` (81 tests covering all eleven keyword variants, header-heuristic disqualifiers against lighting / door / panel headers, every cell parser including the dual-form voltage round-trip and the fractional HP parser, every single-letter header collision scenario including the four-way TWO-PASS validation, single + multi-equipment extraction across all seven equipment families, QTY vs. no-QTY routing, capacity-unit detection for TONS / CFM / MBH / GPM / BTUH, refrigerant / fuel-type detection, the `extract_hvac_schedule_from_page` + `extract_hvac_schedule` disk-path entry points, the `to_schema` Pydantic bridge, end-to-end through `prepass_drawing_pdf`, and the confidence-scoring envelope), `tests/test_hvac_takeoff_synthesis.py` (26 tests across the per-family fan-out shape — AHU / RTU with QTY → 3 items, VAV / BOILER → 2 items no disconnect, PUMP / CHILLER / FAN with motor → 3 items — CSI mapping for every equipment type, confidence calibration at every threshold, the source-tag / role / sheet-id notes contract, and the schedule-result-wrapper accepting variant), `tests/test_hvac_dedupe.py` (8 tests including the per-equipment-tag suppression sweep, three cross-pollination guards against plumbing / lighting / panel rows, the empty-synthesis preserve-all contract, and the anchored-aggregate-regex unrelated-23 preservation test), `tests/test_takeoff_t2_8_integration.py` (4 end-to-end tests through `prepass_drawing_page` + `reconcile()`, including a mechanical + lighting + panel three-discipline-coexist test and the T6 banding contracts for the LS rough-in row → HAND_TAKEOFF, the EA disconnect row → OPERATOR_REVIEW, and the QTY-present equipment row → AUTO_APPROVE).

**Known limitations of this slice:**
- **Rough-in LS quantity is always 1.0.** A single AHU and a 50-AHU campus chiller plant both synthesise the same `1 LS @ 23 05 00 @ conf 0.45` row. The estimator catches both in the HAND queue, but the worklist doesn't tell the operator that the 50-AHU plant needs proportionally more ductwork takeoff effort. A future enhancement could scale the rough-in LS quantity by the equipment count or by aggregate CFM / tonnage.
- **No fuel-line / refrigerant-piping synthesis.** GAS-fired boilers imply a `22 11 13` gas-supply line; refrigerant-bearing chillers imply a `23 23 00` refrigerant-piping line; neither is synthesised here. Both would land naturally as a fourth `TakeoffItem` family per record (`23 23 00` Refrigerant Piping, `22 11 13` Facility Natural-Gas Piping) when the relevant attribute is set.
- **Pump CSI is one-bucket.** All pumps land at `23 22 23` (HVAC HW). A domestic-water booster pump on a plumbing-schedule page (T2.9 candidate) will need its own `22 11 23` extractor; the current HVAC slice will misclassify it if a plumbing-schedule extractor doesn't ship before a domestic-water pump appears on the calibration set.
- **No equipment-curve / capacity-unit normalisation.** TONS / CFM / MBH / GPM / BTUH are stored as-extracted strings; we don't normalise (e.g. convert TONS to BTUH using the 12,000 BTU/ton conversion). Pricing downstream uses the CSI section + family-default lookup, not the capacity value, so this doesn't break the takeoff flow — but it limits future "price-per-ton" parametric work.

**Most fragile parsing case observed:** The fractional-HP cell parser (`_parse_hp` with `1/2` / `1/4 HP`). The current implementation handles `1/2`, `1/4`, `3/4`, `1/8` via a regex-then-divide path, but a schedule that publishes `0.5 HP` (decimal form) is the dominant case in practice and goes through the standard numeric parser instead. The fragility is mostly in HVAC schedules that mix decimal and fractional forms across rows in the same table (a calibration-set boiler-room schedule had `0.5 HP` for the circulating pump and `1/4 HP` for the air-handler dampers) — both parse correctly, but the test corpus has only the synthetic case and a real-bid free-text HP cell with a mixed unit (`3/4 HP (0.75 kW)`) is the most likely place this leaks.

**Validation outcomes (per brief return-list):**
- **`header_index_excluding` collisions fired in test corpus.** Yes — `T`/`TONS`, `H`/`HP`, `V`/`VOLTAGE`, `Q`/`QUANTITY` all fired (six dedicated regression tests). The TWO-PASS orchestration (pin every long-form first, then every short-form with all long-forms excluded) was necessary — the one-pair-at-a-time pattern from lighting / panel had bare `T` stealing `VOLTAGE` because `T` substring-matches `VOLTAGE` and lighting's `W` doesn't substring-match `VOLTAGE`, so this collision was novel to HVAC. The two-pass pattern is the new portable shape going forward.
- **CSI mapping decisions per equipment type.** Eight family mappings; one ambiguity (PUMP → `23 22 23` HVAC vs. `22 11 23` domestic; defaulted to HVAC because source is an HVAC schedule). All eight mappings tested via `test_csi_mapping_per_equipment_type`. Other-bucket (`23 00 00`) catches the long tail.
- **VAV / BOILER disconnect-skip rationale.** Matches brief: VAV is duct-fed (no motor disconnect needed) and boilers ship with integrated controls. Both skips validated by dedicated tests.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T2.9 — Plumbing fixture schedule.** Domestic water + sanitary + storm fixture schedules on P-series sheets. CSI Division 22 (`22 40 00` plumbing fixtures parent; `22 41 00` residential / `22 42 00` commercial / `22 45 00` emergency-shower per fixture type). 1-to-1 EA synthesis with parametric supply/waste rough-in LS row. Same dispatcher shape; would close the Division 22 + 23 + 26 + plumbing trifecta started in T2.6 / T2.7 / T2.8 and is the natural fifth downstream validation of the now-load-bearing `header_index_excluding` helper.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T2.9 section below.
- ~~**Phase T6.1 — Confidence-propagation cleanup.** The `confidence` field is now set by every T1–T2.9 extractor + synthesiser, but the `_derive_takeoffs` legacy LLM path still emits `0.7` by default. A consistency pass to map LLM-row confidences from their underlying `extraction_confidence` (when available) into the `TakeoffItem.confidence` field would tighten the HAND queue further. BB's confidence-propagation notes (referenced in the T7 wiring commit) outline the specific edit points.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T6.1 section below.
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote integration.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup for mechanical equipment ("see attached AHU quote from Trane"); pricing these against a vendor quote PDF instead of the CWICR catalog would replace the synthesised parametric EA price with the real sub-quote price + markup. This is the natural complement to T2.8 (which currently uses the seed DB / CWICR for HVAC EA pricing).

### Phase T6.1 — Confidence-propagation cleanup + MANUAL_OVERRIDE wire-in

**Status:** SHIPPED — quality slice between T2.8 (HVAC) and T2.9 (plumbing). Closes four issues Workers W and BB flagged after the T6 / T7 calibration shipped: (1) hard-coded derived-item confidences in synthesis, (2) missing chain-derivation decay in backfill, (3) CWICR-min-similarity vs. T6 / T7 band misalignment (Issues 3a + 3b), and (4) `MANUAL_OVERRIDE` end-to-end wire-in. Suite: 1432 → 1498 (+66 tests across two new files plus ~5 extensions to the CWICR-integration suite; 1 skipped unchanged). Five pre-existing tests in T2.6 / T2.7 / T2.8 were updated to reflect the new propagation rules — every adjustment documented inline in this section.

**Issue 1 — Synth derived-item confidence inheritance.** Worker W flagged that secondary / unit-converted items (panel branch breakers from the parent panel record, fixture lamp/driver from the parent fixture row, equipment disconnect+flex from the parent HVAC row) used a hard-coded `0.85` / fixture-default / `0.70` confidence regardless of how confident the underlying source record actually was — a 0.95-source row produced an 0.85-confidence derived row that landed in `OPERATOR_REVIEW` instead of `AUTO_APPROVE`, even though the derived count is uniquely determined by the source. The fix introduces `inherit_with_haircut(source_confidence) = max(0.45, source_confidence × 0.95)` in `core/extraction/takeoff_synthesis.py` and applies it to the three secondary-item paths (panel branch breakers, lighting lamps, HVAC disconnect+flex). Primary items (door enclosure, window enclosure, panel enclosure, fixture EA, equipment EA) keep their unmodified source confidence — the haircut only applies to *secondary / derived* rows. Parametric placeholders (panel feeder LF at 0.55, HVAC MEP rough-in LS at 0.45) keep their epistemological flat values because their uncertainty isn't about derivation depth, it's about the operator needing to walk the riser / plan to fill the real quantity in. **Audit count:** three hard-coded `0.85` / `0.70` values found and replaced (one per electrical / lighting / HVAC discipline). Door + window + finish synthesis already routed enclosure rows through the source confidence directly (no derivation step) so no change there.

**Issue 2 — Chain-derivation decay helper.** Worker W flagged that chained derivations (e.g. paint second-coat from wall area + primer + tape) reuse the parent's confidence verbatim instead of degrading slightly per derivation step — *"Optimistic, not wrong."* The fix exposes `chain_decay(parent_confidence, depth)` in `core/extraction/takeoff_backfill.py` with multipliers `(1.00, 0.95, 0.90, 0.85)` and a 0.45 floor. **Audit count:** the current backfill pipeline is a 1:1 transformer (wall → SF, base → LF, ceiling → SF) with no real multi-step fan-out, so `chain_decay` is exposed for *future* N-from-one paint primer / topcoat / joint-tape derivations to call into without re-deriving the multipliers. The geometry-fallback case in `_backfill_wall` and `_backfill_base` keeps its conservative 0.65 flat value because the 0.65 is calibrated for the *geometric approximation* uncertainty (`perimeter ≈ 4 × √area`), not for chain depth — see the module docstring.

**Issue 3a — CWICR_MIN_SIMILARITY raised 0.55 → 0.75.** Worker BB flagged that CWICR similarity 0.55 (the legacy default) lands in `INTERPOLATED @ price_conf=0.65`; combined with default qty 0.7 produces 0.455 → `HAND_TAKEOFF`. So a barely-above-threshold CWICR hit on a default-confidence takeoff bands into HAND post-T7. The new 0.75 default aligns the matcher floor with the `CATEGORY_MATCH` boundary — any line that survives the matcher is at least `CATEGORY_MATCH` quality (price_conf ≥ 0.75 × 0.85 = 0.6375). The `CWICR_MIN_SIMILARITY` env var still honours operator overrides for backtesting (set to 0.55 to reproduce the pre-T6.1 behaviour).

**Issue 3b — LLM-no-confidence default raised 0.70 → 0.80.** The schema-level `TakeoffItem.confidence` and `CostLine.confidence` defaults are preserved at `0.70` per the no-touch-schemas constraint (Worker DD owns the schema slice for T2.9). Instead, `core/estimator.py:_combined_band` now uses `LLM_DEFAULT_QTY_CONFIDENCE = 0.80` only when `qty_confidence is None` — the legacy LLM-emitted-no-confidence path. This puts default LLM lines at the `OPERATOR_REVIEW` band boundary (still below `AUTO_APPROVE`'s 0.85 threshold) so a no-confidence-from-LLM line lands in REVIEW instead of the pre-T6.1 HAND.

**Issue 4 — MANUAL_OVERRIDE end-to-end.** `core/estimator.py:apply_manual_override(estimate, line_id, new_unit_cost, operator_note=None) → Estimate` lets operator-vouched prices propagate through the round-trip. Returns a *new* Estimate (immutable; the input is preserved for rollback / diff) with one `CostLine` replaced: `unit_cost` updated, `total_cost` recomputed (= `unit_cost × quantity`), `cost_source_tier = MANUAL_OVERRIDE`, `price_confidence = 1.0`, `cost_band` recomputed against the new combined confidence, `suppressed = False` (hand-pricing IS the resolution to a unit-mismatch suppression), and `notes` updated with the `"operator override"` sentinel prefix so downstream readers (Excel / PDF / Streamlit) can detect the override. `line_id` accepts an `int` index (negative-index OK) or a `str` matching a unique `cost_source` / `description` value; ambiguous matches raise `ValueError`. `apply_manual_override` is *idempotent* under same-arguments re-application except for the optional `operator_note`, which is appended once per call with a non-empty value (so retries should pass `operator_note=None` to avoid bloating the notes blob). **The Streamlit UI wiring is intentionally deferred to T6.2** — this slice exposes the function only.

#### T6.1 Calibration Notes

The T6 / T7 band thresholds are AUTO ≥ 0.85 / REVIEW ≥ 0.65 / HAND otherwise. After the T6.1 raises, the calibration math is:

| Source | qty_conf | price_conf | combined | band |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Default LLM line + min-similarity CWICR (`CATEGORY_MATCH @ 0.75 × 0.85`) | 0.80 | 0.6375 | 0.51 | HAND_TAKEOFF |
| Default LLM line + EXACT_MATCH CWICR (`0.95 × 0.95`) | 0.80 | 0.9025 | 0.722 | OPERATOR_REVIEW |
| Default LLM line + seed-DB hit (price_conf 0.95) | 0.80 | 0.95 | 0.76 | OPERATOR_REVIEW |
| Schema-default takeoff (0.70) + EXACT CWICR | 0.70 | 0.9025 | 0.632 | HAND_TAKEOFF |
| Schema-default takeoff (0.70) + seed-DB hit | 0.70 | 0.95 | 0.665 | OPERATOR_REVIEW |
| High-confidence T1–T5.1 typed-extractor line (0.92) + EXACT CWICR | 0.92 | 0.9025 | 0.830 | OPERATOR_REVIEW |
| High-confidence (0.92) + seed-DB hit | 0.92 | 0.95 | 0.874 | AUTO_APPROVE |
| Manual-override on any line | (preserved) | 1.0 | qty × 1.0 | qty determines |

Worker BB's intended outcome is captured: a barely-above-threshold CWICR hit on a default-confidence takeoff still flags for review (HAND_TAKEOFF) because *both* defaults are at boundaries — the combined number is at boundaries too. The high-confidence typed-extractor lines (panel + door + window + finish + lighting + HVAC at 0.90+) plus a seed-DB or near-EXACT CWICR hit reliably land in AUTO_APPROVE post-T6.1, which is the design target.

**Pre-existing tests adjusted** (5 total — every adjustment is a fixture-drift consequence of the propagation rules, not a functional regression):
1. `tests/test_panel_takeoff_synthesis.py::test_branch_breakers_confidence_is_panel_data_high` — breaker rows: hard-coded `0.85` → inherit-with-haircut `0.8075` (= `0.85 × 0.95`).
2. `tests/test_hvac_takeoff_synthesis.py::test_ahu_with_qty_emits_three_items` — disconnect with QTY-published equipment (0.90 parent): hard-coded `0.70` → `0.855` (= `0.90 × 0.95`).
3. `tests/test_hvac_takeoff_synthesis.py::test_disconnect_confidence_lands_at_070` (renamed `_inherits_equipment_haircut`) — disconnect with no-QTY AHU (0.55 parent): hard-coded `0.70` → `0.5225` (= `0.55 × 0.95`, floor 0.45).
4. `tests/test_lighting_takeoff_synthesis.py::test_synthesize_lamp_inherits_fixture_confidence` (renamed `_ea_row_confidence_with_haircut`) — lamp inherits the *EA row's* QTY-aware confidence (0.55 hand-takeoff or 0.90 QTY-published) instead of the record's raw `confidence` field. Now lands at `0.5225` for the no-QTY fluorescent fixture.
5. `tests/test_takeoff_t2_8_integration.py::test_roughin_rows_route_to_hand_takeoff_band` — disconnect band: REVIEW → HAND for a no-QTY AHU schedule (0.55 parent → 0.5225 disconnect → HAND), which is the *correct* cascade behaviour: a hand-takeoff parent should never AUTO_APPROVE its derivations.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T6.2 — Streamlit `MANUAL_OVERRIDE` UI.** Wire `apply_manual_override` into the Streamlit "Recalculate totals" round-trip so an operator can hand-price a HAND_TAKEOFF row directly in the UI. Should use the operator-note field for vendor / source attribution.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T6.2 section below.
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote integration.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup for mechanical equipment (Trane / Carrier AHU quotes). MANUAL_OVERRIDE is the manual single-line variant; T8 wires up bulk PDF-quote ingestion + line-by-line markup application.
- **Phase T9 — Alternates / VE pricing.** Each `BidPackage` carries an `alternates` field that's currently informational; T9 would wire pricing branches per alternate and surface the delta in the headline.

### Phase T6.2 — Streamlit operator price-override UI

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit wires the T6.1 `apply_manual_override()` function into the Streamlit Estimate tab as a first-class operator affordance with vendor / quote-ref attribution, override history, audit-trail CSV export, and a single-button reset path. Suite: 1590 → 1621 (+31 tests; 1 skipped unchanged). Pure UI slice — `core/estimator.py`, `core/schemas.py`, exporters, and every `core/extraction/*` / `core/pricing/*` module remain untouched.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Pure-helper factoring (testability).** Streamlit's `AppTest` harness does not cleanly support form-submit round-trips on a heavy app like `app.py` (the analyze pipeline path requires real PDFs / LLM calls / pricing). Per the brief's "factor the override-application logic into pure helper functions ... and test those exhaustively" guidance, the override surface is split into six pure helpers in `app.py` — `_format_operator_note`, `_select_line_label`, `_sort_lines_by_tier`, `_format_override_delta`, `_apply_operator_override`, and `_build_override_history_csv` — plus an `_initialize_override_session_state` seed helper. The Streamlit form is a thin wrapper that (1) collects input, (2) hands it to `_apply_operator_override`, and (3) renders the result; every interesting code path is exercised by `tests/test_streamlit_override_ui.py` without spinning up Streamlit at all. A smoke `import app` covers the form wiring itself.
- **Operator-note format.** `[vendor: <vendor>] [quote-ref: <quote_ref>] <free_text>` — empty fields are skipped (no double-space gaps), all-empty input collapses to `None` so the underlying override pass falls back to the bare `MANUAL_OVERRIDE_NOTE_PREFIX` sentinel ("operator override"). Pinned by `test_format_operator_note_*` (7 tests).
- **Line-selector dropdown.** Tier-sorted: MANUAL_OVERRIDE first (operator-touched rows surface immediately), then EXACT → CATEGORY → INTERPOLATED → PARAMETRIC → MISSING. Stable-sorted within each tier so two same-tier rows preserve physical order. Label format: `#<idx> | <description, truncated to 60 chars> | $<unit_cost>/<unit> | <tier label>`. The leading `#<idx>` is the stable line identifier the override pass consumes (CostLine has no `entity_id` field per the T7 schema; `apply_manual_override` accepts an int index OR a `cost_source` / `description` string, but ambiguity from duplicate descriptions is dodged by always passing the index back to the function).
- **Session-state design.** Three keys total. `st.session_state["estimate"]` already existed — mutated atomically on each successful override via `st.session_state["estimate"] = new_estimate` followed by `st.rerun()`. Two new keys: `estimate_original` (deep-copy snapshot of the post-analyze estimate, used for delta computation + reset) and `override_history` (list of dicts: `{timestamp, line_index, description, csi_division, csi_section, original_unit_cost, new_unit_cost, operator_note}`, appended on each successful override; used for the CSV download). Seeded at analyze time via `_initialize_override_session_state` and defensively re-seeded inside the Estimate tab so a session that predates T6.2 (e.g. an estimate left in `st.session_state` from a prior streamlit run) still works cleanly without an analyze re-trigger.
- **Reset strategy: single global "Reset all overrides" button** (per the brief's "pick the simpler option and document the choice" guidance). Restores the pre-override snapshot captured at analyze time and clears the override history. A per-line stack-based reset would require tracking the prior estimate per override application and would push session-state complexity past the simplification line for this slice. Per-line reset is a viable T6.3 follow-up if operators ask for it.
- **Override-history CSV export.** Header-fixed (`timestamp / line_index / description / csi_division / csi_section / original_unit_cost / new_unit_cost / operator_note`) so a downstream auditor can rely on the column shape. Empty history emits a header-only CSV (still a valid file). Original-unit-cost is pulled from the snapshot when the index aligns; for a pre-T6.2 session where the snapshot was seeded after-the-fact, the snapshot's current value is used (one-time edge case). Embedded commas in the operator note round-trip via `csv.DictWriter`'s default `QUOTE_MINIMAL` quoting. The download button is `disabled=True` when no MANUAL_OVERRIDE-tier lines exist, so the operator gets a no-op-disabled button rather than a zero-row download. Pinned by 4 CSV-shape tests.
- **Top-of-section banner.** When ≥ 1 MANUAL_OVERRIDE-tier line exists, an `st.info` banner above the override expander reports the count + the cumulative dollar adjustment (`+$X` or `−$X`) vs. the original estimate. Cheap visual signal that overrides are in flight; opt-in to the existing T6 / T7 visual vocabulary (no row-level highlighting or diff toggle this slice — the brief's "optional polish" knobs are deliberately deferred to T6.3 follow-up so the slice stays thin).
- **Form atomicity.** `st.form` + `st.form_submit_button` keeps the four input widgets (line selector, unit cost, vendor, quote-ref, free-text) atomic — Streamlit batches widget changes until submission, so an operator can edit the unit cost AND fill in the vendor before either touches the underlying estimate. `clear_on_submit=False` so an operator can iterate (e.g. apply a wrong override, then reset and try again) without re-typing the vendor each time.
- **Error surface.** A `ValueError` from `apply_manual_override` (negative unit cost, line index out of range, ambiguous string match) is caught at the form-submit boundary and rendered via `st.error(f"Override failed: {exc}")`; no stack trace, no estimate mutation, the snapshot stays intact. Pinned by `test_apply_operator_override_propagates_value_error_*` (2 tests).
- **Edge cases handled:** zero unit cost (allowed — legitimate giveaway / cost-recovered value); idempotent re-application (re-running the same override with no operator note grows the notes blob by one sentinel only on the first call, per T6.1's idempotency contract); deep-copy snapshot guard (mutating the live estimate post-snapshot does NOT echo into `estimate_original`, pinned by `test_initialize_override_session_state_seeds_snapshot_and_history`).
- **Edge cases NOT handled (deferred):** a scaled / regional unit-cost prefill (the form defaults to the line's current `unit_cost`; a vendor quote in a different region would need manual region-multiplier mental math); per-line reset stack (single global reset only — see "Reset strategy" above); override against a SUPPRESSED line via the dropdown is currently visible but the brief did not call it out — it works correctly because `apply_manual_override` clears `suppressed=False` automatically, so a suppressed line gets resurrected into the headline by the override; row-level highlighting in the priced-line-items data editor is deferred (the operator gets a `[MANUAL]` cue via the leading dropdown sort + the cost_source_tier badge in the data editor's existing rendering, plus the top-of-section banner).
- **Imports added.** `csv`, `io`, `datetime.datetime` (stdlib only — no new third-party deps per the brief constraint). `apply_manual_override` and `MANUAL_OVERRIDE_NOTE_PREFIX` from `core.estimator`; `CostLine` from `core.schemas`.

**Files modified:** 2.
- `app.py` — +6 helper functions, +1 session-state seed call after analyze run, +1 "Operator price overrides" expander section in the Estimate tab (post-suppressed, pre-totals).
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — this section + a strikethrough on the T6.1 next-slice predicting T6.2.

**Files created:** 1.
- `tests/test_streamlit_override_ui.py` — 31 tests across the six pure helpers + two integration shapes (full-helper-chain simulation, session-state seed). Streamlit-free; runs in 0.5s on a stock developer laptop.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `app.py` and the existing T6.1 `tests/test_manual_override.py` continues to pass byte-identically against the unchanged `apply_manual_override` contract. Suite: 1590 passed, 1 skipped → 1621 passed, 1 skipped.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T6.3 — Batch override from CSV.** Upload a vendor-pricing spreadsheet (`description / unit_cost / vendor / quote_ref` columns), match each row to a CostLine by description fuzzy-match (CWICR-shaped, with a similarity floor), and apply overrides across all matched lines in one pass. Natural extension of the T6.2 single-line affordance; the per-line override semantics are already pinned, so T6.3 is mostly the matcher + the bulk-apply UI. Highest leverage when an operator has a real subcontractor quote with 50+ line items.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T6.3 section below.
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote integration.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup for mechanical equipment (Trane / Carrier AHU quotes). MANUAL_OVERRIDE is the manual single-line variant (T6.1) + the manual UI variant (this slice); T8 wires up bulk PDF-quote ingestion + line-by-line markup application. Pairs naturally with the T6.3 matcher above (same fuzzy-match-by-description scaffold, different input shape: PDF instead of CSV).
- **Phase T9 — Alternates / VE pricing.** Each `BidPackage` carries an `alternates` field that's currently informational; T9 would wire pricing branches per alternate and surface the delta in the headline.

---

### Phase T6.3 — Batch operator overrides from vendor CSV

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit wires a fuzzy-match + bulk-apply pipeline on top of the T6.1 `apply_manual_override()` primitive and the T6.2 single-line Streamlit affordance. The operator uploads a vendor pricing CSV, the matcher reconciles each row to a CostLine by description, the UI previews the match plan with per-row status / similarity / alternates, the operator resolves any AMBIGUOUS rows, and a single Apply button commits every MATCHED + resolved row in one pass. **Closes the operator-override family entirely:** T6.1 (the override primitive) → T6.2 (single-line UI) → T6.3 (bulk CSV ingestion). Pure-UI + pure-logic slice — `core/estimator.py`, `core/schemas.py`, exporters, and every `core/extraction/*` / `core/pricing/cwicr_matcher.py` module remain untouched. Suite: 1747 → 1805 (+58 tests across two new files; 1 skipped unchanged).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Module layout.** New pure-logic module `core/pricing/batch_override.py` (~590 LOC, stdlib-only — `csv` + `difflib` + `io` + `re` + `dataclasses` + `enum`). Three dataclasses (`BatchOverrideRow`, `BatchMatchResult`, `BatchOverridePlan`) + one enum (`BatchMatchStatus`) + four pure functions (`parse_vendor_csv`, `match_cost_lines`, `apply_batch_plan`, `export_match_plan_csv`) + one helper (`format_batch_operator_note`). No Streamlit, no I/O, no file-system reads — pass CSV text in, get a match plan out. Streamlit wrapper in `app.py` is a thin two-stage form (preview → apply) wrapping these helpers.
- **Fuzzy-match algorithm choice.** `difflib.SequenceMatcher.ratio()` over `rapidfuzz` / `fuzzywuzzy` / TF-IDF cosine for two reasons: (1) **stdlib-only constraint** per the brief — no new third-party dependency — and (2) **right-sized for the input.** A typical vendor CSV is 5-100 rows matched against 50-2,000 CostLines, so the O(N×M) sequence-matcher loop runs in well under a second even at the upper bound (no embedding model to load, no TF-IDF index to build). The CWICR matcher (`core/pricing/cwicr_matcher.py`) uses TF-IDF + MiniLM embeddings, but it's matching against a 55k-row corpus — the right tool for that scale, the wrong tool for ours.
- **Normalisation rules applied before match.** Five steps in order: (1) strip leading CSI section prefix via `_CSI_PREFIX_RE`; (2) lowercase; (3) replace punctuation with whitespace; (4) collapse whitespace runs to a single space; (5) `strip()`. Documented in `_normalise_description`. The CSI-prefix stripper accepts all three formats the brief asks about: `26 27 26 -`, `26 27 26.13 -`, AND `26 27 26.13 - ` (trailing whitespace is consumed by the regex's trailing `\s*`). The regex also accepts en-dash (`\u2013`) and em-dash (`\u2014`) separators because operators sometimes paste descriptions through tools that auto-promote `-` to a typographic dash. **Conservative**: the separator is REQUIRED so a numeric-looking description like "100 200 300 mph" is not mis-stripped. Three regression tests pin all three formats individually (`test_csi_prefix_stripped_before_match`, `test_csi_prefix_with_extension_stripped`, `test_csi_prefix_with_trailing_space_stripped`).
- **Default thresholds: 0.65 similarity, 0.10 ambiguity margin.** The 0.65 similarity threshold deliberately matches the Phase T6 `OPERATOR_REVIEW` band lower bound (`COST_BAND_REVIEW_THRESHOLD` in `core/schemas.py`) — a 0.65-similarity match is precisely the operator-review-or-better boundary the existing pricing pipeline uses for "good enough to ship pending review". A row landing exactly at threshold gets the same human-review attention a 0.65-confidence priced line gets, so the operator's mental model stays consistent. The 0.10 ambiguity margin is calibrated against the BPC calibration set: wide enough that "Interior latex paint, walls" vs. "Interior latex paint, ceiling" (typical sim delta ~0.07) is correctly flagged AMBIGUOUS, but narrow enough that "Door 101A" vs. "Door 201A" (typical sim delta ~0.20) auto-resolves. The UI surfaces both knobs as sliders inside an "advanced" expander so a power user can tune up or down without touching code.
- **Match status decision tree (`_classify_match`).** Priority order: `best_sim < 0.40` → NO_MATCH; `best_sim < threshold` → LOW_SIMILARITY; `(best_sim - runner_up_sim) < margin` → AMBIGUOUS; else MATCHED. The 0.40 NO_MATCH floor is the bright line for "nothing useful here" — below it the matcher emits a `best_match_index=None` and the UI shows the row as read-only audit only. Only MATCHED + operator-resolved-AMBIGUOUS rows are ever auto-applied; LOW_SIMILARITY + NO_MATCH never auto-apply.
- **Quantity tiebreaker.** Optional `quantity` column on the CSV (alias: `qty` / `q`). When supplied AND a candidate's quantity matches to within 5%, the candidate's effective similarity gets a +0.02 multiplicative nudge (capped at 1.0). Small enough never to push a sub-threshold row over threshold on its own; just enough to resolve a `0.65 vs 0.66` tie in favour of the row whose quantity matches. Documented in `_qty_tiebreaker`. **Note:** quantity is NOT applied to the unit cost or override math — it's a tiebreaker only.
- **Operator-note format.** `[batch] [vendor: <vendor>] [quote-ref: <quote_ref>] [csv-row: N] <free_text>` — `[batch]` always leads (signals the override came from a CSV upload), `[csv-row: N]` is always present (every row has a known CSV row index), the other fields appear only when populated. `apply_manual_override` prefixes the whole string with `MANUAL_OVERRIDE_NOTE_PREFIX` ("operator override") so the stamped `notes` field reads `operator override: [batch] [vendor: ...] [csv-row: N] ...`. Pinned by `test_format_batch_operator_note_all_fields` + `test_apply_operator_note_carries_batch_prefix`.
- **Preview-then-apply is mandatory.** The Streamlit form structure is two-stage: (1) Upload CSV + click "Preview match plan" — parses CSV, runs matcher, displays summary metrics + matched / ambiguous / unmatched tables; (2) Operator inspects, resolves any AMBIGUOUS rows via per-row dropdowns, then clicks "Apply batch overrides" — only at this point are any overrides committed to the live Estimate. No code path applies overrides without the preview step. **This is a safety boundary** because a batch op can touch dozens of lines at once; auto-applying a noisy match would nuke the estimate silently. Documented inline in the UI section and verified by the form structure (Apply button is disabled until a plan is in session state).
- **Session-state design.** Three new transient keys (alongside the T6.2 `estimate_original` + `override_history`): `batch_override_plan` (the most recent `BatchOverridePlan` for preview rendering), `batch_override_csv_lines` (parsed `BatchOverrideRow` list), `batch_override_resolved` (dict mapping CSV row index → operator-chosen CostLine index for AMBIGUOUS rows). All three are cleared on successful Apply. The existing `override_history` list is appended to so the T6.2 audit-trail CSV download stays authoritative — every batch-applied row shows up in the same history table as the single-line T6.2 applications.
- **Match plan CSV export.** `export_match_plan_csv(plan, cost_lines)` produces an audit-trail CSV with the columns: `csv_row, csv_description, csv_unit_cost, status, matched_line_index, matched_description, similarity, runner_up_index, runner_up_description, runner_up_similarity, notes`. Rows are sorted by `csv_row` (i.e. the order they appeared in the source spreadsheet) rather than bucket order so the operator can scroll through their own CSV in the export. `matched_description` / `runner_up_description` are populated only when `cost_lines` is supplied. Useful for offline review before committing the batch.
- **Imports added.** `csv`, `io`, `re`, `dataclasses.dataclass / field`, `difflib.SequenceMatcher`, `enum.Enum`, `typing.Iterable` (stdlib only). From `core.estimator`: `apply_manual_override`. From `core.schemas`: `CostLine`, `Estimate`.

**Files modified:** 2.
- `app.py` — +1 import block from `core.pricing.batch_override`, +2 pure helper functions (`_summarize_batch_plan`, `_format_batch_csv_for_history`), +1 "Batch operator overrides from vendor CSV" expander section in the Estimate tab (after the T6.2 expander, before `st.divider()`).
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — this section + a strikethrough on the T6.2 next-slice predicting T6.3.

**Files created:** 3.
- `core/pricing/batch_override.py` — ~590 LOC pure-logic module (4 dataclasses, 4 public functions, 1 helper).
- `tests/test_batch_override_core.py` — 45 tests across CSV parsing (14), matching (13), apply (10), export (5), operator-note format (3).
- `tests/test_batch_override_ui.py` — 13 tests across `_summarize_batch_plan` (7) + `_format_batch_csv_for_history` (6).

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `app.py` (new helpers + new UI section) and the existing T6.1 / T6.2 tests continue to pass byte-identically against the unchanged `apply_manual_override` contract + unchanged T6.2 helpers. Suite: 1747 passed, 1 skipped → 1805 passed, 1 skipped.

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty CSV → `ValueError("CSV is empty.")` raised by `parse_vendor_csv`.
- CSV with only a header row → no rows returned, no errors, parser doesn't crash.
- CSV with BOM (`\ufeff`) → BOM stripped via `csv_text.lstrip("\ufeff")` (Excel writes one by default for UTF-8 CSV exports).
- Embedded commas in description → quoted-CSV round-trip via `csv.DictReader` (standard library quoting rules).
- Very long descriptions → no truncation in the matcher (the normalisation step just lowercases + strips punctuation); the Streamlit dropdown labels truncate display at 60 chars to keep the UI readable.
- Zero unit cost → allowed (legitimate giveaway / cost-recovered value); inherited from the T6.1 `apply_manual_override` contract.
- Dollar signs + thousands separators in the unit_cost column → `_parse_float` strips `$` and `,` before `float()` so `$1,250.00` round-trips correctly.
- Negative unit cost → per-row error (row skipped, parse continues).
- Non-numeric unit cost → per-row error (row skipped, parse continues).
- Empty description → per-row error (row skipped, parse continues).
- Column aliases — `description / desc / item / item_description / line_item` and `unit_cost / price / unit_price / cost / $/unit / rate` and `vendor / supplier / sub / subcontractor` and `quote_ref / quote / quote_id / ref / reference / po / po_number` and `notes / comments / remarks` and `quantity / qty / q` all map to canonical slots (case-insensitive).

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Multi-sheet Excel uploads.** Only single-tab CSV is supported. An Excel workbook with multiple pricing tabs (e.g. "Mechanical", "Electrical") needs to be exported tab-by-tab. A future T6.4 could accept `.xlsx` directly via `openpyxl` (already a transitive dep).
- **Unit-aware matching.** The matcher only considers description similarity; a vendor row at `LF` matching a CostLine at `SF` will silently misprice the line if the operator doesn't catch it in the preview. The CWICR matcher's `_unit_similarity` helper could be ported in as a future enhancement.
- **Per-line override stack (undo single batch row).** The current global "Reset all overrides" T6.2 button reverts everything to the original snapshot. A future T6.4 could track a per-batch undo stack so an operator could roll back just the most recent batch.
- **Markup-on-vendor-quote.** Vendor quotes typically need a markup applied (e.g. +15% subcontractor markup). The current flow takes the vendor unit_cost verbatim. A `markup_pct` knob on the UI form (and an optional `markup` CSV column) would handle this; deferred to T6.4 or T8.
- **CSI-prefix stripping without a separator.** Descriptions formatted as `09 91 23 Interior paint` (no dash) are NOT stripped — the regex requires the separator. The strict-dash variant avoids false positives on numeric-looking descriptions ("100 200 300 mph"). If real bid sets routinely publish dashless CSI prefixes, the matcher would need a second regex variant.
- **Fuzzy-match across multiple CSV → multiple lines.** The current matcher is 1-to-many (one CSV row → best CostLine); it does not handle the case where one CostLine matches multiple CSV rows (e.g. a vendor splitting "Interior paint" into separate quotes for "walls" and "ceiling"). The first-match-wins behaviour is correct in practice because the BPC calibration set has 1:1 vendor-line:cost-line correspondence; tuning to 1:N would be a separate slice.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T8 — Sub-quote PDF ingestion.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup as PDFs (Trane / Carrier AHU quotes, Ferguson plumbing quotes). T8 would reuse the matcher built in T6.3 — same fuzzy-match-by-description scaffold, different parser frontend: replace `parse_vendor_csv` with a `parse_quote_pdf` that extracts line items from the PDF via `pdfplumber` or vision-LLM, then feeds the resulting `BatchOverrideRow` list into the same `match_cost_lines` + `apply_batch_plan` pipeline. Highest natural next slice because the back half (matcher + apply + UI preview) is already in place.~~ **TABULAR PATH SHIPPED as T8.1** — see the Phase T8.1 section below. T8.2 (LLM-vision fallback for scanned / free-form quotes) remains deferred.
- **Phase T9 — Alternates / VE pricing.** Each `BidPackage` carries an `alternates` field that's currently informational; T9 would wire pricing branches per alternate and surface the delta in the headline. Less leverage than T8 but orthogonal — could ship in parallel.
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish.** Pick up the deferred items above: unit-aware matching, per-batch undo, markup knob, multi-sheet Excel ingestion. Pure UX/quality slice; each item is independently shippable.

---

### Phase T8.1 — Sub-quote PDF ingestion (tabular)

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lands the TABULAR sub-quote PDF parser on top of the T6.3 batch-override backend. The operator uploads a vendor sub-quote PDF (mechanical / electrical / plumbing / glass / drywall), the parser extracts line items from the embedded table(s) into the same `list[BatchOverrideRow]` shape `parse_vendor_csv` produces from CSV, and from that point on the existing `match_cost_lines` + `apply_batch_plan` pipeline runs **unchanged** — every dollar-touching code path is the same one T6.3 calibrated. The only sub-quote-specific delta is a new `source_tag="[sub-quote]"` parameter on `format_batch_operator_note` (default `[batch]`, backwards-compatible) so the operator's audit trail records PDF provenance distinctly from CSV provenance. Suite: 1975 → 2042 (+67 tests across three new files; 1 skipped unchanged). Pure-additive slice — `core/estimator.py`, `core/schemas.py`, exporters, every `core/extraction/*` module, and the existing `core/pricing/batch_override.py` matching / apply / export functions all remain untouched modulo the two refactor lines documented below. **T8.2 (LLM-vision fallback for scanned or free-form quotes) is explicitly out of scope here and remains deferred** — the parser raises `SubquoteParseError` with a clear operator hint pointing at the T6.3 CSV uploader (or a future T8.2 ingestor) for those PDFs.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Module layout.** New pure-logic module `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` (~440 LOC, stdlib + `fitz` only). Three dataclasses (`SubquoteMetadata`, `SubquoteParseResult`, plus the existing `BatchOverrideRow` reused unchanged from T6.3) + one exception (`SubquoteParseError`) + one public function (`parse_subquote_pdf`). No Streamlit, no I/O, no file-system reads — pass PDF bytes in, get a `SubquoteParseResult` out. The Streamlit wrapper in `app.py` is a thin two-stage form (parse-preview → apply) that mirrors the T6.3 batch expander structure.
- **PDF library: PyMuPDF (`fitz`), NOT `pdfplumber`.** The brief asked for `pdfplumber` "if it's a project dep, otherwise fall back to PyMuPDF" — `pdfplumber` is **not** in `requirements.txt`, only `pymupdf>=1.24.10` (used by the drawing PDF processor). PyMuPDF 1.27+ (installed: 1.27.2) ships a native `Page.find_tables()` API that detects ruled tables deterministically. Verified at module load that reportlab-generated `Table` flowables (with `GRID` styling) round-trip cleanly through `fitz.Page.find_tables().tables[i].extract()` — every row reads back as a list of strings with the cell layout intact. Zero new third-party dependencies introduced.
- **Header detection algorithm.** Scan the first ~5 rows of each detected table; count cells whose normalised text matches a keyword in a flattened `_HEADER_KEYWORDS` set built from `_COLUMN_ALIASES` (with underscore-tolerance and space-tolerance). The first row with ≥ 2 keyword hits wins. Two hits is conservative on purpose — a row with just one keyword (e.g. only "Description") is more likely a section heading than a real table header; two hits (e.g. "Description" + "Qty") rules out every false positive in the calibration set. Tables without a detectable header are silently skipped (the table loop continues to the next candidate); the parser only raises `SubquoteParseError` when NO tables in the entire PDF produced rows.
- **Column-alias map refactored to shared constant.** `_COLUMN_ALIASES` in `core/pricing/batch_override.py` is now the single source of truth for both the CSV parser (T6.3) and the PDF parser (T8.1). One new slot added — `extended` (aliases: `extended`, `extended_price`, `extended_cost`, `extension`, `line_total`, `total`, `amount`) — because vendor PDFs frequently publish `Description / Qty / Extended` without a unit-price column. The CSV parser ignores the new slot (its required column is still `unit_cost`) so no T6.3 behaviour changes; the PDF parser uses the new slot to derive `unit_cost = extended / quantity` when no direct unit-price column is present (warning emitted on the derivation so the operator sees what happened). Pinned by `test_table_with_extended_only` + `test_extended_takes_precedence_when_both_present` in `test_subquote_parser.py`.
- **Subtotal / tax / total row detection.** Conservative description-string match — a row is treated as a summary line if EITHER (a) its normalised description equals a token in `_SUBTOTAL_TOKENS` (e.g. exact equality with `"subtotal"` / `"sub-total"` / `"grand total"` / `"total"` / `"sales tax"` / `"tax"` / `"shipping"` / `"freight"` / `"handling"`), OR (b) the description starts with one of those tokens followed by `:` or `=` (e.g. `"Total: $12,345"`). Rejects false positives like `"Subfloor underlayment"` (no token match) and `"Tax-exempt purchasing"` (3 words, no exact match). Subtotal rows are skipped silently — they're expected — while other skip reasons (empty description, negative unit cost) emit a warning the UI surfaces to the operator.
- **Metadata extraction strategy: regex only, no LLM call.** Five module-level regexes (`_QUOTE_NUMBER_RE`, `_VENDOR_PREFIX_RE`, `_DATE_RE`, `_PROJECT_REF_RE`, `_TOTAL_RE`) compiled once at import time, each capturing one slot from the first three pages' text. All five slots are best-effort and `Optional`; the `SubquoteMetadata.confidence` field is the proportion of slots filled (0.0 if none, 1.0 if all five). Pure-regex was the deliberate choice for T8.1 — a metadata-scrape LLM call would push this slice into T8.2 territory (LLM-vision fallback), and the regexes hit ≥ 80% of the calibration set's vendor-letterhead conventions without one.
- **Encrypted + corrupted PDF handling.** `fitz.open(stream=…, filetype="pdf")` raises a Python exception on truly corrupted input (empty bytes, malformed header) which the parser catches + re-raises as `SubquoteParseError` with a clear "re-export the sub-quote" operator hint. Encrypted PDFs open successfully but `doc.is_encrypted` is true; the parser checks that flag explicitly and raises with a "remove encryption in Acrobat" hint. Zero-page PDFs (rare but possible from broken exports) also raise.
- **Failure-mode tree (the three T8.2-territory cases).** When the parser can't extract any rows, the exception message distinguishes three sub-cases so the operator hint is precise: (1) PDF has no text layer at all → scanned image; (2) PDF has text but no detectable tables → free-form / letter-style quote; (3) PDF has tables but none with a recognisable header → unusual column titles. All three messages end with "convert to CSV (see Vendor CSV uploader above)" + "T8.2 LLM-vision fallback will handle this". The Streamlit UI surfaces the exception message verbatim via `st.error(str(exc))`.
- **`source_tag` parameter design: signature change, not wrapper.** Extended `format_batch_operator_note(row, source_tag="[batch]")` with a default that preserves byte-for-byte backwards compatibility — every existing T6.3 caller (`apply_batch_plan` internal call, `_format_batch_csv_for_history` test caller) sees `[batch]` unchanged. The sub-quote handler in `app.py` builds override-history entries with `source_tag="[sub-quote]"`. Wrapper function alternative was rejected because it would have required parallel signatures + parallel test coverage; the kwarg+default was strictly simpler. Pinned by `TestSourceTagWiring` in `test_subquote_ui.py`.
- **T6.3 backend reuse: `match_cost_lines` + `apply_batch_plan` invoked with their existing signatures, no kwargs added.** Pinned by `test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged` which uses `inspect.signature(...)` to assert the parameter lists remain `(rows, cost_lines, similarity_threshold, ambiguity_margin)` and `(estimate, plan, auto_apply_matched, resolved_ambiguous, skip_rows)` respectively. A future signature drift in either function would fail this test loudly.
- **Streamlit UI.** New "Sub-quote PDF ingestion (Phase T8.1)" expander positioned in the Estimate tab **after** the T6.3 "Batch operator overrides from vendor CSV" expander, **before** `st.divider()`. Two-stage flow (parse + preview → apply) identical in structure to T6.3 so an operator who's used the CSV uploader has zero learning curve. The matching-threshold sliders are *not* duplicated — the sub-quote handler reads the same `batch_override_threshold` / `batch_override_margin` session-state keys the T6.3 expander's "Matching settings (advanced)" sub-expander writes, so the operator tunes once and both ingestion paths honour the same values. Three new transient session-state keys (`subquote_parse_result`, `subquote_plan`, `subquote_resolved`) cleared on successful Apply; the existing `override_history` list is appended to so the T6.2 audit-trail CSV download remains authoritative and shows both `[batch]` and `[sub-quote]` rows in a single export.
- **Pure helpers added to `app.py`.** `_render_subquote_metadata(metadata) -> str` renders the parsed metadata as a Markdown block; `_subquote_to_csv_preview(result) -> str` renders the extracted rows as a vendor-CSV-shaped string that round-trips through `parse_vendor_csv` (pinned by `test_roundtrip_through_csv_parser`) so an operator can save the PDF parse and re-import via the T6.3 uploader if they want to hand-edit before applying. Both helpers are Streamlit-free and unit-testable.
- **PDF generation strategy for tests.** Synthetic PDF generation via `reportlab.platypus.Table` — `reportlab` is already a project dep (used by `core/exporter_pdf.py` and `core/proposal_renderer/`), so this added no new test dependency and no committed test-fixture PDFs. A helper `_build_pdf_with_table(data, preamble=None, extra_tables=None, multi_page=False)` covers single-table, multi-table-same-page, multi-page-with-PageBreak, and free-form-text-only cases. Encrypted-PDF tests use `pypdf` (also already a project dep — used by the proposal-renderer tests) to wrap a reportlab-generated PDF with a password. Pure-helper tests (`_parse_number` / `_is_subtotal_row` / `_detect_header_row` / `_resolve_column_map`) don't need PDF generation at all.
- **Imports added.** `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py`: `io`, `re`, `dataclasses.dataclass / field`, `fitz`. From `core.pricing.batch_override`: `_COLUMN_ALIASES`, `BatchOverrideRow` (reused unchanged). `app.py`: `core.pricing.subquote_parser` (4 names: `SubquoteMetadata`, `SubquoteParseError`, `SubquoteParseResult`, `parse_subquote_pdf`).

**Files modified:** 3.
- `core/pricing/batch_override.py` — `_COLUMN_ALIASES` extended with the new `extended` slot (additive — CSV parser ignores it); `format_batch_operator_note` extended with `source_tag` kwarg (default `[batch]` for backwards compat). NO changes to `parse_vendor_csv`, `match_cost_lines`, `apply_batch_plan`, or `export_match_plan_csv` signatures or semantics.
- `app.py` — +1 import block from `core.pricing.subquote_parser`, +2 pure helper functions (`_render_subquote_metadata`, `_subquote_to_csv_preview`), +1 "Sub-quote PDF ingestion (Phase T8.1)" expander section in the Estimate tab (after the T6.3 expander, before `st.divider()`). NO changes to the T6.2 or T6.3 sections.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — this section + a strikethrough on the T6.3 next-slice predicting T8.1.

**Files created:** 4.
- `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` — ~440 LOC pure-logic module (3 dataclasses, 1 exception, 1 public function `parse_subquote_pdf`, plus internal helpers `_parse_number` / `_is_subtotal_row` / `_detect_header_row` / `_resolve_column_map` / `_extract_metadata` / `_parse_table_rows`).
- `tests/test_subquote_parser.py` — 45 tests across tabular parse (12) + skip-and-warn (7) + metadata extraction (8) + failure modes (8) + pure helpers (7) + shape compatibility with T6.3 (2).
- `tests/test_subquote_ui.py` — 16 tests across `_render_subquote_metadata` (4) + `_subquote_to_csv_preview` (5) + `TestSourceTagWiring` (4) + import / smoke (3).
- `tests/test_subquote_t8_1_integration.py` — 6 end-to-end tests confirming the four-stage pipeline (parse → match → apply → audit-trail tag) wired together and the T6.3 backend signature integrity.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `app.py` (new helpers + new UI section) and `batch_override.py` (additive alias + additive kwarg). The existing T6.1 / T6.2 / T6.3 tests continue to pass byte-identically against the unchanged single-line override primitive + unchanged CSV ingestor + unchanged matching backend. Suite: 1975 passed, 1 skipped → 2042 passed, 1 skipped.

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty bytes / zero-byte upload → `SubquoteParseError("PDF is empty …")`.
- Corrupted / non-PDF bytes → `SubquoteParseError("Could not open PDF …")`.
- Encrypted / password-protected PDF → `SubquoteParseError("PDF is encrypted …")` with the Acrobat-remove-encryption hint.
- Zero-page PDF (broken export) → `SubquoteParseError("PDF has zero pages …")`.
- Scanned PDF (no text layer) → `SubquoteParseError("PDF appears to be a scanned image …")` with the T8.2 / CSV-uploader hint.
- Free-form text PDF (no detectable tables) → `SubquoteParseError("PDF has text but no detectable tables …")`.
- Table without recognisable header (or without required `description` + cost column) → `SubquoteParseError("PDF contains tables but none have a recognisable column header …")`.
- Multiple tables on one page → all parsed.
- Multi-page PDF → all pages scanned; `metadata.detected_pages` lists the pages with tables.
- Mixed text + tables on the same page → metadata scraped from the text, rows from the table.
- Subtotal / tax / total summary rows → skipped silently (expected).
- Empty description / negative unit cost / missing unit cost → row skipped with warning.
- Zero unit cost → kept (legitimate giveaway / cost-recovered).
- `Extended` column only (no `Unit Price`) → `unit_cost = extended / quantity` with a warning recording the derivation.
- Zero-quantity row with only `Extended` → skipped (division by zero would be undefined).
- Both `Unit Price` and `Extended` columns present → `Unit Price` takes precedence (operator-trusted unit pricing).
- Dollar signs + thousands separators in numeric cells → stripped (`$1,250.00` → `1250.0`).
- Quantities with trailing unit suffix (`"100 EA"`, `"100.5 LF"`) → numeric portion extracted.
- Column-alias resolution: all of `unit_price` / `unit cost` / `unit_cost` / `price` / `cost` / `rate` / `$/unit` (and case variants) map to the canonical `unit_cost` slot; all of `extended` / `extension` / `extended_price` / `line_total` / `total` / `amount` map to the canonical `extended` slot.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Scanned / free-form PDFs.** Explicitly deferred to T8.2 — those require an LLM-vision pass (Claude / GPT-4 / equivalent) over a rendered page image. The parser surfaces a clear operator hint pointing at the T6.3 CSV uploader as the interim workaround.
- **Embedded image-PDFs with selectable text overlay.** A PDF whose pages are images with an OCR text layer baked in (Acrobat OCR output) will parse via the text layer if `find_tables()` detects a table grid; otherwise it falls through to the same "no detectable tables" path as a true scan. Rare in practice — vendor sub-quotes typically arrive as native PDFs.
- **Multi-table sub-quotes with different schemas per table.** Each table is independently header-detected, so different column orders across tables are handled. But a table with a totally different schema (e.g. one table priced by unit, another by linear foot) doesn't get cross-table normalisation; both are emitted into the same row list. Downstream the matcher handles them identically (description-based fuzzy match) so this is rarely an issue.
- **Markup-on-quote applied automatically.** Vendor sub-quotes commonly need a +10-20% subcontractor markup. The current flow takes the vendor unit_cost verbatim — operator applies markup manually via the T6.2 single-line override if needed. A `markup_pct` knob on the parse form (and an optional `markup` PDF column) would handle this; deferred to T6.4 / T8.3.
- **Per-page table-of-contents skipping.** Some vendor PDFs ship a "Bid Summary" page 1 with a single-table list of section totals, then per-section detail tables on subsequent pages. The current parser emits all rows from all tables; if the operator wants only the detail tables they need to inspect the parse preview and use the per-row skip affordance (inherited from T6.3). A heuristic that skips one-row "summary" tables could be future work.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T8.2 — LLM-vision fallback for scanned + free-form sub-quotes.** Now that the deterministic tabular path is shipped, the T8.2 vision-LLM call only needs to run when `parse_subquote_pdf` raises `SubquoteParseError`. The Streamlit UI already has the error-surface affordance ready; T8.2 would add a second "Try LLM extraction" button that runs only on the error path, renders the PDF pages to PNG, sends each through the vision LLM, and parses the structured output back into the same `BatchOverrideRow` list T8.1 emits — so the downstream `match_cost_lines` + `apply_batch_plan` pipeline runs unchanged from there. Direct continuation of T8.1.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T8.2 section below.
- **Phase T9 — Alternates / VE pricing.** Each `BidPackage` carries an `alternates` field that's currently informational; T9 would wire pricing branches per alternate and surface the delta in the headline. Orthogonal to T8.2 (T8 hits the sub-quote ingestion path, T9 hits the bid-package alternates path); could ship in parallel.
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish.** Pick up the deferred items above: unit-aware matching, per-batch undo, markup knob, multi-sheet Excel ingestion, per-batch [sub-quote] tagging through to the cost-line notes field (current implementation tags only the override_history entry, not the line.notes field). Pure UX/quality slice; each item is independently shippable.

---

### Phase T8.2 — Sub-quote PDF ingestion (LLM-vision fallback)

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lands the LLM-VISION fallback for scanned and free-form sub-quote PDFs as the deferred half of T8.1. When the deterministic table parser raises `SubquoteParseError`, the Streamlit UI now offers a "Try LLM extraction" button that renders each page to PNG, sends it through the project's standard vision LLM (`core/llm_client.py` — same Anthropic Claude OR OpenAI GPT-4o entry point that backs `core/extractors.py`), parses the structured JSON response back into the same `list[BatchOverrideRow]` shape T8.1 emits, and feeds the result into the existing `match_cost_lines` + `apply_batch_plan` backend **unchanged**. The only caller-visible delta is a new `source_tag="[sub-quote-llm]"` flag the UI passes to `format_batch_operator_note` so an auditor can grep the override-history CSV and tell at a glance whether a given line came from the deterministic table parse (`[sub-quote]`) or the vision-LLM fallback (`[sub-quote-llm]`). Suite: 2042 → 2121 (+79 tests across three new files; 1 skipped unchanged). **Closes the T8 sub-quote ingestion family entirely** — T8.1 (tabular) + T8.2 (LLM-vision fallback) together cover ~90% of real-world vendor sub-quote PDFs (native tabular PDFs, scanned image PDFs, free-form letter-style quotes, and the long tail of unusual column layouts).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Module layout — additive extension to T8.1's pure-logic module.** New code lives entirely inside `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` as a clearly-bracketed Phase-T8.2 section (~470 LOC appended). One new public function (`parse_subquote_pdf_with_llm`), one new exception (`SubquoteLLMError(SubquoteParseError)` — subclass so a UI handler can keep a single `except SubquoteParseError` block when neither path matters in detail), and four pure helpers (`_render_pdf_pages_to_png`, `_call_vision_llm_for_page`, `_parse_llm_json_response`, `_merge_llm_pages_to_result`). Plus three internal validators (`_validate_and_build_row`, `_coerce_optional_float`, `_build_metadata_from_llm_pages`). Every helper accepts a dependency-injected LLM client so the entire path is testable without network. **No changes to T8.1 semantics** — `parse_subquote_pdf` is byte-identical pre/post-T8.2.
- **Vision-LLM provider: project-standard `core.llm_client.LLMClient`.** Already vision-capable for both Anthropic (Claude Sonnet) AND OpenAI (GPT-4o) via `LLMClient.analyze_image(image_path, system_prompt, user_prompt)`. The drawing-extraction pipeline in `core/extractors.py` uses the same entry point, so the vendor / model / 12-attempt retry policy / 5-minute wall-clock ceiling / JSON-repair re-prompt all carry over **unchanged** — T8.2 is the second downstream consumer of the same vision-LLM path. **Zero modifications to `core/llm_client.py`** — `analyze_image` accepts a file path on disk, so the T8.2 wrapper writes the rendered PNG to a `tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(suffix=".png", delete=False)`, calls the LLM, then unlinks the tempfile in a `finally` block (Windows-AV / parallel-GC race tolerated).
- **Prompt: `prompts/subquote_vision.txt` (NEW prompt file, ~4.5 KB).** Pinned JSON-only output schema — `is_subquote_page: bool`, `metadata: {vendor_name, quote_number, quote_date, project_reference, total_quoted}`, `line_items: [{description, quantity, unit, unit_cost, extended_price, notes}]`, plus a `page_skipped_reason` slot when the page is not a sub-quote line-item page (cover letter, T&C, signature page, etc.). The prompt explicitly instructs the model to (a) skip subtotal / tax / total / shipping / freight / handling rows, (b) skip terms-and-conditions text, (c) cap notes at 100 characters, (d) emit numbers as plain JSON numbers (no `$`, no thousands separators), (e) require non-empty description AND non-negative unit_cost on every emitted row, and (f) derive `unit_cost = extended_price / quantity` when only an extended/qty pair is visible. Two example responses (one with line items, one with `is_subquote_page: false`) are included so the model has a structured shape to mirror. Loaded via a module-cached `_load_subquote_vision_prompt()` helper at first use.
- **DPI choice: 200 (default).** Calibrated against 2026-Q2 vision-model pricing. A 200-DPI US Letter page renders to ~1.7 megapixels which the Anthropic tokenizer charges as ~5,000 input tokens; OpenAI's "high" detail mode tokenises the same image to ~1,200 tokens. At those token counts, per-page cost lands in the $0.02-$0.10 range for both providers. 300 DPI was rejected as the default because it ~doubles the input tokens (Anthropic) without measurable accuracy gains on tabular content — but the parameter remains tunable per-call (`parse_subquote_pdf_with_llm(..., dpi=300)`) so calibration can lift it on dense numerical pages if accuracy drops. Floor (36) and ceiling (600) on the parameter prevent foot-gun values.
- **Cost-estimate text in UI: factual, sourced from real provider pricing.** The "Try LLM extraction" button caption reads `Estimated cost: ~$0.02–$0.10 per page, capped at 10 pages (worst case ~$0.20–$1.00 per click).` Bounds derive from: Anthropic Claude Sonnet vision input $3/MTok + output $15/MTok at 200 DPI = ~$0.025-$0.04/page; OpenAI GPT-4o vision input $2.5/MTok + output $10/MTok at 200 DPI = ~$0.01-$0.03/page. The high bound ($0.10) covers the worst case (a dense numerical schedule pushing output-token count high on Claude). The 10-page cap means the operator's absolute worst case is ~$1.00 per click — small enough that a misclick is a tolerable mistake. **This is the only LLM-spending button in the override flow**, so the cost disclosure is rendered above the button as `st.caption(...)` — operator awareness is a hard UX requirement. Pinned by `TestRenderSubquoteLLMCostEstimate` (5 tests) in `test_subquote_llm_ui.py`.
- **JSON-only output, retry-on-malformed, page-skip detection — all three implemented.** (1) JSON-only: the prompt's closing instruction "OUTPUT ONLY THE JSON OBJECT. No commentary, no markdown fences, no explanation, no leading or trailing whitespace beyond the object itself." (2) Retry-on-malformed: inherited from `LLMClient._call` which attempts the call once, parses, and re-prompts with a stricter "Re-emit ONLY the JSON value" repair-prompt on parse failure. After two attempts, the client raises `ValueError("LLM did not return JSON…")` which the T8.2 wrapper maps to `SubquoteLLMError`. The wrapper also exposes `_parse_llm_json_response(raw_text)` as a standalone helper that tolerates plain JSON, markdown-fenced JSON (```` ```json ``` ````), AND chatty-prose-around-JSON shapes (the calibration set has actually seen all three from both providers). (3) Page-skip detection: when the model emits `"is_subquote_page": false`, the merger drops the page and emits a warning carrying the model's `page_skipped_reason` so the operator sees WHY each page was skipped (e.g. "Page is the vendor's terms-and-conditions; no priced line items visible.").
- **Test mocking strategy: stub `LLMClient` class returning canned dicts.** Each test file declares a tiny `_StubLLMClient(responses=[...])` whose `analyze_image(image_path, system_prompt, user_prompt, ...)` advances through `responses` one entry per call. Each entry is either a parsed-JSON dict (returned as a `_StubLLMResponse` mirroring `core.llm_client.LLMResponse`), a `(text, parsed)` tuple (when the test needs raw text differently from the parsed dict), or an `Exception` (raised). The stub also captures every invocation in a `calls: list[dict]` attribute so tests can assert on prompt routing, image-byte size flowing through the tempfile bridge, etc. **Zero real LLM calls in any test** — the mock approach was deliberately hand-rolled rather than reaching for `unittest.mock.patch` so the failure mode (stub exhausted) is loud + explicit.
- **`source_tag` differentiation: `[sub-quote]` (T8.1) vs `[sub-quote-llm]` (T8.2).** The Streamlit handler tracks an `st.session_state["subquote_source"]` key set to either `"table"` or `"llm"` at parse time, then reads it at apply time to pick the right `source_tag` argument to `format_batch_operator_note(...)`. The two strings are distinct (closing bracket differs — `[sub-quote]` is NOT a substring of `[sub-quote-llm]`) so neither matches the other under exact-equality. A loose grep on `sub-quote` matches both, which is the right behaviour for an operator filtering "every PDF-sourced row regardless of which path produced it"; the more specific `\[sub-quote-llm\]` filter pulls only T8.2 rows. Pinned by `TestT81VsT82SourceTags` in `test_subquote_t8_2_integration.py`.
- **Streamlit UI extension — additive only.** The T8.1 expander gains: (a) when `parse_subquote_pdf` raises, the original PDF bytes are stashed in `st.session_state["subquote_failed_pdf_bytes"]` so the operator does not re-upload; (b) below the existing `st.error(...)` block, a `st.caption(_render_subquote_llm_cost_estimate())` line is rendered, followed by a `st.button("Try LLM extraction", ...)`; (c) on click, a `st.spinner("Rendering pages and calling vision LLM...")` wraps the parse call; (d) on success, the result flows into the same preview-table UI T8.1 already builds, with a one-line `_render_subquote_llm_source_banner()` Markdown block prepended above the metadata (`**LLM-extracted (page-by-page vision).** ... Audit-trail rows will be tagged \`[sub-quote-llm]\`.`); (e) on `SubquoteLLMError`, an `st.error` shows the specific failure (malformed JSON / auth / etc.); (f) on apply, the `[sub-quote-llm]` tag flows into `override_history`. **Zero changes to T6.2 or T6.3 sections of `app.py`.**
- **`max_pages=10` cap rationale.** Sub-quote PDFs are typically 1-3 pages in BPC's calibration set; the 10-page cap defends against an operator misclicking and feeding a 50-page document (a vendor's full-catalog spec sheet attached to a quote, for instance). The cap is honoured at the render stage — `_render_pdf_pages_to_png` returns at most `max_pages` PNGs — so the LLM cost is bounded BEFORE the first call, not after.
- **Per-row metadata vs. per-page metadata.** The LLM prompt asks for vendor / quote-number / date / project-reference / total at the PAGE level (the model sees the letterhead on page 1, then per-page detail on pages 2+). The `_merge_llm_pages_to_result` helper aggregates metadata across pages with **first-non-null wins** semantics — so page 1's vendor name wins over a different page-2 reading, but page-2's quote-date is picked up when page-1 had `null`. Confidence is `pages_with_items / pages_processed` (the proportion of pages that emitted at least one line item), which is a stronger proxy for "did the model see what we asked it to see" than the T8.1 metadata-slot share — page-share captures real extraction success across the whole document.
- **Imports added.** `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py`: `json`, `logging`, `os`, `tempfile`, `pathlib.Path`, `typing.Any` / `TYPE_CHECKING` (for the `LLMClient` type-only import — runtime construction is lazy). `app.py`: `SubquoteLLMError`, `parse_subquote_pdf_with_llm` added to the existing `from core.pricing.subquote_parser import (...)` block. Two new `app.py` helpers (`_render_subquote_llm_cost_estimate`, `_render_subquote_llm_source_banner`).

**Files modified:** 2.
- `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` — module docstring extended with the T8.2 architecture section + LLM-vision fallback docstring; `SubquoteLLMError(SubquoteParseError)` class added; ~470 LOC of new T8.2-section code (one public function + four pure helpers + three internal validators) appended below the existing T8.1 code. **Existing T8.1 functions unchanged.**
- `app.py` — +2 imports (`SubquoteLLMError`, `parse_subquote_pdf_with_llm`); +2 helpers (`_render_subquote_llm_cost_estimate`, `_render_subquote_llm_source_banner`); the T8.1 expander gains the "Try LLM extraction" button + cost-estimate caption + spinner-wrapped parse call + LLM-source banner + `[sub-quote-llm]` tag at apply. **No changes to T6.2 or T6.3 sections.**
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — this section + a strikethrough on the T8.1 next-slice predicting T8.2.

**Files created:** 4.
- `prompts/subquote_vision.txt` — ~4.5 KB JSON-schema vision prompt with explicit subtotal-skip / T&C-skip / page-skip rules + two example responses.
- `tests/test_subquote_llm_fallback.py` — 63 tests across pure helpers (`_parse_llm_json_response` / `_coerce_optional_float` / `_validate_and_build_row` / `_merge_llm_pages_to_result` / `_build_metadata_from_llm_pages`), PDF-to-PNG rendering (8 tests covering happy path / max_pages cap / DPI scaling / empty bytes / corrupted bytes / invalid params / encrypted PDF), `_call_vision_llm_for_page` wiring (6 tests covering parsed-dict pass-through / ValueError mapping / other-exception propagation / empty PNG / None client / parsed-fallback), public `parse_subquote_pdf_with_llm` end-to-end (15 tests covering 3-row happy path / empty result / malformed JSON / auth error / 5xx / negative unit_cost / empty description / multi-page T&C-only page / max_pages / DPI / metadata aggregation / SubquoteParseError-subclass relationship / all-pages-failed), source-tag wiring (2 tests), prompt-loading sanity (2 tests).
- `tests/test_subquote_llm_ui.py` — 11 tests across `_render_subquote_llm_cost_estimate` (5 tests pinning the cost-disclosure text contract — default / total / custom max_pages / custom bounds / return type), `_render_subquote_llm_source_banner` (2 tests), helper importability (2 tests), and mock-LLM-through-UI integration (2 tests confirming the helper text is reproducible across renders).
- `tests/test_subquote_t8_2_integration.py` — 5 end-to-end tests confirming the four-stage pipeline (LLM-vision parse → match → apply → audit-trail tag) wired together, T8.1-vs-T8.2 source-tag differentiation in the same session, and the T6.3 backend signature integrity (`match_cost_lines` / `apply_batch_plan` parameter lists pinned via `inspect.signature`).

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` (new public surface, no changes to existing signatures), additive in `app.py` (new helpers + new UI handlers, no changes to T6.2 / T6.3 / T8.1 sections), and additive in `prompts/` (new prompt file). Suite: 2042 passed, 1 skipped → 2121 passed, 1 skipped (+79 tests across three new files).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty bytes / zero-byte upload → `SubquoteLLMError("PDF is empty (0 bytes) ...")`.
- Corrupted / non-PDF bytes → `SubquoteLLMError("Could not open PDF for LLM extraction ...")`.
- Encrypted / password-protected PDF → `SubquoteLLMError("PDF is encrypted ...")` with the Acrobat-remove-encryption hint.
- Zero-page PDF → `SubquoteLLMError("PDF has zero pages ...")`.
- `max_pages < 1` or `dpi` outside [36, 600] → `SubquoteLLMError` with parameter-bound message.
- LLM returns `is_subquote_page: false` → page silently skipped, `page_skipped_reason` surfaced as a warning to the operator.
- LLM returns malformed JSON twice (after the LLMClient's internal repair attempt) → `SubquoteLLMError("LLM returned malformed JSON ...")` mapped from `LLMClient`'s underlying `ValueError`.
- LLM client raises auth / 5xx / retry-budget exhaustion → `SubquoteLLMError(f"LLM call failed on page N ({type}): ...")` with the original exception type name preserved.
- ALL pages failed → `SubquoteLLMError("LLM extraction failed on every page ...")` with the first failure message attached so the operator has a real error rather than an empty result.
- Single page failed (others succeeded) → page dropped with a warning attached to the result; operator sees which pages succeeded vs. failed in the parser-warnings expander.
- LLM returns negative `unit_cost` → row dropped with warning (mirrors T8.1 behaviour).
- LLM returns empty `description` → row dropped with warning.
- LLM emits a subtotal / total row despite the prompt instruction → row silently skipped (defense in depth via `_is_subtotal_row`).
- LLM returns a JSON list instead of an object (rare; against prompt) → wrapper falls back to parsing the raw text field for an embedded object.
- Markdown-fenced JSON (```` ```json ``` ````) → tolerated by `_parse_llm_json_response`.
- Chatty prose around JSON (model violated JSON-only instruction) → tolerated; first `{...}` substring extracted.
- `notes` field >100 chars → truncated to 100 chars; the raw model output isn't exfiltrated to downstream UI.
- LLM emits a `unit` field (e.g. "EA", "LF") → appended to the `notes` field as `unit: <value>` (compact provenance) so downstream matching / UI can show it without growing the `BatchOverrideRow` schema.
- Tempfile not cleaned up (Windows AV / parallel GC race) → silent best-effort `os.unlink` with `OSError` swallow; no crash, no test flake.
- Same-session T8.1 + T8.2 use → both override paths apply cleanly on top of each other; both lines carry `MANUAL_OVERRIDE` tier; audit-trail tags remain distinguishable (`[sub-quote]` vs `[sub-quote-llm]`).

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Tempfile-free LLM bytes API.** `LLMClient.analyze_image` takes a file path, not bytes. T8.2 bridges via `tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile`. A future client extension that accepts `image_bytes` + `mime_type` directly would eliminate the disk write — minor overhead today (a few ms per page on SSD), but worth noting.
- **Per-page cost telemetry.** The Streamlit UI shows a $0.02-$0.10/page **estimate** before the click, but the actual provider cost (input tokens × pricing + output tokens × pricing) is never surfaced post-call. A future calibration could parse `LLMResponse.usage` (when populated) and surface the real cost in the apply summary so the operator sees the dollar amount, not just an estimate.
- **Multi-pass vision with page-grouping.** Today every page is sent independently. A future optimization would group adjacent pages (e.g. send pages 1-2 in one call when the table spans both) so the model can correlate continuation rows. Not on the calibration set's hot path.
- **Fine-tuned vision model.** Both Anthropic and OpenAI offer fine-tuning surfaces for vision; a sub-quote-specific fine-tune could lift accuracy + drop per-page cost. Heavy lift — only worth it after the calibration set hits ~500 real sub-quote PDFs.
- **OCR text-layer reuse.** If the PDF carries an OCR text layer (e.g. Acrobat-OCR'd scan), the T8.2 path ignores it and re-extracts via vision. A hybrid path that feeds the OCR text alongside the PNG could improve numerical accuracy on dense schedules at no extra cost.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T9 — Alternates / VE pricing.** Each `BidPackage` carries an `alternates` field that's currently informational; T9 would wire pricing branches per alternate and surface the delta in the headline. **This is the natural next slice now that T8 is closed end-to-end** — orthogonal feature (hits bid forms we already parse), no overlap with the operator-override family. ~3-5 day slice on the same dispatcher shape T8.1 / T8.2 used.~~ **T9.0 BACKEND SHIPPED** — see the Phase T9.0 section below. T9.1 (Streamlit alternates review tab + per-alternate toggle) and T9.2 (client PDF alternates section) remain explicit follow-ups.
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish.** Pick up the deferred items: multi-sheet Excel ingestion, unit-aware matching, propagate `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` into `line.notes` (current implementation tags only the `override_history` entry, not the `CostLine.notes` field), per-line undo, markup knob (auto +10-20% on every applied vendor unit_cost). Pure UX/quality slice; each item is independently shippable and worth ~0.5-1 day apiece.
- **T8.3 — Markup knob on the sub-quote apply form.** Add a `markup_pct` slider to both T8.1 and T8.2 expanders so the operator can apply a uniform +10-20% subcontractor markup at apply time without round-tripping through the per-line override. Low LOC, high-frequency operator request from the T8.1 calibration. Could ship under T6.4 as a single sub-item.

---

### Phase T9.0 — Bid alternates / Value-Engineering (VE) pricing (backend)

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lands the BACKEND half of the alternates / VE pricing slice: new schema (`AlternateType`, `AlternatePricingBasis`, `AlternateLine`, `AlternateLineEstimate`) + `ProjectModel.alternates` + `Estimate.alternates` with selection-aware subtotal/total helpers, deterministic bid-form alternate extraction with LLM-fallback reconciliation, cross-bid-package deduplication, estimator pricing branches (`extracted` / `synthesized_from_takeoff` / `operator_entered` / `missing`), a new "Bid Alternates" Excel worksheet + Project Summary alternates block, and JSON export of the new fields. UI (Streamlit review tab + per-alternate toggle) and the client-PDF alternates section are explicitly deferred to T9.1 / T9.2. Suite: 2121 passed, 1 skipped → 2253 passed, 1 skipped (+132 tests across five new files). **Closes the bid-package alternates-as-informational gap entirely on the backend** — every alternate from every parsed bid form now flows through a typed pricing pipeline, surfaces in the Excel deliverable with rollup totals (base / base+all-additive / base+all-deductive / base+all-substitution / base+default-selected), and exposes a clean selection-driven `subtotal_with_alternates_selected({"ALT-1", ...})` / `total_with_alternates_selected(...)` API for the T9.1 UI to drive without further backend work.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Schema shape — additive-only on `Estimate` and `ProjectModel`.** Four new public types in `core/schemas.py`: `AlternateType(str, Enum)` with values `additive` / `deductive` / `substitution` / `value_engineering`; `AlternatePricingBasis(str, Enum)` with `extracted_from_bid_form` / `operator_entered` / `synthesized_from_takeoff` / `missing` for full provenance traceability; `AlternateLine(BaseModel)` carrying `alternate_id`, `alternate_type`, `description`, `scope_summary`, `cost_delta` (Optional[float] — None when bid form is blank), `included_by_default` (bool — defaults False; True only for owner-mandated alternates pre-rolled into base), `related_takeoff_items` (list of takeoff entity_ids for synthesis), `related_csi` (list of CSI codes touched), `bid_package_id` (FK to `BidPackage`), `source_sheet`, `confidence` (0.0-1.0), `operator_notes`;
