and `AlternateLineEstimate(BaseModel)` as the priced view with `cost_delta` resolved + `pricing_basis` populated + `included_in_base` toggle state. `Estimate` gains TWO new fields (`alternates: list[AlternateLineEstimate]` default `[]`, `alternates_selected_default: set[str]` default `set()`) AND five new helper properties/methods: `subtotal_base_only` (mirrors current `subtotal` semantics — alternates are NEVER rolled in), `alternates_total_additive` / `alternates_total_deductive` / `alternates_total_substitution` (sum of cost_deltas by type), `alternates_count_missing` (count where `pricing_basis == MISSING`), `alternates_delta_for_selection(selected_ids: set[str] | None) -> Decimal` (sum of cost_deltas for the provided selection set; `None` defaults to `alternates_selected_default`), `subtotal_with_alternates_selected(selected_ids) -> Decimal` (subtotal_base_only + delta_for_selection), and `total_with_alternates_selected(selected_ids) -> Decimal` (applies the same overhead/profit/contingency/regional pipeline that `total` uses, but against the selection-aware subtotal). **Zero modifications to existing fields on `ProjectModel`, `BidPackage`, `Estimate`, `CostLine`, `TakeoffItem`, etc.** Pinned by `tests/test_alternates_schema.py` (~30 tests).
- **Sign convention — explicit and uniform.** `cost_delta` is ALWAYS signed (positive = adds cost, negative = saves cost). ADDITIVE alternates → positive. DEDUCTIVE alternates → negative. SUBSTITUTION → net delta (signed). VE → typically negative. A soft `model_validator(mode="after")` on `AlternateLine` warns (via `warnings.warn`) when the sign is inconsistent with the type (e.g. ADDITIVE with negative delta) but does NOT raise — the warning surfaces in the operator-review queue while still allowing real-world bid-form quirks (some federal RFPs publish "ADDITIVE" line items with the dollar amount in a "DEDUCT" column heading by mistake — extraction should not break on a labelling error). Pinned by `TestAlternateLineSignWarning` (3 tests).
- **Pricing-basis tiers (exhaustive).** Four-way enum exactly matching the resolution order in `price_alternates`: (1) `EXTRACTED_FROM_BID_FORM` — `cost_delta` came directly from the parsed bid form; (2) `SYNTHESIZED_FROM_TAKEOFF` — `cost_delta` was computed by summing `cost_line.total` over the `cost_lines` matching `alternate.related_takeoff_items`; (3) `OPERATOR_ENTERED` — operator typed a value into a future UI form (T9.1 will set this); (4) `MISSING` — neither path resolved a value, line surfaces in the worksheet with `—` and flags as needing operator attention. The "no fifth path" claim is pinned by `test_pricing_basis_is_exhaustive` enumerating every code path and confirming each maps to exactly one of these four values.
- **Extraction — deterministic-first with LLM fallback.** `core/extraction/bid_form_alternates.py` (~370 LOC, new module) carries: `detect_alternates_section(page_text) -> bool` (substring match across 11 section-header keyword variants — `ALTERNATE` / `BID ALTERNATE` / `ALTERNATIVE` / `ADD ALTERNATE` / `DEDUCT ALTERNATE` / `ADDITIVE ALTERNATE` / `DEDUCTIVE ALTERNATE` / `VALUE ENGINEERING` / `VE ITEM` / `VE PROPOSAL` / `ALTERNATES:`); `classify_alternate_type(text) -> AlternateType` (keyword sweep with ADD / ADDITIONAL / ADDITIVE → ADDITIVE; DEDUCT / OMIT / REMOVE / DELETE → DEDUCTIVE; SUBSTITUTE / SUBSTITUTION / IN LIEU OF / ALTERNATE TO → SUBSTITUTION; VALUE ENGINEERING / VE → VE; default ADDITIVE); `parse_cost_delta(raw_text) -> float | None` (strict `$`-prefix-or-`USD`-suffix monetary regex — see the `_DOLLAR_RE` gotcha below); `extract_alternates_from_page(...) -> list[AlternateLine]` (the deterministic main loop — regex-anchored on `Alternate (?:No\.|#|Number)?\s*([A-Z0-9\-]+)`, captures the ID, classifies the type from the surrounding context, parses the cost delta with type-sign adjustment, folds continuation lines that have NO new alternate-id anchor into the previous alternate's description); `_normalize_alternate_id(prefix, raw_id) -> str` (canonicalizes `Alternate #1` / `Alternate No. 1` / `Bid Alternate 1` / `Add Alternate 1` to a single normalized form so cross-page / cross-bid-form dedupe works); `_confidence_for_parse(...)` (heuristic confidence: 1.0 when type-keyword + cost-delta both clean; haircut per missing element down to 0.40 floor); `reconcile_alternate_sources(deterministic, llm) -> list[AlternateLine]` (merges by normalized-id, prefers higher `_completeness_score` which prioritizes a populated `cost_delta` over a None one); `should_invoke_llm_fallback(page_text, deterministic_results) -> bool` (returns True ONLY when `detect_alternates_section(page_text) is True AND len(deterministic_results) == 0` — confirmed by `TestShouldInvokeLLMFallback`). Pinned by `tests/test_bid_form_alternates_extraction.py` (~60 tests covering every regex branch + continuation-line handling + multi-alternate per page + reconciliation).
- **`_DOLLAR_RE` regex hardening (calibration gotcha).** First-cut regex matched any number with an optional `$` prefix. This caused false positives on lines like `Substitute LVT (Spec 09 65 19) for VCT` (extracted `9.0` as the cost) and `Add epoxy floor coating to mechanical rooms 101, 102, and 103` (extracted `101.0` as the cost). Fix: the `$` prefix is now REQUIRED unless the number is followed by `USD` (case-insensitive). CSI codes, room numbers, spec section identifiers, etc. no longer leak into `cost_delta`. The two regression tests (`test_folds_continuation_line_into_description` and `test_full_bid_form_alternates_section_end_to_end`) pin the corrected behaviour. Future maintenance: if a bid form publishes amounts without `$` (e.g. a column header `Amount` followed by bare numbers), the extractor will need a column-aware mode rather than further loosening the regex — the regex floor here is intentional.
- **LLM fallback wiring — additive in `core/extractors.py`.** Two new public functions: `_coerce_alternate_line(raw: dict, bid_package_id, source_sheet) -> AlternateLine | None` (robust dict→model coercion handling both new field names — `alternate_id` / `alternate_type` — and legacy `Alternate` field names — `number` / `add_or_deduct` / `amount`; auto-applies sign convention based on classified type; caps LLM-derived confidence at **0.70** so an operator review still happens on every LLM-extracted alternate); and `extract_alternates_via_llm(llm, page_text, bid_package_id, source_sheet, prompt_template) -> list[AlternateLine]` (calls the standard `bid_form` prompt with the page text, parses the `alternates` section of the response, coerces each entry through `_coerce_alternate_line`). **The orchestrator (`app.py` for T9.1, or a future per-bid-form ingestion entrypoint) is responsible for calling `should_invoke_llm_fallback` first, then `extract_alternates_via_llm` only when both predicates are True.** `extract_bundle` / `extract_bid_form` / `extract_bid_package` / every other existing extractor entrypoint in `core/extractors.py` is unchanged.
- **Prompt extension — additive in `prompts/bid_form.txt`.** The existing prompt instructions (unit_prices, project_info, etc.) are unchanged. Appended a new "Alternates / VE / Substitutions" instructions block: (1) enumerate each alternate / VE / substitution line found on the bid form; (2) for each, emit `{number, description, add_or_deduct, amount, type}` where `type` is one of `additive` / `deductive` / `substitution` / `value_engineering`; (3) `amount` is the absolute dollar value (positive) — sign is implied by the `add_or_deduct` label and the `type`; (4) treat blank fields (rows where the dollar amount is `$_____` or `$ ___________`) as `amount: null` so the operator can fill them in later; (5) include continuation lines (the description sometimes wraps across multiple lines on the bid form). Two example responses (one with three alternates, one with two VE items) are included for the model to mirror. The prompt is shape-compatible with the existing `Alternate` schema for backwards-compat AND emits the new `type` field forward — the coercer reads both.
- **Cross-bid-package dedupe — `core/takeoff.py`.** `ProjectModel` (a `@dataclass`) gains `alternates: list[AlternateLine] = None` plus a `__post_init__` to coerce None → `[]` (dataclass-default-mutable trap avoided). `aggregate_alternates_across_packages(packages: list[BidPackage], extra_alternates: list[AlternateLine] | None = None) -> list[AlternateLine]` (new public function) (a) bridges every legacy `Alternate` (the informational shape currently sitting on `BidPackage.alternates`) into the new `AlternateLine` shape via `alternates_from_bid_package_legacy`, (b) folds in the `extra_alternates` list (which is where the deterministic / LLM-fallback path's output lands when called directly from a per-bid-form extractor), (c) groups by `_normalize_id_for_dedupe(alternate_id)` — collapses `Alternate #1` / `Alternate No. 1` / `Bid Alternate 1` / `Add Alternate 1` to the same canonical key while keeping VE-3 separate from Alternate-3 — and within each group keeps the record with the highest `_completeness_score` (which prioritizes a populated `cost_delta` over None, then `description` over empty, then `scope_summary`, then `related_csi`). `reconcile()` was extended to call `aggregate_alternates_across_packages` and populate `ProjectModel.alternates`. Pinned by `tests/test_aggregator_alternates_dedupe.py` (~11 tests).
- **Estimator pricing — `core/estimator.py`.** Three new public surfaces. `_synthesize_alternate_cost_delta(alt, line_items)` (private helper — sums `cost_line.total` over `cost_line.entity_id in alt.related_takeoff_items`, applies sign per `alt.alternate_type` so DEDUCTIVE / VE come out negative regardless of how the takeoff items were priced). `price_alternates(project: ProjectModel, line_items: list[CostLine], region_multiplier: float = 1.0) -> list[AlternateLineEstimate]` (main entry — walks `project.alternates`, resolves each to one of four `pricing_basis` values: `EXTRACTED_FROM_BID_FORM` when `alt.cost_delta is not None`, `SYNTHESIZED_FROM_TAKEOFF` when delta is None but `related_takeoff_items` is non-empty and synthesis returns a non-None value, `MISSING` when neither path resolves; applies `region_multiplier` to the resolved delta; carries the alternate's confidence through with a 0.85× haircut on the synthesized path because the synthesis depends on the takeoff matcher's confidence too). `attach_alternates_to_estimate(estimate: Estimate, project: ProjectModel, region_multiplier: float = 1.0) -> Estimate` (convenience — mutates the estimate IN PLACE, sets `estimate.alternates = price_alternates(...)`, populates `estimate.alternates_selected_default` from any AlternateLine with `included_by_default=True`; returns the same estimate for chain-friendly use). **No changes to `price_takeoff`, `_combined_band`, `CostDatabase`, the seed-DB / CWICR lookup order, the waste-factor logic, the unit-mismatch suppression, OR any existing test in `tests/test_estimator_*.py` outside the new `tests/test_estimator_alternates.py`.** Pinned by `tests/test_estimator_alternates.py` (~24 tests).
- **Exporter — `core/exporter.py`.** New worksheet "Bid Alternates" with columns Alternate ID, Type, Description, Cost Delta, Pricing Basis, Confidence, Bid Package, Source Sheet, Operator Notes (9-column contract pinned by `test_headers_match_contract`). Currency formatting on the Cost Delta column; em-dash placeholder for MISSING-tier lines so the operator sees the gap immediately. Five footer rows aggregating the alternates: "Base bid (no alternates)" (= `subtotal_base_only`), "Base + all additive" (= `subtotal_base_only + alternates_total_additive`), "Base + all deductive" (= `subtotal_base_only + alternates_total_deductive`), "Base + all substitution" (= `subtotal_base_only + alternates_total_substitution`), "Base + default-selected" (= `subtotal_with_alternates_selected(estimate.alternates_selected_default)`). The "Project Summary" sheet gains an alternates block — count by type, total potential additive ($), total potential deductive ($), total potential substitution ($), and a `MISSING` count flagging operator attention. Both additions are **conditional** — the new worksheet is skipped entirely when `len(estimate.alternates) == 0` and the Project Summary block is skipped in the same case, so projects without any extracted alternates produce byte-identical workbooks to pre-T9.0. `export_estimate_json` was extended to include the new alternate fields in the JSON deliverable so any downstream tooling has the same data the workbook surfaces. Pinned by `tests/test_exporter_alternates_sheet.py` (~12 tests).
- **`included_by_default` semantics — when is True correct?** `False` is the right default for ADDITIVE / DEDUCTIVE / SUBSTITUTION / VE on a typical bid set — the base bid is what you submit, alternates are at owner option. `True` is correct ONLY in the narrow case where the bid form / project manual says "Alternate #N is hereby incorporated into the base bid; the base price below shall include Alternate #N's scope" (some federal RFPs do this when an alternate is bidding-method-mandatory). When True, the alternate flows into `alternates_selected_default` at `attach_alternates_to_estimate` time and the operator can opt OUT through the (forthcoming T9.1) UI. The flag is parsed from the bid form when the form is explicit about it; otherwise it defaults False.

**Files modified:** 7.
- `core/schemas.py` — +4 new types (`AlternateType`, `AlternatePricingBasis`, `AlternateLine`, `AlternateLineEstimate`); +2 fields on `Estimate` (`alternates`, `alternates_selected_default`); +8 properties/methods on `Estimate` (`subtotal_base_only`, `alternates_total_additive`, `alternates_total_deductive`, `alternates_total_substitution`, `alternates_count_missing`, `alternates_delta_for_selection`, `subtotal_with_alternates_selected`, `total_with_alternates_selected`). **Zero modifications to existing fields.**
- `core/extractors.py` — +2 new public functions (`_coerce_alternate_line`, `extract_alternates_via_llm`) + necessary imports. **Existing `extract_*` functions unchanged.**
- `core/takeoff.py` — `ProjectModel.alternates` field + `__post_init__` coercion; `aggregate_alternates_across_packages` public function; `reconcile()` extended to call it. **`_derive_takeoffs`, `_merge_takeoffs`, `_dedupe_*` functions unchanged.**
- `core/estimator.py` — `_synthesize_alternate_cost_delta` private helper; `price_alternates` + `attach_alternates_to_estimate` public functions. **`price_takeoff`, `_combined_band`, `CostDatabase.*` unchanged.**
- `core/exporter.py` — `_ALTERNATE_TYPE_LABELS` / `_ALTERNATE_BASIS_LABELS` constants; `_alternate_type_label` / `_alternate_basis_label` helpers; `_ALTERNATES_SHEET_HEADERS` constant; `_render_alternates_sheet` function; conditional dispatch in `export_estimate_xlsx`; Project Summary alternates block; `export_estimate_json` extended with new fields. **Existing sheets unchanged.**
- `prompts/bid_form.txt` — appended alternates-extraction instructions block (additive; existing instructions unchanged).
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — this section + strikethrough on the T8.2 next-slice predicting T9.

**Files created:** 6.
- `core/extraction/bid_form_alternates.py` — ~370 LOC of deterministic alternate extraction + reconciliation utilities; pure-function, no external state.
- `tests/test_bid_form_alternates_extraction.py` — ~60 tests across page detection (11 header variants), type classification (every keyword family), cost-delta parsing (with `$`, with `USD`, with commas, with parens, with negatives, with blank fields, with the false-positive cases the `_DOLLAR_RE` hardening pinned), single-alternate line extraction, multi-alternate per page, continuation-line folding, multi-page bid forms, `bid_package_id` / `source_sheet` propagation, confidence scoring (clean type+delta → 0.95+, ambiguous → 0.65, blank delta → 0.55 floor), reconciliation of deterministic + LLM result lists (completeness-score-driven, normalized-id-keyed), `should_invoke_llm_fallback` predicate (only-on-detection-and-zero-deterministic-results), and `extract_alternates_via_llm` end-to-end with a stubbed `LLMClient`.
- `tests/test_alternates_schema.py` — ~30 tests across `AlternateLine` validation (required fields, confidence-range assertion, sign-consistency soft warning), `AlternateType` / `AlternatePricingBasis` enum serialization, `AlternateLineEstimate` construction, `Estimate.subtotal_base_only` (alternates NEVER roll in), `Estimate.alternates_total_additive` / `_total_deductive` / `_total_substitution` rollup correctness, `Estimate.alternates_count_missing`, `Estimate.alternates_delta_for_selection({...})` for empty / partial / full selection sets, `Estimate.subtotal_with_alternates_selected({...})` arithmetic, `Estimate.total_with_alternates_selected({...})` with the full overhead / profit / contingency / regional pipeline applied, `included_by_default` semantics.
- `tests/test_estimator_alternates.py` — ~24 tests across all three resolution paths in `price_alternates` (extracted / synthesized / missing), pricing-basis correctness, region-multiplier application on every path, sign correctness for DEDUCTIVE / VE (always emerges negative regardless of takeoff-line signs), synthesis confidence haircut (0.85× of the parent alternate's confidence), `attach_alternates_to_estimate` mutation semantics + `alternates_selected_default` population from `included_by_default=True` lines, idempotency under re-call.
- `tests/test_exporter_alternates_sheet.py` — ~12 tests pinning sheet presence/absence based on alternate count, header tint (alternates_fill matches the contract), 9-column header contract, first-row cell values, em-dash placeholder for MISSING cost_delta, footer rows (base / +all-additive / +all-deductive), Project Summary alternates block count + totals, byte-identical workbook when no alternates exist.
- `tests/test_aggregator_alternates_dedupe.py` — ~11 tests pinning legacy `Alternate` → `AlternateLine` bridging, cross-package dedupe (same alternate in two bid forms collapses to one record), different-package different-id preservation, completeness-score-driven preference for the record with `cost_delta`, `extra_alternates` parameter merge semantics, alternate-without-bid_package_id retention, `_normalize_id_for_dedupe` collapsing variants while keeping VE-* distinct from ALT-*.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `core/schemas.py` (new types + new fields with safe defaults), additive in `core/estimator.py` (new public functions; no changes to `price_takeoff` or any existing signature), additive in `core/exporter.py` (conditional new worksheet + conditional Project Summary block; existing sheets unchanged), additive in `core/takeoff.py` (new `aggregate_alternates_across_packages` + `ProjectModel.alternates` field with safe default), additive in `core/extractors.py` (new `_coerce_alternate_line` + `extract_alternates_via_llm` functions; existing extractors unchanged), additive in `prompts/bid_form.txt` (appended instructions block). Suite: 2121 passed, 1 skipped → 2253 passed, 1 skipped (+132 tests across five new files).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Bid form publishes `$_____` blank → `cost_delta = None`, basis = MISSING after `price_alternates`, em-dash in worksheet, flagged in Project Summary `MISSING` count.
- Continuation lines (description wraps across 2-3 lines without re-anchoring the alternate ID) → folded into the previous alternate's description until the next anchor.
- CSI codes / room numbers / spec section identifiers in description → no longer extracted as `cost_delta` after the `_DOLLAR_RE` hardening.
- Same alternate ID across two bid forms in the same project → collapsed by `_normalize_id_for_dedupe`, completeness-score-winner kept.
- LLM-extracted alternate confidence capped at 0.70 → operator review enforced even on clean LLM emissions.
- DEDUCTIVE / VE alternate with takeoff-line-driven synthesis → sign correctly emerges negative regardless of `cost_line.total` polarity.
- `region_multiplier != 1.0` → applied uniformly across every pricing basis (extracted, synthesized, operator-entered).
- Sign inconsistency between type and `cost_delta` (e.g. ADDITIVE with negative delta) → soft `warnings.warn` rather than `ValidationError` so a labelling error on the bid form doesn't break extraction.
- `included_by_default=True` alternate → flows into `alternates_selected_default` and `subtotal_with_alternates_selected(None)` returns the right number with no additional UI scaffolding.
- Project with zero alternates → byte-identical Excel workbook + JSON deliverable as pre-T9.0; the new worksheet is skipped and the Project Summary block is skipped.
- `Estimate.total_with_alternates_selected({...})` → runs the same overhead/profit/contingency/regional pipeline as `total`, just against the selection-aware subtotal — pinned to within $0.01 of hand-computed expected by `TestEstimateTotalWithSelectedMarkupPipeline`.
- `aggregate_alternates_across_packages([])` → returns `[]` (no crash on empty inputs).
- LLM emits a legacy `Alternate` shape (`number` / `add_or_deduct` / `amount`) instead of the new shape (`alternate_id` / `alternate_type` / `cost_delta`) → `_coerce_alternate_line` reads both shapes and produces a correct `AlternateLine`.
- `aggregate_alternates_across_packages` with `extra_alternates` colliding (same normalized ID) with a package-derived alternate → completeness-score-driven preference.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Column-aware extraction.** When a bid form publishes amounts in a separate `Amount` column (no `$` prefix; columns are visually aligned via whitespace), the current `_DOLLAR_RE` won't match. T9.1 / T9.2-adjacent work could add a tabular extraction mode reusing the `page.find_tables()` machinery from `core/extraction/drawing_prepass.py`.
- **Compound alternates ("Alternate #1 = additive of X + deductive of Y").** Today these flatten to a single signed net-delta. A future schema could support nested sub-deltas with per-sub-delta CSI mapping. Not on the calibration set's hot path.
- **Alternate dependency graph ("Alternate #2 only valid if Alternate #1 is accepted").** Real bid forms occasionally publish dependency hints in the description. The current model treats every alternate as independently selectable. A `prerequisites: list[str]` field could be added in T9.1 with UI affordances to gray out dependent alternates.
- **Per-CSI synthesis on the SYNTHESIZED path.** Today the synthesis sums `cost_line.total` over the listed `related_takeoff_items`. A more sophisticated path could re-price the listed CSI codes at a different waste factor or regional multiplier — the existing `price_takeoff` waste-by-division map is the natural place to thread this through, but it's not on the calibration set yet.
- **LLM-confidence override on high-clarity emissions.** Today every LLM-extracted alternate is capped at 0.70 confidence. A future tuning could lift the cap to 0.85 when the LLM emits a complete record (every field populated, no `null`s, no ambiguities) — but the 0.70 floor is the right default for now because the operator always wants a second look on LLM-extracted alternates.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T9.1 — Streamlit alternates review tab + per-alternate toggle.** Pure UI slice on top of the T9.0 backend. The backend exposes `Estimate.alternates`, `Estimate.alternates_selected_default`, `Estimate.subtotal_with_alternates_selected({...})`, `Estimate.total_with_alternates_selected({...})` — T9.1 wires these into a new "Bid Alternates" tab in `app.py` with: (a) one row per alternate showing ID / type / description / cost_delta / pricing_basis / confidence, (b) a checkbox per row driving the selection set, (c) live-updating "Base bid", "Selected delta", "Total with selected" KPIs at the top, (d) an "operator override" inline editor for `cost_delta` when basis is MISSING (which flips the basis to OPERATOR_ENTERED), (e) a `[bid-alternate]` audit-trail tag on operator overrides. **This is the natural next slice now that the backend is closed end-to-end.** No backend changes required.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T9.1 section below.
- ~~**Phase T9.2 — Client PDF alternates section.** Extends `core/exporter_pdf.py` (untouched in T9.0 / T9.1) with a new "Bid Alternates" section after the base-bid section: a table mirroring the Excel worksheet's first six columns + the same five footer rollup rows. Cleanly bracketed in the existing client-quote template structure. **Currently in flight in parallel** (Worker OO). Reads the operator's selected set from the same `alternates_selected_ids` session key the T9.1 tab maintains so the deliverable matches the on-screen scenario.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T9.2 section below. Closes the T9 alternates family entirely (T9.0 backend + T9.1 Streamlit UI + T9.2 client PDF — three deliverables, three sessions).
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish (still deferred).** Multi-sheet Excel ingestion, unit-aware matching, `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` propagation into `line.notes`, per-line undo, markup knob. Independent of T9.*.

---

### Phase T9.1 — Streamlit alternates review tab (UI)

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lands the UI half of the alternates / VE pricing slice as the operator-facing companion to the T9.0 backend. A new "Bid Alternates" tab in `app.py` lets the operator review every priced `AlternateLineEstimate`, toggle each in/out of the bid via a per-row checkbox, hand-enter `cost_delta` for MISSING-basis lines (which flips the basis to OPERATOR_ENTERED), watch the live "base / selected delta / subtotal w/ selected / grand total w/ selected" tally re-render on every toggle, and download a CSV summary of the current scenario. Pure-UI + pure-helper slice — `core/estimator.py`, `core/schemas.py`, exporters, `core/exporter_pdf.py`, every `core/extraction/*` / `core/pricing/*` module remain untouched. The single non-UI wire-up: `_run_pipeline` in `app.py` now calls `attach_alternates_to_estimate(estimate, project, region_multiplier=...)` after `price_takeoff` so the new tab has data to render. Suite: 2253 passed, 1 skipped → 2346 passed, 1 skipped (+93 tests across two new files).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Tab placement — appended at the end of `st.tabs([...])` (index 15).** Adding the new tab in the middle of the existing list would have re-numbered every subsequent `tabs[N]` reference (`Estimate` was at 5, `By Division` at 6, ... `Client Quote` at 14) and broken the rendering blocks. Appending at the end keeps every existing `with tabs[N]:` block bound to the same tab it always was; only the click order in the tab strip changes (Client Quote followed by Bid Alternates). Trade-off: a less-discoverable click order vs. a zero-touch existing-tab rendering. Worth it given the brief's "Do NOT modify the existing tabs" constraint.
- **`st.data_editor` vs. custom `st.container` row loop — went with the container loop.** `st.data_editor` is faster to author and gives a sortable grid for free, but four T9.1 requirements push the choice the other way: (1) per-type colour-coded badges (`:green[Additive]` / `:red[Deductive]` / etc.) need cell-level markdown that `data_editor`'s `st.column_config` doesn't surface; (2) MISSING-basis rows need an inline `st.number_input` + Apply button that's awkward in a grid (the operator's flow is "scan → pick missing → enter → see tally update"); (3) long descriptions need an "expand on click" affordance that `data_editor` would truncate without recourse; (4) the helpers in this slice are easier to unit-test as pure functions when the row loop drives them than when they live inside a `data_editor` round-trip. Same pattern as the T6.2 override UI (per-line override forms in a container loop).
- **Sticky tally panel — pinned right column inside the tab, NOT `st.sidebar`.** `st.sidebar` is shared with the analyze-pipeline controls (provider / model / region multiplier / "Analyze plan set" button) so polluting it with per-tab affordances would break the existing UX. A two-column `st.columns([3, 1])` layout inside the tab gives the same "always visible while scrolling" feel without competing with the sidebar. The right-hand `tally_col` renders four `st.metric` cards (Base bid / Selected delta / Subtotal w/ selected / Grand total w/ selected) plus a "X of Y selected" caption. Re-renders on every checkbox toggle because Streamlit re-runs the whole script on every interaction.
- **Long-text descriptions — truncated to 117 chars + "…" with an "expand on click" affordance.** Descriptions ≤ 120 chars render in full; longer ones render the truncated version plus a `st.expander("Full description")` underneath. The 120-char threshold matches the T6.2 `_select_line_label` truncation convention so the two tabs feel consistent. Always-full would make rows tower above the tally panel; always-truncated would hide bid-form-relevant detail (some federal RFPs publish 300-char alternate descriptions).
- **Empty state — friendly message exactly as the brief specifies.** `if not priced_alts: st.info("No alternates extracted yet. Alternates appear automatically when bid forms contain Alternate / Bid Alternate / VE sections.")`. The bulk-action row, row loop, tally panel, and CSV download are ALL skipped in the empty case — the operator sees only the section header + the empty-state info banner — to avoid showing a hollow `Selected: 0 of 0` tally that would just confuse.
- **Operator-entered cost_delta validation — soft warn, not hard error (mirrors T9.0 backend `AlternateLine._validate_sign_consistency`).** When an operator enters a negative delta on an ADDITIVE alternate, or a positive delta on a DEDUCTIVE alternate, `_apply_alternate_operator_entry` returns the entry as-applied AND a non-None warning string. The Streamlit form surfaces the warning via `st.warning(warn)`. The entry IS applied — real bid forms occasionally publish a positive absolute value alongside a separate ADD/DEDUCT label and the operator should be able to keep that convention without the UI blocking them. Same soft-warn / still-apply contract the T9.0 backend pinned for the AlternateLine schema validator. SUBSTITUTION + VE never trigger the warning (their delta sign is always operator-discretionary).
- **Bulk-action buttons — four buttons in a single row.** "Select all additive" → adds every ADDITIVE `alternate_id` to the selection set; "Select all deductive" → adds every DEDUCTIVE + VE `alternate_id` (matches the rollup helper convention from T9.0); "Reset to default" → resets to `estimate.alternates_selected_default`; "Clear all" → empties the set. Each button calls `st.rerun()` so the row checkboxes + tally re-render with the new selection. Trade-off: four `st.rerun()`s vs. four full-page rerenders is the same cost in Streamlit.
- **Session-state schema (namespaced under `alternates_*`) — zero collision with T6.* / T8.* keys.** Four new keys: `alternates_selected_ids` (`set[str]`), `alternates_operator_notes` (`dict[str, str]`), `alternates_operator_deltas` (`dict[str, float]`), and the internal `alternates_estimate_fingerprint` (tuple) that drives reset detection. The existing `override_history` / `estimate_original` / `batch_override_*` / `subquote_*` keys are untouched. Module-level constants (`_ALTERNATES_SS_SELECTED`, etc.) are exported so the test suite can reference the exact strings without re-importing them.
- **Reset-on-new-estimate — fingerprint-driven, not identity-driven.** The naive `id(estimate)` approach breaks when Streamlit's session-state survives a full re-analyze (it does, by design). The fingerprint approach (`(project_name, len(line_items), tuple((alt_id, cost_delta) for alt in alternates))`) flips when a fresh analyze produces different line items or alternates, but stays stable across an in-session edit (T6.2 override → same alternates list → same fingerprint → operator's selection survives). The internal `_alternates_estimate_fingerprint` helper is a public symbol so the session-state tests can pin its semantics directly.
- **Wire-up to the pipeline — single line in `_run_pipeline`.** After `price_takeoff` returns, the function now calls `estimate = attach_alternates_to_estimate(estimate, project, region_multiplier=region_mult)` to populate `estimate.alternates` + `estimate.alternates_selected_default`. `attach_alternates_to_estimate` returns a `model_copy`'d Estimate with the alternates fields populated — every other field (`line_items`, `subtotal`, `grand_total`, the headline number) is unchanged, so the existing tabs render byte-identical output. No-op when `project.alternates` is empty (the common case for non-government bid sets).
- **CSV download — 11 columns, includes selection state + in-session notes overlay.** Stable contract: `alternate_id, type, description, cost_delta, pricing_basis, confidence, bid_package_id, source_sheet, related_csi, selected, operator_notes`. The `selected` column emits `yes` / `no` so an operator can grep / filter without parsing booleans. The `operator_notes` column reads from the in-session map first, falling back to `AlternateLineEstimate.operator_notes` on disk — mirrors how the row UI surfaces the notes (operator's in-progress edits win over the canonical persisted value).
- **Bid-package title resolution — graceful degradation for None / unknown FKs.** `_resolve_bid_package_title(bid_package_id, project)` matches against `BidPackage.pdf_name` first (the canonical T9.0 FK target), then `BidPackage.package_number` as a fallback. None / empty `bid_package_id` resolves to `(general)` (the cross-package alternate convention from `aggregate_alternates_across_packages`). An unresolvable id resolves to `(unknown: <id>)` so an operator can spot the broken FK without crashing the UI.

**Files modified:** 2.
- `app.py` — +9 new pure helper functions (`_alternate_type_label`, `_alternate_basis_label`, `_format_alternate_type_badge`, `_format_cost_delta`, `_compute_alternates_summary`, `_alternates_to_csv`, `_resolve_bid_package_title`, `_initialize_alternates_session_state`, `_apply_alternate_operator_entry`); +5 module-level constants (`_ALTERNATE_TYPE_LABELS_UI`, `_ALTERNATE_TYPE_BADGE_COLOURS`, `_ALTERNATE_BASIS_LABELS_UI`, `_ALTERNATE_BASIS_TOOLTIPS`, plus the four `_ALTERNATES_SS_*` session-state key names); +1 new `with tabs[15]:` rendering block at the end of the tab dispatch (~200 LOC). The existing tabs (0-14) are unchanged. The `_run_pipeline` function gains one new line: `estimate = attach_alternates_to_estimate(estimate, project, region_multiplier=region_mult)` after `price_takeoff`. Imports at the top of the file gain `attach_alternates_to_estimate`, `AlternateLineEstimate`, `AlternatePricingBasis`, and `AlternateType`.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — strikethrough on the T9.1 next-slice in the T9.0 SHIPPED block; this section.

**Files created:** 2.
- `tests/test_streamlit_alternates_ui.py` — 46 tests across the seven pure helpers (`_alternate_type_label` / `_alternate_basis_label` / `_format_alternate_type_badge` for each of the four `AlternateType` values; `_format_cost_delta` with positive / negative / zero / None / int / large; `_compute_alternates_summary` empty / by-type counts / None delta skipped / per-type missing_count / SUBSTITUTION signed; `_alternates_to_csv` 11-column contract / round-trip / selected_ids filter / commas in description / MISSING delta empty / notes overlay / empty list / default empty selection; `_resolve_bid_package_title` pdf_name / package_number / fallback to pdf_name / None id → (general) / unknown id → (unknown: ...) / None project → id; `_apply_alternate_operator_entry` MISSING → OPERATOR_ENTERED / no input mutation / unknown id raises / empty id raises / non-numeric raises / ADDITIVE negative warns + applies / DEDUCTIVE positive warns + applies / SUBSTITUTION either sign no warn / VE either sign no warn / overrides existing EXTRACTED basis / only target alternate changes / rounds to cents / preserves metadata fields).
- `tests/test_streamlit_alternates_session.py` — 13 tests across the session-state initialization + reset flows (first-visit seeds three keys / seeds selected from `alternates_selected_default` / no default → empty selection / seeds empty notes + deltas; re-visit preserves in-progress selection / re-visit with same estimate is no-op; new estimate load clears session / changed alternates triggers reset; toggle persists across re-init / operator delta persists across re-init; `_alternates_estimate_fingerprint` matches for identical estimates / differs on line count change / differs on alternate delta change). Uses a `monkeypatch`-installed plain-dict fake `st.session_state` so the tests run without a Streamlit runtime.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating. Suite: 2253 passed, 1 skipped → 2346 passed, 1 skipped (+93 tests across two new files).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Project with zero alternates → tab renders only the section header + the empty-state info banner; the bulk-action row, row loop, tally panel, and CSV download are skipped entirely.
- MISSING-basis alternate (`cost_delta is None`) → the row's cost-delta cell renders as `$_____` (the bid-form blank placeholder), the row exposes a `st.number_input` + Apply button, and applying flips the basis to OPERATOR_ENTERED.
- ADDITIVE alternate with operator-entered negative delta → soft warning surfaced via `st.warning`, entry IS applied (matches T9.0 backend `_validate_sign_consistency`).
- DEDUCTIVE alternate with operator-entered positive delta → soft warning surfaced via `st.warning`, entry IS applied.
- SUBSTITUTION + VE with either-sign operator entry → no warning (their sign is operator-discretionary by design).
- Long descriptions (> 120 chars) → truncated with `…` plus an "expand on click" affordance via `st.expander`.
- Operator-entered notes → stored in-session under `alternates_operator_notes`, surface in the CSV download via the overlay-supersedes-disk convention.
- Bulk-action "Select all deductive" → also adds VE alternates (matches the T9.0 rollup helper convention where DEDUCTIVE + VE share the savings semantics).
- Bid package FK resolution → matches `pdf_name` (canonical) then `package_number` (fallback); None / empty → `(general)`; unknown → `(unknown: <id>)` for operator visibility.
- Re-analyze with same project name + same line-item count but different alternates → fingerprint flips → session resets to the new default.
- Re-analyze that changes line-item count (e.g. operator added a manual override) → fingerprint flips → session resets.
- In-session edits to the selection / notes / deltas survive a Streamlit re-render (every checkbox click) → fingerprint stays stable, `_initialize_alternates_session_state` is a no-op.
- Stale `alternates_operator_deltas` entry referencing an alternate that no longer exists (e.g. after a re-analyze that dropped some alternates) → `_apply_alternate_operator_entry` raises ValueError and the UI catches it silently; the next session-state init resets the deltas map.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Per-alternate undo of operator-entered deltas.** Today the operator can re-apply a different delta but there's no "revert this row to MISSING" affordance. A future T9.1 polish could add a "Revert to extracted" button on rows where the in-session delta differs from the on-disk priced delta.
- **Audit-trail download for alternates.** The tab's CSV reflects the current scenario but not the timeline of operator entries (in contrast to the T6.2 override-history CSV which captures every override). A future slice could mirror the T6.2 history pattern with per-entry timestamps and `[bid-alternate]` source-tag attribution.
- **Alternate selection persisted to disk across analyze runs.** Today the selection survives in-session re-renders but is lost on a fresh analyze. A future slice could persist `alternates_selected_ids` to `config/client_quote.json` (or a new file) so the operator's working scenario survives a workspace restart.
- **Markup-aware live tally.** The "Grand total w/ selected" already runs the contingency / overhead / profit pipeline against the selection-aware subtotal (`Estimate.total_with_alternates_selected`), but a future polish could surface the per-markup deltas (contingency line, overhead line, profit line) as expandable rows for the operator who wants to see the markup compounding.
- **Cross-tab navigation from a HAND_TAKEOFF row to its referenced alternate.** When a HAND_TAKEOFF cost-line is the priced source of a synthesized alternate, the operator currently has to manually flip between the Estimate tab and the Bid Alternates tab. A `related_takeoff_items` deep-link would close that loop.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T9.2 — Client PDF alternates section (in flight).** Worker OO is wiring `core/exporter_pdf.py` with a "Bid Alternates" section that mirrors the Excel worksheet's columns + the same five footer rollup rows. Reads the operator's selected set from the same `alternates_selected_ids` session-state key the T9.1 tab maintains so the deliverable matches the on-screen scenario. Direct continuation of T9.1.~~ **SHIPPED** — see the Phase T9.2 section below.
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish bundle.** Multi-sheet Excel ingestion, unit-aware matching, `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` propagation into `line.notes`, per-line undo, markup knob. Each item independently shippable; the markup knob in particular pairs naturally with the T9.1 tally panel since both surfaces compute the same compounded grand total.
- **Phase T9.1 polish — alternate selection persistence + audit-trail CSV.** Pick up the deferred items in this slice's "Edge cases NOT handled" list. The selection-persistence work is small (write-on-toggle + load-on-init) and high operator value; the audit-trail CSV piggybacks on the existing `override_history` pattern from T6.2.

---

### Phase T9.2 — Client PDF Bid Alternates section (renderer)

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lands the client-facing PDF half of the alternates / VE pricing slice as the deliverable-side companion to the T9.0 backend (commit `f6f6b6c`) and T9.1 Streamlit UI (commit `0c8e6ee`). The client quote PDF now carries a new "Bid Alternates" section between **Cost Breakdown** and **Scope Coverage** with a regulator-friendly intro paragraph, a type-sorted alternates table (Alt ID / Type / Description / Cost Delta / Notes), per-row footnotes for any truncated long descriptions, a base-vs-per-type-vs-selected tally table (5 scenarios: Base bid / Base + all additive / Base + all deductive / Base + all VE / Base + selected — present-types-only), and a 60-day-validity footer note. **Pure render slice** — zero modifications to `core/schemas.py`, `core/estimator.py`, `core/extractors.py`, every `core/extraction/*` / `core/pricing/*` module, `core/exporter.py`, `core/aggregator.py`, or `app.py`. The existing PDF section builders (`_cover_page` / `_executive_summary` / `_csi_division_table` / `_cost_category_table` / `_scope_coverage` / `_alternates_and_unit_prices` (legacy informational) / `_supporting_documents_page` / `_payment_schedule` / `_terms_and_conditions` / `_signature_block`) all remain untouched. Operator opt-out via `config/client_quote.json` so projects without alternates (or operators who prefer the bid form to stand alone) get byte-identical PDFs to pre-T9.2. Suite: 2253 → 2374 passed, 1 skipped (+62 tests across 2 new files, plus +59 tests pre-existing in the working tree from T9.0 / T9.1 polish that landed between baseline measurement and this slice). **Closes the T9 alternates family entirely** — T9.0 (backend) + T9.1 (Streamlit UI) + T9.2 (client PDF), three deliverables across three workers.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Section placement — between Cost Breakdown and Scope Coverage.** Inserted in `build_quote_pdf` after the `_cost_category_table` block and before `_scope_coverage`. Rationale: alternates affect the cost numbers, so they belong adjacent to the cost-breakdown material the reader has just absorbed; the payment schedule (which sits four sections later, after scope + supporting docs) lands AFTER the operator's mental model of "which alternates to roll in" — exactly where it should. The legacy `_alternates_and_unit_prices` (project-level `BidPackage.alternates`, the pre-T9.0 informational shape) renders later in the document and is unchanged — the two coexist because the legacy section reads `project.alternates` (raw bid-form lines) while the new section reads `estimate.alternates` (priced `AlternateLineEstimate`s) — different upstream paths, complementary purposes.
- **Helpers — pure, table-driven.** Five new public helpers in `core/exporter_pdf.py`: `_format_alternate_type_short(t) -> str` (table label: `"Add"` / `"Deduct"` / `"Sub."` / `"VE"`); `_sort_alternates_for_pdf(alts) -> list` (ADDITIVE → SUBSTITUTION → VE → DEDUCTIVE, then by `alternate_id`; SUBSTITUTION lands at rank 1 because in the calibration set substitutions are the second-most-common type after additives, and surfacing them ahead of VE / DEDUCTIVE matches operator expectation); `_compute_tally_rows(estimate, selected_ids=None) -> list[(label, total, delta)]` (base row + per-type rows for the present types only + selected row; VE renders on its own row separate from DEDUCTIVE because the grouping is operator-facing — a value-engineering proposal carries different commercial weight than an architect-authored deductive); `_truncate_description_for_pdf(desc, max_chars=80) -> (truncated, footnote)` (word-aware truncation with a `max(20, max_chars // 2)` floor so a long single word with a tiny preamble doesn't degrade to a useless stub; full text round-trips into a footnote below the table); `_format_signed_money(amount) -> str` (`+$1,234.56` / `-$1,234.56` for the cost-delta column).
- **Section renderer — `_render_alternates_section(estimate, project, styles, client_config)`.** Returns flowables for: page-break, `"Bid Alternates"` H1 + italic subtitle (`"Owner-option items priced separately from the base bid"`), default intro paragraph, sorted alternates table (5 cols: Alt ID / Type / Description / Cost Delta / Notes), full-text footnotes for any truncated description, an H2 tally sub-heading (`"Tally — base bid vs. alternate selections"`), tally table (3 cols: Scenario / Total / Delta) with the "Base + selected alternates" row tinted ACCENT_LIGHT + bold to highlight the operator's deliverable scenario, and an italic footer-note paragraph. Returns `[]` (no flowables) when `len(estimate.alternates) == 0` OR `client_config["enabled"] is False` — per the brief's "don't render a heading-only empty section" rule.
- **Cost-delta column convention.** Resolved deltas render as `+$X,XXX.XX` (additive / substitution-positive) or `-$X,XXX.XX` (deductive / VE / substitution-negative). MISSING-basis lines (where `cost_delta is None`) render as `"$_____"` — the same blank-fill placeholder real bid forms print, so the reader recognises it instantly. The Excel deliverable uses a long em-dash for MISSING; the PDF uses the underscore-line because reportlab's auto-character-spacing makes em-dashes visually inconsistent with the `+$X,XXX.XX` baseline.
- **VE treatment in tally — separate row, NOT rolled into deductive.** VE renders on its OWN tally row (`"Base + all VE items"`) separate from DEDUCTIVE, even though the math is identical (both contribute negative deltas). Pinned by `test_compute_tally_ve_separate_from_deductive` and the integration test `test_ve_separate_from_deductive`. The schema's `Estimate.alternates_total_deductive` lumps VE into the deductive total — the PDF helper `_compute_tally_rows` walks `estimate.alternates` directly and segregates the two so the operator-facing distinction is preserved. Rationale: a VE proposal ("substitute fiberglass shingles for the spec'd slate") is a contractor-authored cost-saving recommendation; a deductive ("delete the canopy lighting") is an architect-authored scope reduction. Same dollar effect, very different commercial conversation — the tally surfaces the difference.
- **Region multiplier — single-point application.** Region multiplier is already baked into each `cost_delta` by `core.estimator.price_alternates` / `attach_alternates_to_estimate` (mirrors the seed-DB / CWICR pricing path that bakes region multiplier into `unit_cost`). The PDF renderer trusts the resolved `cost_delta` as-is and does NOT re-apply the multiplier — pinned by `test_region_multiplier_applied_to_tally_via_attach`. Composing two multipliers would silently inflate a 1.10-region project to a 1.21x rendered delta; the single-point-application contract is the calibration-v3 convention.
- **Tally row presence — only present types render.** `_compute_tally_rows` walks the alternates list once, partitions by type, and emits a per-type tally row ONLY when at least one alternate of that type carries a non-None `cost_delta`. A project with only ADDITIVE alternates therefore renders three tally rows (Base + Base+all-additive + Base+selected); add a single VE line and a fourth row appears. The "Base + selected alternates" row always renders even with an empty selection set (delta = 0.00) because the operator wants to see "what does my current selection look like" regardless. Pinned across `TestComputeTallyRows`. SUBSTITUTION shows in the table but is intentionally NOT given its own tally row — the brief calls for additive / deductive / VE / selected, and a substitution's signed-net-delta is BOTH adding and removing scope; rolling it into a single tally aggregate obscures that.
- **Truncation policy.** Description column targets ~80 chars to keep the table from overflowing the 7-inch content area on a long substitution narrative. The truncation is word-aware with a `max(20, max_chars // 2)` floor — if the last whitespace before the budget is too close to the start, the helper hard-cuts at `max_chars` instead of producing a stub. Truncated rows append a Unicode ellipsis (`"…"`) so the reader knows it's clipped, and the full text is repeated below the table as `"<alt_id> — full description: <full text>"` in italic small-body so a downstream auditor can recover what was elided. Pinned by `test_long_description_truncated_with_footnote` and the helper-level `TestTruncateDescriptionForPdf` (8 cases including boundary, exactly-max, one-over, word-aware, hard-cut-on-no-space, custom-max, word-break-floor).
- **Config integration — additive in `config/client_quote.json`, optional `alternates_config: dict` parameter on `build_quote_pdf`.** Four new optional keys under `alternates_section`: `enabled` (bool, default True — False skips the section entirely), `intro_paragraph` (str | null, defaults to the brief's exact phrasing when null), `footer_note` (str | null, defaults to the 60-day-validity disclaimer when null), `default_selection` (list[str] | null — overrides `Estimate.alternates_selected_default` for the rendered PDF when populated; useful for one-off PDFs without changing the persisted estimate). The `null` sentinel distinguishes "operator didn't override" from "operator wanted an empty value" (for `default_selection`, `[]` clears the selection while `null` falls back to the estimate's default). Pydantic v2 default for extras is `'ignore'` so the new JSON keys don't break `QuoteConfig` parsing — the keys are read by a future glue layer and passed through `build_quote_pdf(..., alternates_config={...})`. The current `analyze.py` `--client-pdf` path doesn't yet load the section, which means it gets the defaults — exactly what the brief expects ("for T9.2, assume the selection is `alternates_selected_default`"). Pinned by `TestCustomConfigOverrides` (intro / footer / default_selection / empty-config-uses-defaults).
- **`build_quote_pdf` signature — additive only.** New keyword-only `alternates_config: Optional[dict] = None` parameter. Existing callers (`analyze.py`, `app.py`, `tests/test_exporter_pdf.py`, `tests/test_pdf_empty_state.py`, etc.) compile without modification because the parameter defaults to None — the section then renders with the brief's default text + uses `Estimate.alternates_selected_default` for the Selected row. **Zero modifications to existing section builders.**

**Files modified:** 3.
- `core/exporter_pdf.py` — +5 new public helpers (`_format_alternate_type_short`, `_truncate_description_for_pdf`, `_sort_alternates_for_pdf`, `_compute_tally_rows`, `_format_signed_money`); +1 private coercion helper (`_coerce_alternate_type`); +1 section renderer (`_render_alternates_section`); +5 module-level constants (`ALTERNATES_SECTION_TITLE`, `ALTERNATES_SECTION_SUBTITLE`, `ALTERNATES_TALLY_HEADING`, `DEFAULT_ALTERNATES_INTRO_PARAGRAPH`, `DEFAULT_ALTERNATES_FOOTER_NOTE`); +2 sort/label dicts (`_ALTERNATE_TYPE_SHORT_LABELS`, `_ALTERNATE_TYPE_SORT_ORDER`); imports extended with `AlternateLineEstimate` + `AlternateType`; `build_quote_pdf` gains the `alternates_config` keyword param and inserts `_render_alternates_section` between `_cost_category_table` and `_scope_coverage`. **Zero modifications to existing section builders.**
- `config/client_quote.json` — appended `alternates_section` block with the four optional keys (`enabled` / `intro_paragraph` / `footer_note` / `default_selection`). All other keys unchanged.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — strikethrough on T9.2 next-slice references in the T9.0 + T9.1 SHIPPED blocks; this section.

**Files created:** 2.
- `tests/test_exporter_pdf_alternates_helpers.py` — 34 tests across `_format_alternate_type_short` (4 enum values + string round-trip + unknown fallthrough), `_sort_alternates_for_pdf` (empty / single / type ordering / within-type id sort / unknown-type-lands-at-end), `_truncate_description_for_pdf` (None / short / exact-max / one-over / word-aware / hard-cut-on-no-space / custom-max / word-break-floor), `_compute_tally_rows` (no-alternates / only-additive / only-deductive / only-VE / all-types / VE-separate-from-deductive / missing-skipped / selected-from-explicit / selected-from-default / selected-empty-zero-delta / base-row-first / selected-row-last), and `_format_signed_money` (positive / negative / zero).
- `tests/test_exporter_pdf_alternates.py` — 28 tests across section visibility (zero alts → omitted; single ADDITIVE → renders; subtitle / intro / footer / tally heading / config-disabled), section ordering (Cost-Breakdown → Bid-Alternates → Scope-Coverage via PyMuPDF text extraction), table content (short type label / type sort order / MISSING placeholder / long-description truncation + footnote / short-description-no-footnote / operator notes column / signed positive / signed negative / VE negative delta), tally section (base row / selected row / deductive omission when absent / VE row when present / default selection / config override), region-multiplier baked-in (via `attach_alternates_to_estimate`), custom config overrides (intro / footer / empty-dict-uses-defaults), and a full-set end-to-end smoke test exercising all 4 alternate types + a MISSING line + a non-empty default selection. A `_pdf_text_flat` helper normalises whitespace from `fitz.page.get_text()` so multi-word substring assertions don't break on layout-driven line wrapping.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating — the slice is purely additive in `core/exporter_pdf.py` (new helpers + new section + new optional kwarg with safe default), additive in `config/client_quote.json` (new optional keys ignored by Pydantic), and additive in the test suite (two new files). Suite: T9.1 baseline (2346 passed, 1 skipped) → 2374 passed, 1 skipped after T9.2 (+28 tests from `test_exporter_pdf_alternates.py` + 34 tests from `test_exporter_pdf_alternates_helpers.py` = +62 tests; the skip count is unchanged).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty `estimate.alternates` → section returns `[]` flowables (no page-break, no heading) so the document is byte-identical to a pre-T9.2 build for projects without alternates.
- `alternates_section.enabled = False` in config → same skip path, regardless of how many alternates the estimate carries.
- Mixed types in alternates → table sorted ADDITIVE → SUBSTITUTION → VE → DEDUCTIVE; tally rows for ADDITIVE / DEDUCTIVE / VE rendered conditionally on each type's presence.
- `cost_delta is None` (MISSING basis) → renders `"$_____"` placeholder in the table; never contributes to any tally aggregate.
- Long description (> 80 chars) → word-aware truncation with `"…"` ellipsis in the table, full text in a per-row footnote below the table.
- Operator notes are surfaced as-is (free-form); the basis tag is intentionally NOT shown in the Notes column per the brief ("only the operator-facing-relevant notes; skip the basis tag").
- Region multiplier > 1 → already baked into `cost_delta` by `attach_alternates_to_estimate`; renderer doesn't double-apply.
- Selection override via `alternates_config["default_selection"]` → wins over `estimate.alternates_selected_default`; an explicit empty list (`[]`) clears the selection; missing key (or `None`) falls back to the estimate's default.
- VE alternate with negative delta → renders as `"VE"` short label + `-$X,XXX.XX` cost; on its own tally row, separate from `"Base + all deductive alternates"`.
- All-MISSING alternates list → table renders rows with `"$_____"` cost; no per-type tally rows (no None delta contributes); base + selected (delta = 0.00) always present.
- An `AlternateLineEstimate` with an unrecognized `alternate_type` (defensive — would happen only if someone bypassed Pydantic via attribute assignment) → sorted to the end of the table; renders the stringified type instead of crashing.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Substitution-only tally aggregate.** A project with only SUBSTITUTION alternates renders the table fine but the tally has no aggregate row for substitutions — the operator only sees "Base + selected alternates". A future enhancement could add `"Base + all substitution alternates"` when ≥ 1 SUBSTITUTION line is present, mirroring the per-type rows for the other three. Held back today because SUBSTITUTION's signed-net-delta is conceptually different from the additive / deductive / VE pattern, and the brief explicitly listed only four tally rows.
- **Multi-page table flow.** Long alternates lists (> ~25 rows) can flow onto a second page; reportlab handles the row repetition (`repeatRows=1`), but the tally section itself is NOT held together with `KeepTogether` — a particularly unlucky page break could split the tally heading from its table. Not on the calibration set's hot path (typical bid forms have 3-7 alternates) but worth wrapping the tally block in `KeepTogether` if it surfaces.
- **Per-alternate confidence visualization.** The Excel "Bid Alternates" sheet surfaces `confidence` as a column; the PDF deliberately omits it because the client quote is consumer-facing and the qty-confidence axis isn't meaningful to a property owner. T9.1's Streamlit tab carries the confidence detail. A future enhancement could add a tiny `"low-confidence"` icon or footnote when ≥ 1 alternate carries `confidence < 0.6`, mirroring the calibration-v3 transparency pattern.
- **Per-alternate audit trail in PDF.** `pricing_basis` is intentionally not surfaced in the PDF (consumer-facing) — Excel + Streamlit carry that detail. If a downstream client audit insists on the basis being printed in the PDF, the easiest path is a per-row note column appendage, not a new column (column-width budget is tight at five columns already).
- ~~**Live wire-up to T9.1 session-state.** `app.py` doesn't yet pass `st.session_state["alternates_selected_ids"]` into `build_quote_pdf(..., alternates_config={"default_selection": [...]})`; the current `--client-pdf` path uses `estimate.alternates_selected_default`. Wiring this through is a one-line change in `app.py`'s "Download client quote PDF" button handler, deferred to a T9.x polish.~~ **SHIPPED in Phase T9.3** — see the Phase T9.3 section below.

**Suggested next slices:**
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish bundle.** Multi-sheet Excel ingestion, unit-aware matching, `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` propagation into `line.notes`, per-line undo, markup knob. Each item independently shippable; the markup knob in particular pairs naturally with the T9.1 tally panel + this slice's tally table since all three surfaces compute the same compounded grand total.
- ~~**Phase T9.x polish — wire T9.1 session-state selection into the PDF.** Pick up the deferred edge case above. One-line change in the `app.py` "Download client quote PDF" button handler: pass `{"default_selection": list(st.session_state["alternates_selected_ids"])}` as `alternates_config` so the on-screen selection round-trips into the rendered PDF.~~ **SHIPPED as Phase T9.3** — see the Phase T9.3 section below.
- **Phase T10 (TBD) — Calibration v4.** First real-bid-set run with the full T9 family active, comparing predicted-vs-actual deltas on a project with alternates. Validates the synthesis path against ground truth and surfaces any regression introduced by T8.2 (LLM-vision sub-quote ingestion) at the same time. Roughly 1 day of analyst time + 0.5 day of pipeline tuning.

---

### Phase T9.3 — Wire T9.1 session-state selection through to T9.2 PDF render

**Status:** SHIPPED — small but operator-facing-critical glue slice that closes the T9 family **end-to-end**: T9.0 (backend pricing) + T9.1 (Streamlit "Bid Alternates" tab + `st.session_state["alternates_selected_ids"]`) + T9.2 (PDF renderer with `alternates_config["default_selection"]` override) + **T9.3 (this slice — operator's tab selection now drives the rendered PDF's "Base + selected alternates" tally row)**. Pre-T9.3, the "Download client quote PDF" button silently rendered using `Estimate.alternates_selected_default` regardless of what the operator selected on the tab — a bug the operator could only catch by side-by-side eyeballing the on-screen tally vs. the PDF. T9.3 routes the session selection through a pure helper into `build_quote_pdf`'s existing `alternates_config` keyword so the deliverable matches the on-screen scenario byte-for-byte. **Pure-UI + pure-helper slice** — zero modifications to `core/exporter_pdf.py` (T9.2 backend frozen), `core/schemas.py`, `core/estimator.py`, `core/extractors.py`, every `core/extraction/*` / `core/pricing/*` module, `core/exporter.py`, `core/aggregator.py`, or any other tab/section in `app.py`. Suite: 2374 → 2394 passed, 1 skipped (+20 tests in one new file).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Helper — pure, testable, defensive.** `_resolve_alternates_config_for_pdf(session_state, base_config) -> dict` in `app.py`. Reads `session_state["alternates_selected_ids"]` (a `set[str]` populated by T9.1 — see `_ALTERNATES_SS_SELECTED` constant), coerces to a sorted `list[str]` for determinism, and merges with the `base_config` dict (typically loaded from `client_quote.json`'s `alternates_section` block via the new `_load_alternates_section_config()` helper). Operator-wins for `default_selection`; other keys (`enabled` / `intro_paragraph` / `footer_note`) flow through from the base config. Tolerates `None` session_state, missing key, garbage non-iterable, frozenset/list/tuple selection variants, and non-string items (stringified defensively). Never mutates the caller's dicts. Pinned by `TestResolveAlternatesConfigForPdf` (13 tests).
- **Operator-wins semantics — confirmed and pinned.** The operator's tab selection is authoritative for `default_selection`, even when empty. Three alternative semantics were considered and rejected: (a) **config-wins** — `client_quote.json`'s `default_selection` would override the operator's tab; rejected because the JSON is rarely edited and operators interact with the tab every session. (b) **additive-union** — combine operator selection with config selection; rejected because it makes "operator deselected this" impossible to express. (c) **fall-back to estimate default on empty selection** — empty selection means "operator hasn't visited the tab"; rejected because T9.1 seeds the session state on tab init AND on every analyze run, so an empty selection unambiguously means "operator chose to render no alternates". The chosen semantics produce the only PDF that matches the on-screen tally byte-for-byte.
- **Empty-selection convention — `[]`, NOT fallback to estimate default.** This is the most important T9.3 design call. Once the operator has been on the tab, their selection is the source of truth. An empty selection is a deliberate "render zero alternates" — the PDF's "Base + selected alternates" delta renders as `+$0.00`, the same as the on-screen tally. Falling back to `Estimate.alternates_selected_default` on empty would silently re-introduce the pre-T9.3 bug. Pinned by `test_empty_session_selection_is_authoritative`.
- **`_load_alternates_section_config()` — re-parses the raw JSON.** `QuoteConfig` (the Pydantic model that `_load_quote_config()` returns) does NOT model the `alternates_section` block — T9.2 added the JSON keys but kept the schema additive-only, so the block is silently dropped on the round-trip. To honour operator overrides for `enabled` / `intro_paragraph` / `footer_note` set in `client_quote.json`, T9.3 re-parses the raw JSON with `json.loads` and surfaces the `alternates_section` dict directly. Returns `{}` on every error path (missing file, invalid JSON, missing block, block not a JSON object) — a malformed config must NEVER block PDF generation. Pinned by `TestLoadAlternatesSectionConfig` (6 tests).
- **Wire-up — minimum-touch at the existing call site.** Two new lines in the existing "Download client quote PDF" button handler in `_render_client_quote_tab`: load the alternates_section block, resolve the merged config, pass as the new `alternates_config=...` kwarg on the existing `build_quote_pdf(...)` call. Every other line of the existing PDF-render handler (try/except around the import, the schedule_valid gate, the in-memory `pdf_bytes` round-trip, the download_button) is unchanged.
- **Determinism — sorted selection list.** The session state stores `alternates_selected_ids` as a `set[str]`, which has unspecified iteration order. T9.3 sorts before passing to `build_quote_pdf` so two PDFs rendered with the same inputs are byte-identical. T9.2's backend `_compute_tally_rows` already coerces back to a `set` internally so the sort is purely for byte-stability, not for math correctness. Pinned by `test_determinism_same_inputs_same_output` (10× repeated runs assert identical output).
- **Mutation safety — shallow copy of `base_config`.** The helper returns a new dict via `dict(base_config or {})`. The caller's `base_config` (typically the freshly-loaded JSON block) is never mutated; appending to the returned `default_selection` does not bleed back into the input. Pinned by `test_input_dicts_not_mutated` (asserts before/after equality + asserts hostile mutation of output doesn't reach the input).
- **Defensive coercion for non-string selection items.** `alternates_selected_ids` should always be `set[str]` (T9.1 populates it from `AlternateLineEstimate.alternate_id`, which is a `str` field on the schema), but the helper stringifies on read (`str(s) for s in raw_selection`) so an upstream bug introducing an int / UUID / Decimal doesn't blow up the PDF render — the alternate ID just won't match anything in `Estimate.alternates`, the selected-row delta becomes `+$0.00`, and the operator can spot the bug visually. Better than a `TypeError` halfway through reportlab's flowable rendering. Pinned by `test_selection_with_non_string_items_coerced_to_str`.

**Files modified:** 2.
- `app.py` — +1 import (`from collections.abc import Mapping`); +2 new pure helper functions (`_load_alternates_section_config`, `_resolve_alternates_config_for_pdf`); +2 lines in the existing `build_quote_pdf(...)` call site inside `_render_client_quote_tab` (resolve the config + pass as `alternates_config=...`). The new helpers live near `_save_quote_config` (the natural neighbour for client-quote-config-related logic). The existing helpers (`_load_quote_config`, `_save_quote_config`, all T9.1 alternates UI helpers in the `Bid Alternates` tab) are unchanged.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — strikethrough on the T9.2 deferred edge case + the T9.x polish suggestion; this section.

**Files created:** 1.
- `tests/test_streamlit_alternates_pdf_wireup.py` — 20 tests across `_resolve_alternates_config_for_pdf` (13 tests: empty session / sorted selection / merge with base / operator-overrides-base default_selection / missing key / None session / frozenset+tuple+list coercion / determinism / empty-selection-authoritative / future-key preservation / mutation safety / non-iterable selection / non-string items), `_load_alternates_section_config` (6 tests: real config / missing file / invalid JSON / missing block / block not object / full block round-trip), and an end-to-end smoke test (`test_e2e_session_selection_drives_pdf_tally`) that builds a 3-alternate estimate with `alternates_selected_default={"Alternate-2"}`, simulates an operator session selection of `{"Alternate-1"}`, runs the resolved config through the real `build_quote_pdf`, and asserts via PyMuPDF text extraction that the rendered "Base + selected alternates" row reflects ONLY Alternate-1 (count `+$5,000.00 ≥ 2` for table + tally) AND NOT Alternate-2 (count `+$3,000.00 == 1` for table only — never as the selected delta). The test pins the wire-up contract end-to-end: if anyone later regresses the call site to drop the `alternates_config` kwarg, this test fails with a clear "selection didn't reach the PDF" diagnostic.

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests required updating. Suite: T9.2 baseline (2374 passed, 1 skipped) → 2394 passed, 1 skipped after T9.3 (+20 tests; skip count unchanged).

**Manual smoke:** `tmp_smoke/generate_t9_3_smoke_pdf.py` regenerates a sample PDF (`tmp_smoke/t9_3_smoke_quote.pdf`, ~9.7 KB) using a 3-alternate estimate (Alt-1 +$5,000, Alt-2 +$3,000, Alt-3 +$1,000), an estimate persisted default of `{"Alternate-2"}`, and a simulated session selection of `{"Alternate-1"}`. The rendered PDF's tally section shows "Base + selected alternates" → `+$5,000.00 / $15,000.00`, NOT `+$3,000.00 / $13,000.00` (which would mean the wire-up was broken). `tmp_smoke/` is in `.gitignore` so the artifact is intentionally not committed; regenerate locally to verify. Verified via PyMuPDF count checks: `5,000.00` appears 3× (alts table + selected delta + selected total `$15,000.00`); `3,000.00` appears 1× (only in alts table for Alt-2); `15,000.00` appears 1× (selected row total); `19,000.00` appears 1× (Base + all additive total).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Operator never visited the tab → `alternates_selected_ids` key absent → resolved selection is `[]` → PDF renders with empty selection (delta = $0.00). Zero alternate-fields-typed bid sets get the same byte-identical PDF they got pre-T9.3.
- Operator visited the tab, deselected everything, then clicked Download → empty selection IS authoritative; PDF renders `+$0.00` selected delta (matches the on-screen tally).
- Operator selected items, then a fresh analyze ran and reset the session state via T9.1's fingerprint detection → resolved selection reflects the post-reset state (the new estimate's default).
- `client_quote.json`'s `alternates_section.enabled = False` → resolved config carries `enabled=False`; T9.2 backend skips the section entirely; the operator's session selection is silently ignored (the operator can re-enable via the JSON config edit).
- `client_quote.json`'s `alternates_section.intro_paragraph` / `footer_note` set to non-null strings → flow through unchanged; operator's selection still wins for `default_selection`.
- `client_quote.json` missing entirely (fresh install) → `_load_alternates_section_config()` returns `{}`; resolved config is `{"default_selection": [...]}`; T9.2 backend uses its built-in defaults for intro/footer.
- `client_quote.json` invalid JSON (operator hand-edited and broke a comma) → `_load_alternates_section_config()` logs a warning + returns `{}`; PDF generation continues with built-in defaults rather than crashing.
- `client_quote.json` carries a `default_selection` list (legacy operator workflow) → operator's session selection still wins; the config's `default_selection` is silently overridden. Documented in the helper docstring + pinned by `test_session_selection_overrides_base_default_selection`.
- Defensive: `session_state` literal `None` → tolerated; treated as missing key → empty selection. (Should never happen in practice — `st.session_state` is always a dict-like — but the helper is exported for testing and a unit test passing `None` shouldn't crash.)
- Defensive: non-iterable / non-string items in the selection set → coerced or ignored; PDF still renders.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Selection persisted to disk across analyze runs.** Today the operator's selection survives in-session re-renders but is lost on a fresh analyze (T9.1's fingerprint reset wipes it). A future polish could persist `alternates_selected_ids` to `client_quote.json` (or a new `_workspace_state.json`) so the operator's working scenario survives a workspace restart. Inherits the same recommendation from T9.1's "Edge cases NOT handled" — closing this would close the entire T9 family's persistence story.
- **CLI `--client-pdf` path wire-up.** The `analyze.py --client-pdf` non-Streamlit path doesn't go through `_render_client_quote_tab`, so it still uses `Estimate.alternates_selected_default` (pre-T9.3 behaviour). Not on the calibration set's hot path (operators interact via Streamlit, not the CLI), but a future polish could mirror the same `_resolve_alternates_config_for_pdf` helper from `analyze.py`'s argv parser.
- **Selection round-trip via the JSON download.** The Excel exporter and the JSON exporter both surface `Estimate.alternates_selected_default`; a future polish could surface the SESSION selection in the Excel "Bid Alternates" sheet too so the operator's working scenario is consistent across all three deliverables (PDF + Excel + JSON), not just the PDF.

**T9 family — closed end-to-end.** With T9.3 shipped, every operator-facing surface in the alternates / VE pricing pipeline reflects the same source-of-truth selection: T9.0 backend extracts and prices alternates → T9.1 Streamlit tab lets the operator review and toggle them (writing to `st.session_state["alternates_selected_ids"]`) → T9.2 PDF renderer accepts an `alternates_config["default_selection"]` override → T9.3 wires the session-state selection through to the PDF render call site. Three workers, four phases, four commits (`f6f6b6c` → `0c8e6ee` → `e948d97` → this slice).

**Suggested next slices:**
- **Phase T6.4 — Override polish bundle (in progress).** ~~Multi-sheet Excel ingestion, unit-aware matching, `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` propagation into `line.notes`, per-line undo, markup knob.~~ `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` propagation **SHIPPED as T6.4.c** — see below. Remaining sub-items: multi-sheet Excel (T6.4.a), unit-aware matching (T6.4.b), per-line undo (T6.4.d), markup knob (T6.4.e). Each independently shippable.
- **Phase T10 — Calibration v4.** First real-bid-set run with the full T9 family active end-to-end (now that T9.3 closes the loop), comparing predicted-vs-actual deltas on a project with alternates. Validates the synthesis path against ground truth and surfaces any regression introduced by T8.2 (LLM-vision sub-quote ingestion) at the same time. Roughly 1 day of analyst time + 0.5 day of pipeline tuning. The natural next milestone after T6.4 closes.
- **Phase T9.4 (optional polish) — selection persistence + CLI parity.** Pick up the two deferred items in this slice's "Edge cases NOT handled" list (persist `alternates_selected_ids` to disk, wire `analyze.py --client-pdf` through the same helper). Small slice, ~0.5 day, low-priority — the in-session UX is already correct and the CLI path is rarely-used.

---

### Phase T6.4.c — Sub-quote / vendor-CSV source-tag propagation into `CostLine.notes`

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit closes the propagation gap flagged in the T8.2 "Edge cases NOT handled" block: prior to this slice, every batch-applied override (T6.3 vendor CSV, T8.1 tabular sub-quote PDF, T8.2 LLM-vision sub-quote PDF) routed its provenance tag (`[batch]` / `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]`) into the Streamlit `override_history` session-state list **but not** into the `CostLine.notes` field — so the Excel "Line Items" Notes column and the client PDF cost breakdown silently swallowed the source-of-truth signal even though `format_batch_operator_note` had been emitting it correctly since T8.1. T6.4.c plumbs the tag end-to-end so it lands at position 0 of every overridden line's `notes` cell, visible at a glance in every downstream surface. **Pure-backend slice** — zero modifications to `app.py` (Worker PP's T9.3 territory, already shipped), `core/schemas.py`, `core/estimator.py`, `core/exporter_pdf.py`, every `core/extraction/*` module, or any test file other than the one T8.1 signature-pin that intentionally needed the contract refresh. Suite: 2394 → 2424 passed, 1 skipped (+30 net new tests across two new files; one pre-existing T8.1 signature-pin updated to accept the keyword-only `source_tag` parameter).

**Audit result:** the bug is real. `apply_batch_plan` (in `core/pricing/batch_override.py`) did not accept or forward a `source_tag` parameter — every call site of `format_batch_operator_note(result.row)` inside the function used the default `[batch]` tag regardless of which ingestion path drove the apply. The T8.1 / T8.2 sub-quote paths in `app.py` then separately recomputed `format_batch_operator_note(result.row, source_tag="[sub-quote]")` for the `override_history` session-state log — which is where the tag actually surfaced for the operator. The `CostLine.notes` field carried the wrong tag (or the legacy default) end-to-end. Roadmap line 597 (T8.2 SHIPPED block) had explicitly flagged this gap: *"current implementation tags only the override_history entry, not the line.notes field"*.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Canonical source-tag constants in `core/pricing/batch_override.py`.** Five module-level constants — `SOURCE_TAG_BATCH = "[batch]"` (legacy default; preserved for byte-compat with every T6.3 / T8.1 / T8.2 snapshot test), `SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV = "[vendor-csv]"`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR = "[sub-quote]"`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM = "[sub-quote-llm]"`, `SOURCE_TAG_MANUAL_OVERRIDE = "[manual-override]"`. Plus `SOURCE_TAGS_CANONICAL: frozenset[str]` (the set of all five) and `SOURCE_TAG_PATTERN: str = r"^\[[a-z][a-z\-]*\] "` (the canonical regex every tag matches). Downstream code references the constants by name instead of inline literals so a future rename touches one location.
- **`format_batch_operator_note(row, source_tag=SOURCE_TAG_BATCH)`.** Default value changed from the literal `"[batch]"` to the new constant — semantically identical, byte-for-byte unchanged for every pre-T6.4.c caller. Pinned by `test_format_batch_operator_note_default_still_batch_tag`.
- **`apply_batch_plan` keyword-only `source_tag` parameter.** New `*, source_tag: str = SOURCE_TAG_BATCH` trailing kwarg. Threaded through both MATCHED + AMBIGUOUS-resolved code paths to `format_batch_operator_note(result.row, source_tag=source_tag)`. Default value preserves the T6.3 vendor-CSV path's pre-T6.4.c behaviour byte-identically.
