Updates one T8.1 signature-pinning test (`test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged`) to assert the new contract: `source_tag` is the trailing keyword-only parameter with the `SOURCE_TAG_BATCH` default — every pre-T6.4.c positional call still works.
- **`_rewrite_notes_with_tag_first(...)` helper.** The novel piece of the slice. After `apply_manual_override` returns (which writes notes in the legacy `<prior_notes> | operator override: <payload>` shape), the helper rewrites the line's `notes` field to `{source_tag} operator override: {payload-without-leading-tag} [ | previous: {prior_notes}]` so the source tag lands at position 0. Idempotency: re-applying the same plan twice does NOT accumulate duplicate tags — the helper detects when `prior_notes` already starts with the same head and short-circuits to return `prior_notes` unchanged.
- **Re-apply semantics: most-recent-wins.** A T8.1 apply followed by a T8.2 apply on the same line writes `[sub-quote-llm]` at position 0 and preserves `[sub-quote]` inside the `| previous: ...` suffix so an auditor can reconstruct the full override-history chain from the `notes` cell alone (no need to consult the Streamlit session state). Same for T6.3 → T8.1 → T8.2 / T8.1 → T6.3 / any permutation. Pinned by `test_reapply_subquote_then_llm_tag_swaps_at_front` and `test_reapply_vendor_csv_after_subquote_swaps_tag`.
- **`apply_subquote_plan(estimate, plan, *, llm=False, ...)` wrapper in `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py`.** Thin wrapper that picks `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR` or `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM` based on the `llm` flag and forwards every other argument to `apply_batch_plan`. Exists so a downstream Streamlit / CLI caller does not have to import the constants directly — the boolean flag captures the intent. Pure-logic; no I/O, no Streamlit. `app.py` will pick this up in a future PP-territory slice (one-line change at each of the two existing `apply_batch_plan(...)` sub-quote call sites). Pinned by `test_apply_subquote_plan_default_uses_tabular_tag` and `test_apply_subquote_plan_llm_flag_uses_llm_tag`.
- **Manual-override-after-batch is out of scope.** `apply_manual_override` is the T6.1 single-line primitive that does NOT route through `format_batch_operator_note`; a manual override applied AFTER a batch apply preserves the batch tag inside the prior-notes string but does not stamp `[manual-override]` at position 0. This is documented and pinned by `test_manual_override_after_batch_apply_uses_legacy_format` — a future slice can add a `format_manual_override_note` helper if the calibration set demands it.
- **Exporter unchanged.** `core/exporter.py`'s "Line Items" sheet already surfaces `CostLine.notes` verbatim in the rightmost column ("Notes") with `_autosize(ws)` default `max_width=60`. Auto-sizing widens the column to `min(longest+2, 60)` chars — easily enough to show the `[sub-quote-llm] operator override: ...` tag-plus-sentinel (35 chars) at a glance. Five new exporter-side tests pin: header location, cell-value round-trip, tag-at-start across all three sources, column width ≥ 35, multi-line consistency.
- **No `app.py` changes.** Worker PP's T9.3 selection wire-up is already shipped; the T6.4.c backend is ready and a future one-line PR can update the two existing `apply_batch_plan(...)` sub-quote call sites in `app.py` to use the new `apply_subquote_plan(estimate, plan, llm=...)` wrapper (or pass `source_tag=...` directly). Until then, the operator-history session-state log still shows the right tag (unchanged from T8.2); the new tag-propagated `notes` field will surface once the one-line `app.py` wire-up lands.

**Notes format chosen (the canonical shape):**

```
[<source-tag>] operator override: [vendor: <V>] [quote-ref: <Q>] [csv-row: N] <notes-from-row> [ | previous: <prior-notes> ]
```

* `[<source-tag>]` is one of the five `SOURCE_TAG_*` constants; matches the regex `^\[[a-z][a-z\-]*\] ` (anchored).
* `operator override:` is the T6.1 `MANUAL_OVERRIDE_NOTE_PREFIX` sentinel — preserved verbatim immediately after the tag so a downstream reader can still detect "this line was hand-priced" with a single substring lookup.
* The `[vendor:..]` / `[quote-ref:..]` / `[csv-row: N]` / vendor-notes payload comes from `format_batch_operator_note` (one or more square-bracketed fields followed by free-text from the row's `notes` column).
* The `| previous: ...` suffix is only appended when the line had non-empty `notes` before the override. Re-applying the SAME override twice does NOT add a `| previous:` suffix (idempotency contract).

**Example.** After a T8.2 LLM-vision apply on a line whose prior `notes` was `"LL@$45/hr; sub-by-AeroMech"`:

```
[sub-quote-llm] operator override: [vendor: Trane] [quote-ref: Q-8821] [csv-row: 3] includes startup commissioning | previous: LL@$45/hr; sub-by-AeroMech
```

**Re-apply semantics — chosen: most-recent-wins with previous-chain preserved.** Three alternatives considered:
- **(a) most-recent-wins, prior-tag preserved in `| previous:` suffix** (CHOSEN) — auditor reconstructs full chain from the `notes` cell alone; matches the operator's intuition that "the latest override is authoritative"; the override_history Streamlit session state remains the rich audit trail; the notes cell remains the lightweight at-a-glance signal.
- **(b) first-wins** — rejected because re-priced sub-quotes (a vendor sends a corrected PDF) would be silently ignored; the operator would have to manually undo the first override before the second could take effect.
- **(c) append-chain (every tag concatenated)** — rejected because the notes cell would grow unboundedly across re-applies; the cell would quickly exceed the column width and lose the at-a-glance signal that T6.4.c is specifically trying to deliver.

**Files modified:** 5.
- `core/pricing/batch_override.py` — +5 source-tag constants + 1 frozen-set + 1 regex constant; `format_batch_operator_note` default switched from inline literal to constant reference (semantically identical); 1 new helper (`_rewrite_notes_with_tag_first`); `apply_batch_plan` gains keyword-only `source_tag` parameter + two post-`apply_manual_override` rewrites (one in the MATCHED loop, one in the AMBIGUOUS-resolved loop).
- `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` — +new imports (`SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR`, `apply_batch_plan`, `BatchOverridePlan`, plus `core.schemas.Estimate` for the type hint); +1 new public function (`apply_subquote_plan`).
- `tests/test_subquote_t8_1_integration.py` and `tests/test_subquote_t8_2_integration.py` — the sister `test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged` / `test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged_from_t82` pins both updated to reflect the new T6.4.c `apply_batch_plan` contract (the trailing keyword-only `source_tag` parameter with the `SOURCE_TAG_BATCH` default). The pre-T6.4.c assertion that "no kwargs are added" is intentionally relaxed; the new pin asserts the original five parameters stay in the original order with their original defaults and `source_tag` is the trailing addition.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — strikethrough on the T6.4 next-slice mention in T9.2 + T9.3's "Suggested next slices"; this section.

**Files created:** 2.
- `tests/test_subquote_tag_propagation.py` — 25 tests across constants (3) + `_rewrite_notes_with_tag_first` (4) + `apply_batch_plan` source-tag propagation (9) + re-apply / idempotency (3) + `apply_subquote_plan` wrapper (3) + production-code-uses-constants (1) + manual-override interplay (1) + T6.3 byte-compat (1).
- `tests/test_exporter_notes_visibility.py` — 5 tests across header location (1) + cell-value round-trip (1) + tag-at-start across all three sources (1) + column-width adequacy (1) + multi-line consistency (1).

**Test deltas:** 2 pre-existing tests updated — the two sister signature pins `test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged` (in `tests/test_subquote_t8_1_integration.py`) and `test_t63_backend_invoked_unchanged_from_t82` (in `tests/test_subquote_t8_2_integration.py`). Both pinned that `apply_batch_plan`'s signature was exactly `[estimate, plan, auto_apply_matched, resolved_ambiguous, skip_rows]` — the intentional guard against drift, and T6.4.c is the intentional drift. Updated to assert the original five parameters keep their order + defaults and `source_tag` is the trailing keyword-only addition. All other pre-existing tests remain byte-identically green. Suite: 2394 passed (post-T9.3) → 2424 passed (+30 new from the two new files).

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty `prior_notes` → no leading whitespace, no `| previous:` suffix. Pinned by `test_rewrite_notes_empty_prior_no_leading_whitespace`.
- Non-empty `prior_notes` → tag at start + payload + `| previous: <prior>`. Pinned by `test_rewrite_notes_with_prior_appends_previous_suffix`.
- Re-applying the same plan twice → idempotent (no duplicate tags). Pinned by `test_reapply_idempotent_same_plan_no_duplicate_tags` + the helper-level `test_rewrite_notes_idempotent_*` cases.
- Re-applying a DIFFERENT source on the same line → most-recent-wins; prior tag preserved in the suffix. Pinned by `test_reapply_subquote_then_llm_tag_swaps_at_front` and `test_reapply_vendor_csv_after_subquote_swaps_tag`.
- AMBIGUOUS resolved via `resolved_ambiguous` → also gets the tag (separate code path through the AMBIGUOUS branch). Pinned by `test_apply_batch_plan_ambiguous_resolved_carries_source_tag`.
- Pre-T6.4.c positional call (no `source_tag`) → still works; defaults to `SOURCE_TAG_BATCH`. Pinned by `test_apply_batch_plan_default_signature_byte_compat`.
- Notes-payload not starting with `source_tag + " "` (defensive — would never happen in practice from `format_batch_operator_note`) → helper falls back to using the payload as-is rather than crashing.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- ~~**`app.py` wire-up.** The two existing `apply_batch_plan(estimate, sq_plan, auto_apply_matched=True, ...)` call sites in `app.py`'s sub-quote section don't yet pass `source_tag` — backend is ready but the user-visible behaviour will only flip once a follow-up `app.py` PR replaces those calls with `apply_subquote_plan(estimate, sq_plan, llm=(st.session_state.get("subquote_source") == "llm"))`. One-line change at each site; deferred to a follow-up PR.~~ **SHIPPED as T6.4.c.1 — see block below.** T6.4.c is now operator-visible end-to-end: the canonical `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` / `[vendor-csv]` tag reaches every overridden line's `CostLine.notes` field at position 0 across all three ingestion paths.
- **Manual-override tag stamping.** `apply_manual_override` is the T6.1 single-line primitive; a manual override after a batch apply preserves the batch tag inside the prior-notes string but does not stamp `[manual-override]` at position 0. A future helper `format_manual_override_note` would close this if the calibration set demands it.
- **Notes column width on very long descriptions.** `_autosize`'s `max_width=60` clamps the Notes column at 60 chars — adequate for the tag + sentinel + a couple of bracketed fields, but a 200-char note with a long vendor name + quote ref + verbose row notes will get clipped on read in Excel (the cell value still round-trips; only the visible width is clamped). A future enhancement could bump the Notes column to a per-column override of `max_width=100` specifically for the Line Items sheet.

**Suggested next slices:**
- **Phase T6.4.a — Multi-sheet Excel ingestion.** Replace the single-CSV uploader with an `.xlsx` upload that walks every sheet, treating each sheet as a separate vendor / discipline. Same `BatchOverrideRow` shape per sheet; the matcher / applier backend is unchanged. Pairs naturally with T6.4.c — multi-sheet uploads typically come from different vendors and benefit from the per-sheet source tag.
- **Phase T6.4.b — Unit-aware matching.** Currently `match_cost_lines` matches purely on description text; a future slice would multiply the similarity by a unit-compatibility factor (1.0 for matching units, 0.5 for compatible but different, 0.0 for incompatible). Would catch the LF×TON-style failure mode the seed DB suppression already handles for cost lookups.
- **Phase T6.4.d — Per-line undo.** Track the pre-override snapshot per line (not just globally as T6.2 does today) so an operator can revert a single line without losing every other override. Pure schema + UI; the backend already returns a new Estimate per override so the undo stack is essentially free.
- **Phase T6.4.e — Markup knob.** Vendor sub-quotes typically need a +10-20% subcontractor markup. The current flow takes the vendor `unit_cost` verbatim. A `markup_pct` parameter on `apply_batch_plan` (and an optional `markup` CSV column) would handle this. Pairs naturally with T9.1's tally panel and T9.2's tally table since all three surfaces compute the same compounded grand total.
- **Phase T10 — Calibration v4.** First real-bid-set run with T6.4.c surfacing source tags in the deliverable PDF + Excel; validates that operators can attribute every priced-line override to its provenance at a glance.

---

### Phase T6.4.c.1 — `app.py` activation of the T6.4.c source-tag wire-up

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit activates the `apply_subquote_plan` wrapper and the explicit `source_tag=SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV` kwarg at the three Streamlit "Apply" call sites in `app.py`. T6.4.c had already shipped the pure-backend plumbing (constants + keyword-only `source_tag` on `apply_batch_plan` + `_rewrite_notes_with_tag_first` helper + the `apply_subquote_plan(estimate, plan, *, llm=...)` wrapper); this slice is the operator-facing flip that closes the T6.4.c family loop. **`app.py`-only slice** — zero modifications to `core/pricing/batch_override.py` (Worker SS's T6.4.b territory), `core/pricing/subquote_parser.py` (backend frozen post-T6.4.c), `core/schemas.py`, `core/estimator.py`, `core/exporter.py`, or `core/exporter_pdf.py`. Suite: 2424 → 2442 passed, 1 skipped (+18 new tests in one new file).

**Audit result — override_history double-stamping:** investigated and **NOT** a regression. Post-T6.4.c.1, the canonical source tag appears in two complementary fields, each carrying the tag exactly once (verified by `test_tag_appears_exactly_once_in_costline_notes` + `test_history_operator_note_and_costline_notes_carry_same_tag`):

1. `CostLine.notes` — the persisted, exporter-visible audit trail on the line itself. Written by `apply_batch_plan` → `_rewrite_notes_with_tag_first` in the format `"[<tag>] operator override: <payload-without-leading-tag> [ | previous: <prior-notes> ]"`.
2. `st.session_state["override_history"][i]["operator_note"]` — the in-session, UI-history-table audit trail. Written by the UI's separate `format_batch_operator_note(result.row, source_tag=...)` call in the format `"[<tag>] [vendor: ...] [csv-row: N] <notes-from-row>"`.

The two strings are NOT byte-identical (the notes cell carries the `operator override:` sentinel + optional previous-notes suffix that the history-row operator_note doesn't have), but they both start with the same canonical tag and share it once each. The pre-T6.4.c.1 history-log code already emitted the right tag for the sub-quote section; the T6.4.c.1 change there is a no-op style refinement (the inline ternary `"[sub-quote-llm]" if subquote_source == "llm" else "[sub-quote]"` is replaced by `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM if sq_is_llm else SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR` so the constants are the single source of truth across both the backend `apply` argument and the UI history-row format). The vendor-CSV path's history-log note is updated symmetrically — previously it called `format_batch_operator_note(result.row)` (defaulting to `[batch]`) which would have left the operator-history log on `[batch]` even after the backend tag flipped to `[vendor-csv]`; now both surfaces agree on `[vendor-csv]`. No deduplication needed; the two fields serve distinct audit purposes and complementary tagging is the intended design.

**The three call-site changes (one-line before/after each):**

| Call site | Before (T6.4.c) | After (T6.4.c.1) |
|---|---|---|
| T6.3 Vendor CSV apply | `apply_batch_plan(estimate, plan, auto_apply_matched=True, resolved_ambiguous=resolved_map)` | `apply_batch_plan(estimate, plan, auto_apply_matched=True, resolved_ambiguous=resolved_map, source_tag=SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV)` |
| T6.3 Vendor CSV history note | `format_batch_operator_note(result.row)` | `format_batch_operator_note(result.row, source_tag=SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV)` |
| Sub-quote apply (T8.1 + T8.2 shared, branches on `subquote_source` session-state) | `apply_batch_plan(estimate, sq_plan, auto_apply_matched=True, resolved_ambiguous=sq_resolved_map)` | `apply_subquote_plan(estimate, sq_plan, llm=sq_is_llm, auto_apply_matched=True, resolved_ambiguous=sq_resolved_map)` (where `sq_is_llm = st.session_state.get("subquote_source") == "llm"`) |

Plus a 6-line refactor in the sub-quote section that pulls `sq_is_llm` out of the inline ternary so it's computed once and reused for both the `apply_subquote_plan(llm=...)` argument AND the `sq_source_tag` constant selection used by the history-row `format_batch_operator_note(...)` call — single source of truth across the two surfaces.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Imports widened.** `app.py` adds `apply_subquote_plan` to the `core.pricing.subquote_parser` import list and `SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM` to the `core.pricing.batch_override` import list. No other module-level changes.
- **Sub-quote section uses the wrapper, not the raw applier.** `apply_subquote_plan(estimate, sq_plan, llm=sq_is_llm, ...)` replaces the prior `apply_batch_plan(estimate, sq_plan, ...)` call. The wrapper internally picks the right tag (`SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM` when `llm=True`, `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR` when `llm=False`) and forwards every other kwarg unchanged.
- **Vendor-CSV section uses the explicit constant.** `apply_batch_plan(estimate, plan, ..., source_tag=SOURCE_TAG_VENDOR_CSV)` replaces the prior implicit `apply_batch_plan(estimate, plan, ...)` call. The default of `SOURCE_TAG_BATCH` is preserved by `apply_batch_plan`'s signature for byte-compat with any pre-T6.4.c.1 direct caller, but the UI no longer relies on the default — the canonical vendor-csv tag is passed explicitly.
- **History-row tag derived from the same flag.** The `sq_source_tag` used by the `format_batch_operator_note(result.row, source_tag=...)` call (which lands in `override_history[i]["operator_note"]`) now reads `SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_LLM if sq_is_llm else SOURCE_TAG_SUBQUOTE_TABULAR` — the same `sq_is_llm` boolean that drove the `apply_subquote_plan(llm=...)` argument. Single source of truth; a future rename of either constant touches one location.
- **No `core/*` changes.** Pure UI activation slice; the backend was already complete after T6.4.c.

**Files modified:** 2.
- `app.py` — imports widened (+4 names); three apply call-site updates (T6.3 vendor CSV applier + its history-row formatter, T8.1 + T8.2 shared sub-quote applier); inline string-literal ternary for the sub-quote source tag replaced with a constants-based ternary that reuses the `sq_is_llm` boolean.
- `docs/ROADMAP_TAKEOFF_AUTOMATION.md` — strike-through on T6.4.c's "Edge cases NOT handled" `app.py` wire-up bullet; this section.

**Files created:** 1.
- `tests/test_streamlit_subquote_apply_wireup.py` — 18 tests across import-surface pins (3) + source-level call-site shape pins (4) + backend round-trip across all three apply paths (4) + override-history-vs-CostLine-notes tag-consistency (3) + edge cases (empty plan, mixed-source guard) (2) + import / source-readability smoke (2).

**Test deltas:** 0 pre-existing tests modified. All 2424 pre-T6.4.c.1 tests remain byte-identically green. Suite: 2424 → 2442 passed, 1 skipped.

**Edge cases handled:**
- Empty sub-quote plan → no `CostLine.notes` mutation on any line. Pinned by `test_empty_plan_does_not_mutate_notes`.
- Re-apply same plan → idempotent; tag still appears exactly once. Pinned by `test_reapply_same_plan_preserves_single_tag`.
- Mixed-source-within-single-apply (defensive) → every applied row carries the SAME tag (the wrapper's contract). Pinned by `test_mixed_source_within_single_apply_uses_caller_tag`.
- Override_history operator_note and `CostLine.notes` agree on the leading tag but carry their distinct formats (sentinel + previous-suffix on notes; bracketed-fields-only on history). Pinned by `test_history_operator_note_and_costline_notes_carry_same_tag`.

**Edge cases NOT handled (recommended future work):**
- **Multi-batch UNDO across all three paths.** The T6.2 global "Undo last batch" affordance still works (it pops the most recent `override_history` entry and restores the prior estimate snapshot) but per-line undo across mixed `[vendor-csv]` / `[sub-quote]` / `[sub-quote-llm]` history rows is out of scope; T6.4.d covers that.
- **Manual override after batch apply.** Still preserves the batch tag inside the prior-notes string (inherited from T6.4.c). A future `format_manual_override_note` helper plus a UI affordance would stamp `[manual-override]` at position 0 if the calibration set demands it.

**Suggested next slices:**
- **Phase T6.4.b — Unit-aware matching.** Worker SS's in-flight slice. Multiplies `match_cost_lines` similarity by a unit-compatibility factor (1.0 matching, 0.5 compatible, 0.0 incompatible) so LF×TON-style failure modes the seed DB suppression already handles for cost lookups also catch in the override matcher.
- **Phase T6.4.e — Markup knob.** Vendor sub-quotes typically need a +10-20% subcontractor markup. Add a `markup_pct` parameter on `apply_batch_plan` (and an optional `markup` CSV column) so the vendor `unit_cost` isn't taken verbatim. Pairs naturally with T9.1's tally panel and T9.2's tally table since all three surfaces compute the same compounded grand total.
- **Phase T10 — Calibration v4.** First real-bid-set run with T6.4.c family fully operator-visible end-to-end; validates that operators can attribute every priced-line override to its provenance at a glance in the Excel "Line Items" Notes column + the client-PDF cost-breakdown table.

---

### Phase T2.9 — Plumbing fixture schedule extraction + synthesis + dedupe

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit landed the full plumbing fixture-schedule slice (extraction → schema → prepass wire-in → 2-or-3 synthesis fan-out → dedupe → reconcile wire-in) as the SEVENTH dispatcher on the door/window/finish/panel/lighting/HVAC scaffold and the FIFTH downstream consumer of the promoted `header_index_excluding` helper. **Closes the Division 22+23+26 typed-schedule trifecta entirely.** Plumbing fixtures are the last single-discipline schedule on the typical commercial bid set that wasn't deterministic-extracted — every Division 22 / 23 / 26 fixture and equipment line now has a typed-record pre-pass + synthesis + dedupe path.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Module layout.** `core/extraction/plumbing_schedule.py` (~750 LOC) mirrors `hvac_schedule.py` structure exactly: pure-function `detect_plumbing_schedule_page(page) → bool`, `extract_plumbing_schedule_from_page(page, idx) → PlumbingScheduleResult`, and `extract_plumbing_schedule(pdf_path, idx)` disk-path entry point. Internal dataclasses (`PlumbingFixtureRecord`, `PlumbingScheduleResult`) bridge to Pydantic models via `to_schema()`.
- **Header collisions resolved via `header_index_excluding` (FIFTH downstream consumer).** Plumbing schedules carry the following short-vs-long collisions:
  1. `D` / `DIA` (short) substring-collides with `DESCRIPTION` (long)
  2. `T` / `TEMP` (short) substring-collides with `TYPE` / `TAG` (long)
  3. `Q` (short) substring-collides with `QUANTITY` / `QTY` (long)
  4. `CW` / `HW` two-letter connection-size headers each must claim a distinct column

  The TWO-PASS strategy from T2.8 ports cleanly: pin every long-form column first (TAG → TYPE → DESCRIPTION → MFR → MODEL → MOUNTING → FLOW → CW → HW → WASTE → VENT → SIZE → QUANTITY → NOTES), then run every short-form lookup (`D` / `DIA` for description, `Q` for quantity) with the union of all long-form indices in the exclusion set. Seven regression tests pin the boundary: `test_header_collision_d_does_not_collide_with_description`, `test_header_collision_short_d_only`, `test_header_collision_dia_does_not_collide_with_description`, `test_header_collision_t_does_not_collide_with_type`, `test_header_collision_temp_distinct_from_type`, `test_header_collision_q_does_not_collide_with_quantity`, `test_header_collision_cw_hw_claim_distinct_columns`. **Fifth-downstream validation outcome: the helper is now load-bearing across five families (door / panel / lighting / HVAC / plumbing). The two-pass orchestration pattern is the canonical shape going forward.**
- **Cell-level parsers.** Flow rate (`1.28 GPF` / `0.5 GPM` / `1.5GPM` / `1.28` with header-fallback for the unit), quantity (`3` / `3 EA` / `0`), connection sizes (round-trip as original string — `"1/2\""` / `"1-1/2\""` / `"3/4\""` / `"4\""` preserved verbatim with `-` / `N/A` / `NONE` collapsing to `None`), ADA detection (free-text keyword sweep across description + notes — `ADA` / `ACCESSIBLE` / `BARRIER-FREE` / `WHEELCHAIR` / `HANDICAP` / `HC`), sensor detection (`SENSOR` / `MOTION` / `AUTOMATIC` / `TOUCHLESS` / `INFRARED` / `IR` / `HANDS-FREE`).
- **Fixture-type classification.** Tag prefix wins when present: `WC-*` → `WATER_CLOSET`, `LAV-*` → `LAVATORY`, `URN-*` / `UR-*` → `URINAL`, `SH-*` / `SHU-*` → `SHOWER`, `EWC-*` / `DF-*` → `EWC`, `MS-*` → `MOP_SINK`, `SK-*` → `SINK`, `WH-*` → `WATER_HEATER`, `HD-*` / `HB-*` → `HOSE_BIBB`, `FD-*` → `FLOOR_DRAIN`. When the tag is uninformative (`X-1`), the description is scanned for `WATER CLOSET` / `TOILET` / `LAVATORY` / `DRINKING FOUNTAIN` / `FLOOR DRAIN` etc. as a fallback. Default is `OTHER` (CSI `22 00 00` parent).
- **Synthesis fan-out (2-or-3 per fixture).** Each `PlumbingFixtureRecord` synthesises into:
  1. **Fixture row** — 1 EA at the family CSI (`22 41 13` WC + URN, `22 41 16` LAV, `22 41 23` shower, `22 47 13` EWC / drinking fountain, `22 41 19` mop sink + sink, `22 33 00` water heater, `22 11 23` hose bibb, `22 13 19` floor drain, `22 00 00` other). Quantity = `fixture.quantity` when the schedule published a QTY column (confidence **0.90** → AUTO_APPROVE); otherwise quantity = 1.0 (confidence **0.55** → routes to HAND_TAKEOFF queue).
  2. **MEP rough-in LS row** — 1 LS at `22 11 16` (Domestic Water Piping) for water-supply-dominant fixtures (LAV / SHOWER / EWC / SINK / MOP_SINK / WATER_HEATER / HOSE_BIBB / OTHER) OR `22 13 16` (Sanitary Waste & Vent Piping) for waste-dominant fixtures (WC / URINAL / FLOOR_DRAIN). Confidence **0.45** (PARAMETRIC tier on T7 banding, HAND_TAKEOFF on T6 banding). ALWAYS emitted.
  3. **Trim / installation hardware LS row** — 1 LS at the SAME fixture CSI section. Confidence **0.70** → OPERATOR_REVIEW. ONLY emitted when BOTH `manufacturer` AND `model_number` are populated — the trim package (faucets / stops / supplies / valves / drain assembly) is mfr-specific and only meaningfully priceable once we know the mfr-model combination.
- **CSI mapping rationale (rough-in split).** Water-supply-dominant fixtures (LAV / SHOWER / EWC / SINK / MOP_SINK / WATER_HEATER / HOSE_BIBB) route to `22 11 16` because the supply rough-in (hot/cold stops, supplies, connection to building domestic water) is the dominant first-cost contributor. Waste-dominant fixtures (WC / URINAL / FLOOR_DRAIN) route to `22 13 16` because the large-diameter (3" / 4") waste lateral + carrier assembly on WCs / urinals dwarfs the 1/2" supply, and FDs are waste-only by construction. WATER_HEATER and HOSE_BIBB carry no waste line, so `22 11 16` is the only correct choice. The split is encoded as a single `_PLUMB_WASTE_DOMINANT_TYPES` frozenset for future tuning.
- **CSI mapping rationale (HOSE_BIBB).** Hose bibbs / wall hydrants live at `22 11 23` (Facility Natural-Gas Piping → no; this is "Facility Water Distribution Pumps" in older MasterFormat catalogs and "Hydrants" in some BPC seed entries). Some catalogs file hose bibbs under `22 14 00` (Facility Storm Drainage) or `22 11 16` (Domestic Water Piping). Picked `22 11 23` to keep hose bibbs at a distinct section from the domestic-water-piping rough-in line they sit on top of — a future maintainer can lift to `22 11 16` if the operator's seed DB prefers a single bucket.
- **Trim-line conditional rationale.** Both `manufacturer` AND `model_number` must be populated. Rationale: trim packages are catalog-specific (American Standard 3461.001 ships with a different supply / stops set than Kohler K-2210; the price difference can be $50-150 per fixture). Without a mfr-model combo the synthesiser can't pick a representative trim SKU, so it skips the row rather than emitting a generic placeholder. Tradeoff: a schedule that publishes only the mfr (no model) loses the trim line; this is intentional — partial mfr data is too thin to price.
- **Dedupe scope.** `plumbing_dedupe.py` runs against CSI prefix `22` (all of Division 22) ONLY. HVAC (`23`), electrical (`26`), door (`08`), finish (`09`), and structural (`03`) rows are NEVER touched. Five cross-pollination guards (`test_dedupe_does_not_touch_division_26_electrical`, `test_dedupe_does_not_touch_division_23_hvac`, `test_dedupe_does_not_touch_division_08_doors`, plus the aggregate / unrelated-22 cases) pin the boundary.
- **Legacy-aggregate regex shapes.** Mirrors `hvac_dedupe._LEGACY_AGGREGATE_RE` shape: anchored on common rollup prefixes (`plumbing\s+(?:fixtures?|systems?)`, `fixtures?(?:\s+(?:and\s+trim|package))?`, `toilets?`, `water\s+closets?`, `wc(?:\s+\d+)?`, `lavator(?:y|ies)`, `lav(?:\s+...)?`, `urinals?`, `urn(?:\s+\d+)?`, `showers?`, `sh(?:\s+\d+)?`, `sinks?`, `kitchen\s+sinks?`, `mop\s+sinks?`, `service\s+sinks?`, `drinking\s+fountains?`, `water\s+coolers?`, `electric\s+water\s+coolers?`, `ewc(?:\s+\d+)?`, `water\s+heaters?`, `wh(?:\s+\d+)?`, `hose\s+bibbs?`, `hose\s+hydrants?`, `floor\s+drains?`, `fd(?:\s+\d+)?`, `domestic\s+water\s+(?:piping|system|distribution)`, `sanitary\s+(?:waste|drainage)`, `waste\s+(?:and|&)\s+vent`) with an optional `[\s,:\-].*?` tail. Description-match enabled (`match_family_by_description=True`) because LLM plumbing rows often land with an empty / generic `csi_section`.
- **"Plumbing fixture" description prefix (not bare "Fixture").** Lighting synthesis (T2.7) uses "Fixture <TAG> — ..." for its descriptions. Even though the CSI-prefix scoping in the dedupe modules prevents cross-discipline confusion in practice, the plumbing synthesiser uses "Plumbing fixture <TAG>" (and the dedupe's `_DESC_MARK_RE` matches the longer prefix) as belt-and-braces against any future refactor that might accidentally drop the CSI-prefix filter. Validates as `test_synthesize_description_prefix_is_plumbing_fixture`.
- **Schema overlap with prior workers.** Disjoint — `core/schemas.py` adds two new Pydantic models (`PlumbingFixtureRecord`, `PlumbingScheduleResult`) in the HVAC neighborhood, and the only edit to `DrawingPrepassResult` itself is the new optional `plumbing_schedule` field. No conflict with the T7 / T2.7 / T2.8 fields.
- **Wire-in.** `core/extraction/drawing_prepass.py:_maybe_extract_plumbing_schedule()` runs alongside the HVAC + lighting + panel detectors (NOT inside the door/window/finish precedence chain, since plumbing schedules typically live on P-series sheets the upstream detectors leave alone). The plumbing detector runs INDEPENDENTLY of the panel / lighting / HVAC detectors — they target different sheet families. `core/takeoff.py:reconcile()` collects `synthesized_plumbing_items` after `synthesized_hvac_items`, appends them to `all_takeoffs`, then calls `dedupe_plumbing_against_synthesis(...)` after `dedupe_hvac_against_synthesis(...)`. Two targeted additions; no refactor of the existing T1–T2.8 paths.  **Worker EE coordination:** the only edit to `takeoff_synthesis.py` is a new `synthesize_plumbing_takeoff_items` function at the END of the file in a clearly-labeled "Phase T2.9 — Plumbing" section; no existing function is touched.
- **Tests.** New tests across four files: `tests/test_plumbing_schedule_extraction.py` (covers all five keyword variants, header-heuristic disqualifiers against lighting / HVAC / door headers, every cell parser including the `MOUNTING` allow-listing, every single-letter / two-letter header collision scenario including the FIFTH-downstream validation of `header_index_excluding`, single + multi-fixture extraction across all ten fixture families, QTY vs. no-QTY routing, manufacturer-slash splitting, ADA + sensor detection, connection-size round-trip preservation, the `to_schema` Pydantic bridge, end-to-end through `prepass_drawing_pdf`), `tests/test_plumbing_takeoff_synthesis.py` (per-family fan-out shape — WC with QTY + mfr+model → 3 items, LAV without QTY → fixture conf=0.55, FD → 2 items, water heater no-trim when model missing — CSI mapping for every fixture type, waste-vs-supply rough-in routing, source-tag / role / sheet-id notes contract, and the `Plumbing fixture` description-prefix guard), `tests/test_plumbing_dedupe.py` (per-fixture-tag suppression, cross-pollination guards against electrical / HVAC / door rows, the empty-synthesis preserve-all contract, the synthesised-rows preserve contract), `tests/test_takeoff_t2_9_integration.py` (4 end-to-end tests through `prepass_drawing_page` + `reconcile()`, including a plumbing + HVAC + lighting + panel four-discipline-coexist test closing the Division 22+23+26 trifecta entirely, and the T6 banding contracts for the LS rough-in row → HAND_TAKEOFF and the QTY-present fixture row → AUTO_APPROVE).

**Known limitations of this slice:**
- **Rough-in LS quantity is always 1.0.** A single WC and a 100-WC stadium restroom both synthesise the same `1 LS @ 22 13 16 @ conf 0.45` row. Same shape as the T2.8 HVAC slice; a future enhancement could scale the rough-in LS quantity by the fixture count.
- **Trim line uses the same CSI section as the fixture.** A WC fixture row at `22 41 13` and its trim row also at `22 41 13` will sort adjacent in the priced output but won't roll up into one combined line. Acceptable for audit clarity; tuning to a separate `22 40 17` (Plumbing Fixture Trim, if your seed DB has it) is a one-line change.
- **No water-heater storage-tank carve-out.** Water heaters synthesise as a single EA row at `22 33 00`; commercial water heaters with separate storage tanks (the dominant restaurant / institutional pattern) should fan out into the heater + storage tank as two distinct rows. Deferred to a future Plumbing-T2.9.1 if the calibration set surfaces it.
- **No fuel-supply line for gas water heaters.** A gas-fired water heater implies a `22 11 13` Facility Natural-Gas Piping line; not synthesised here. Same shape as the HVAC slice's missing gas-line synthesis; would land naturally as a fourth `TakeoffItem` family when `description` contains `GAS` / `NATURAL GAS`.

**Most fragile parsing case observed:** The `MOUNTING`-not-disqualified path. Lighting fixtures also publish `MOUNTING` (RECESSED / SURFACE / WALL / PENDANT), so the plumbing `_looks_like_plumbing_header` had to NOT disqualify on `MOUNTING` (else it would reject every legitimate plumbing schedule with a mounting column). The disambiguation falls entirely on the positive-signal check (must have at least one of `GPF` / `GPM` / `CW` / `HW` / `WASTE` / `VENT` / `FLOW`) AND the disqualifier set (rejecting `WATTS` / `LUMENS` / `LAMP` / `BALLAST` / `DRIVER`). If a future combined-discipline schedule appears with both plumbing AND lighting columns on the same table, this disambiguation will get tested. The current test corpus pins the negative (`test_detect_plumbing_schedule_negative_lighting_schedule` and `test_looks_like_plumbing_header_rejects_lighting_disqualifier`).

**Validation outcomes (per brief return-list):**
- **`header_index_excluding` collisions fired in test corpus (FIFTH-use validation).** Yes — `D` / `DIA` / `DESCRIPTION`, `T` / `TEMP` / `TYPE` / `TAG`, `Q` / `QUANTITY`, `CW` / `HW` all fired (seven dedicated regression tests). The TWO-PASS orchestration from T2.8 ported cleanly; no new pattern needed.
- **CSI mapping decisions.** Ten family mappings + the OTHER fallback; one ambiguity (HOSE_BIBB → `22 11 23` vs. `22 11 16`; defaulted to `22 11 23` to keep hose bibbs distinct from the domestic-water rough-in line). All eleven mappings tested.
- **Trim-line conditional (mfr+model both required).** This is intentionally restrictive — partial mfr data is too thin to price a trim package. Calibration-set evidence supports the gate. Schedules that publish mfr but not model lose the trim line; if real bid sets routinely publish mfr-only this gate may need to relax to mfr-only with a different (lower) confidence.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T2.10 — Specialty schedules.** Kitchen equipment (`11 40 13`), laboratory casework (`12 35 53`), AV / low-voltage (`27 41 16`), security (`28 ...`). Same dispatcher shape; each family is smaller in dollar value than the T2.6-T2.9 stack but covers the long tail of typed-record opportunities.~~ **KITCHEN + LAB + AV + SECURITY ALL SHIPPED** — Kitchen + Lab in Phase T2.10 section below; AV (Div 27) + Security (Div 28) in Phase T2.11 section below.  T2.x typed-extraction family is now closed entirely (9 typed schedule families across 6 MasterFormat Divisions — see T2.11 closure stats below).
- **Phase T6.1 — Confidence-propagation cleanup.** The `confidence` field is now set by every T1–T2.9 extractor + synthesiser, but the `_derive_takeoffs` legacy LLM path still emits `0.7` by default. A consistency pass to map LLM-row confidences from their underlying `extraction_confidence` (when available) into the `TakeoffItem.confidence` field would tighten the HAND queue further. Worker EE in-flight at the time of this commit.
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote integration.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup for plumbing fixtures ("see attached lavatory schedule from Ferguson"); pricing these against a vendor quote PDF instead of the CWICR catalog would replace the synthesised parametric EA price with the real sub-quote price + markup. Natural complement to T2.6 / T2.7 / T2.8 / T2.9.

---

### Phase T2.10 — Kitchen + lab specialty-schedule extraction + synthesis + dedupe

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit landed the kitchen-equipment-schedule + lab-casework-schedule slices (extraction → schema → prepass wire-in → 1-to-3 synthesis fan-out → dedupe → reconcile wire-in) as the EIGHTH and NINTH dispatchers on the door/window/finish/panel/lighting/HVAC/plumbing scaffold and the SIXTH + SEVENTH downstream consumers of the promoted `header_index_excluding` helper.  **AV (Division 27) + Security (Division 28) extractors are DEFERRED to Phase T2.11** — the four Pydantic record / result pairs (`AVDeviceRecord` / `AVScheduleResult` / `SecurityDeviceRecord` / `SecurityScheduleResult`) already live in `core/schemas.py` from the T2.10 scaffold commit `d7a28c1`, but the extractor / synthesis / dedupe paths are not yet wired.  Suite: 1621 → 1747 (+126 new tests across four files; 1 skipped unchanged).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Header-helper audit decision: KEPT local helpers.** Both `core/extraction/kitchen_schedule.py:_header_index` and `core/extraction/lab_casework_schedule.py:_header_index` survive unchanged from the T2.10 scaffold commit `d7a28c1`.  Both helpers are used ONLY for the initial unrestricted ``tag`` / ``mark`` lookup; every collision-prone subsequent lookup (``H`` / ``HEIGHT``, ``W`` / ``WIDTH``, ``B`` / ``BTU``, ``T`` / ``TYPE``, ``Q`` / ``QTY``, etc.) routes through the shared `header_index_excluding` via the same TWO-PASS picker that T2.8 (HVAC) and T2.9 (plumbing) ship.  The local helper has no exclusion semantics, but it can't misfire on collisions in practice because every short-form header is excluded BEFORE the local helper would be reached.  Six header-collision regression tests in `tests/test_kitchen_schedule.py` pin the boundary (``H`` / ``HEIGHT``, ``W`` / ``WIDTH``, ``B`` / ``BTU``, ``Q`` / ``QTY``, short-form-only fallback, no-long-form fallback).
- **Kitchen CSI mapping decisions.** Six families: RANGE/GRIDDLE/FRYER/OVEN → `11 40 13.13` (Food Cooking Equipment); REFRIGERATOR/FREEZER/WALK_IN/ICE_MACHINE → `11 40 16.13` (Food Refrigeration Equipment); DISHWASHER → `11 40 19.13` (Food Dishwashing Equipment); MIXER/PREP_TABLE/SINK → `11 40 13` (generic Food Service Equipment); HOOD/EXHAUST_FAN → `11 40 13.16` (Food Service Hoods, equipment itself); OTHER → `11 40 00` (generic Foodservice Equipment).  **Kitchen HOOD split-CSI rationale.** The hood EQUIPMENT itself routes to `11 40 13.16` per the spec convention that Division 11 (foodservice) wins on the equipment line — the hood is shipped, installed, and warrantied by the foodservice subcontractor.  The hood ROUGH-IN (ductwork) routes to `23 31 13` (Kitchen Hood Exhaust Ductwork Rough-In) under Division 23 because the duct, fan motor, and gravity / fire-damper assembly are the HVAC subcontractor's scope and the ductwork cost dominates.  This split-CSI pattern is the kitchen-side analog to the T2.8 HVAC equipment + 26 28 disconnect split (equipment in one Division, MEP rough-in in another).
- **Lab CSI mapping decisions.** Seven families: BASE_CABINET / WALL_CABINET / TALL_CABINET / LAB_BENCH → `12 35 53.13` (Laboratory Bench Casework); FUME_HOOD → `11 53 13` (Lab Fume Hoods); SAFETY_CABINET → `11 53 43` (Lab Safety Equipment); EYEWASH_STATION → `22 45 19` (Eyewash Equipment, cross-Division to plumbing); OTHER → `12 35 53` (generic Lab Casework).  **Lab EYEWASH cross-Division rationale.** Eyewashes appear on lab casework schedules because the architect groups them with the rest of the lab fit-out, but they are plumbing scope (potable water inlet, tempered-water mixing valve, optional floor drain).  Routing the eyewash row to `22 45 19` ensures the cost lands in the plumber's bid package rather than the casework installer's.  This is the only cross-Division mapping in the T2.10 slice; the eyewash row is also explicitly excluded from the lab dedupe scope (the lab dedupe regex scope is `12 35` + `11 53`, never `22 ...`), so the synthesised eyewash row is preserved by the source-tag check and the upstream plumbing dedupe owns whether to suppress any LLM rows under Division 22.
- **MEP rough-in dominant-utility rules.** Per-equipment-record rough-in is synthesised ONLY when at least one utility flag fires.  Kitchen: HOOD/EXHAUST_FAN → `23 31 13` (ductwork wins for hoods regardless of other flags); any piped utility (gas / water / drain) → `22 11 16` (water-side rough-in catches gas piping too, keeping the rough-in row count per record to one — vs. fanning out a separate gas-piping row that would double-bill on combined gas+water equipment); electric-only → `26 27 26` (equipment wiring); no flags → no rough-in row.  Lab: any piped utility (gas / vacuum / water) → `22 11 16` (water-side catches gas + vacuum too); electric-only → `26 27 26`; no flags → no rough-in row.  Both dominance rules are encoded in dedicated helper functions (`_kitchen_roughin_csi`, `_lab_roughin_csi`) so the rule precedence is greppable.
- **Trim-line conditional.** Per the brief, the LS trim / installation-hardware row is synthesised ONLY when BOTH `manufacturer` AND `model_number` are populated on the record.  Two type-level exclusions apply on the lab side: FUME_HOOD (factory-supplied hoods ship with integrated trim — sash, light, service fittings, cup sinks, baffles — so a separate trim line would double-count) and EYEWASH_STATION (the eyewash IS the trim — there's no separate finish carpentry layer).  Both exclusions live in `_LAB_TRIM_EXCLUDED: frozenset[str]` as a single source of truth.  Kitchen side has no type-level exclusions currently (`_KITCHEN_TRIM_EXCLUDED = frozenset()`), held as an explicit constant so a future maintainer can add WALK_IN or other exclusions without touching the main loop.
- **Confidence inheritance — T6.1 hard requirement.** Every derived row (rough-in + trim) uses `inherit_with_haircut(parent_confidence)` from T6.1; NO hard-coded 0.8 / 0.85 derived confidence anywhere in the kitchen or lab synthesis.  Trim rows additionally apply the specialty-trim multiplier `0.70` (matches plumbing trim banding from T2.9) via `inherit_with_haircut(parent, multiplier=0.95 * 0.70)`.  Verified by two dedicated tests per family (`test_roughin_inherits_haircut_from_parent_confidence`, `test_trim_inherits_double_haircut_from_parent_confidence`).
- **Dedupe-regex breadth audit (Worker DD plumbing bug guard).**  Both kitchen and lab dedupe regexes require EITHER an unambiguous schedule-section prefix (`kitchen equipment` / `food service` / `foodservice` / `commercial kitchen` for kitchen; `lab` / `laboratory` + casework/furniture/equipment for lab) OR an explicit digit-suffixed tag (`K-\d+`, `RA-\d+`, `WI-\d+`, `BC-\d+`, `FH-\d+`, `EW-\d+`, etc.).  Bare common words (`fixtures?`, `casework`, `millwork`, `hood`, `sinks?`) are NEVER in the alternation.  Specifically guarded:
  - **Kitchen sink vs plumbing lavatory.** Kitchen `SK-\d+` is in the regex, but the CSI prefix scope (`11 40`) keeps a plumbing fixture row (CSI `22 41 16` lavatory) entirely outside the kitchen dedupe scope.  Pinned by `test_dedupe_preserves_plumbing_fixture_rows` and the integration `test_kitchen_and_plumbing_schedules_do_not_cross_suppress`.
  - **WC-1 lab wall cabinet vs WC-1 plumbing water closet.** The bare per-mark `wc-\d+` form is INTENTIONALLY EXCLUDED from the lab regex alternation (a WC-1 plumbing row would otherwise misfire).  Wall-cabinet coverage relies on the description-mark fallback `"Lab casework WC-N — ..."` only.  Pinned by `test_dedupe_preserves_plumbing_water_closet_marked_wc`.
  - **Generic Div 6 millwork.** The lab regex never matches a bare `millwork` or `casework` token — both require an explicit `lab` / `laboratory` qualifier (`lab(?:oratory)?\s+casework`).  Pinned by `test_dedupe_preserves_general_div_6_millwork`.
  - **HVAC ductwork.** The kitchen regex never matches a bare `hood` token — only `HOOD-\d+` or the phrases `kitchen hood` / `exhaust hood`.  HVAC dedupe owns the `23 31 13` rough-in row that the kitchen synthesis emits cross-Division.
- **Wire-in.** `core/extraction/drawing_prepass.py` gains `_maybe_extract_kitchen_schedule()` + `_maybe_extract_lab_schedule()` orchestrated AFTER `_maybe_extract_plumbing_schedule()` in both `prepass_drawing_page` and `prepass_drawing_pdf`, plus two new dataclass fields (`kitchen_schedule`, `lab_schedule`) and two new `to_schema` bridge entries.  Same disjoint-detector posture as panels / lighting / HVAC / plumbing — kitchen + lab schedules live on K-series / I-series / lab-plan sheets that the door / window / finish / room precedence chain never claims.  `core/takeoff.py:reconcile()` collects `synthesized_kitchen_items` + `synthesized_lab_items` after `synthesized_plumbing_items`, appends them to `all_takeoffs`, then runs `dedupe_kitchen_against_synthesis(...)` + `dedupe_lab_against_synthesis(...)` after `dedupe_plumbing_against_synthesis(...)`.  Pure additions; no refactor of existing T1–T2.9 paths.  **No edits to `core/schemas.py`** — the four T2.10 record / result pairs were already shipped by the scaffold commit `d7a28c1`.
- **AV + Security explicitly NOT touched.** `AVDeviceRecord` / `AVScheduleResult` / `SecurityDeviceRecord` / `SecurityScheduleResult` exist on `core/schemas.py` from the scaffold commit but no extractor / synthesis / dedupe / wire-in for either family in this commit.  `DrawingPrepassResult.av_schedule` / `.security_schedule` Pydantic fields likewise exist but stay `None` until T2.11 ships.

**Tests added (126 across four files):**
- `tests/test_kitchen_schedule.py` (50 tests) — page detection (4 phrase variants + 2 negatives), full item-type classifier coverage (RA/FRY/OV/REF/FZ/WI/IM/DW/HD/EF/SK/K + description fallback), cell parsers (BTU plain/comma/K-shorthand/garbage, quantity, inches, size triple with + without height, voltage 120V/208V/480V/blank, utility flag tri-state, utility text scan), header heuristic (positive + 2 negatives), header collision audit (4 collision pin tests + short-form fallback), end-to-end extraction (single record / multi record / QTY column / voltage→electric / BTU→gas / notes→utility), `to_schema` round-trip.
- `tests/test_kitchen_takeoff_synthesis_dedupe.py` (28 tests) — synthesis shape (empty / RANGE 3-row / REFRIGERATOR 2-row / WALK_IN water-dominant / HOOD ductwork rough-in / DISHWASHER CSI / SINK CSI / OTHER fallback / blank-tag skip / no-utility skip rough-in), confidence inheritance via `inherit_with_haircut` (rough-in haircut + trim double haircut + no-QTY HAND_TAKEOFF + QTY AUTO_APPROVE), trim conditional (mfr missing / model missing / both present), source-tag wiring (notes prefix + description prefix + sheet_id threading), dedupe (kitchen-equipment aggregate suppression + per-mark suppression + plumbing-row preservation + lighting-row preservation + door-row preservation + no-op when no synth + unrelated-kitchen-row preservation + walk-in-cooler aggregate suppression).
- `tests/test_lab_schedule_synthesis_dedupe.py` (43 tests) — page detection (3 phrase variants + plumbing rejection), classifier (BC/WC/TC/FH/LB/SC/EW + description fallback), cell parsers, multi-record extraction, `to_schema` round-trip, synthesis (empty / base cabinet / wall cabinet / lab bench electrical / FUME_HOOD with NO trim line / safety cabinet / EYEWASH cross-Division 22 with NO trim / OTHER fallback), confidence inheritance, dedupe (lab-casework aggregate + fume-hood aggregate + per-mark + Div 6 millwork preservation + plumbing-WC preservation + eyewash Div 22 preservation + no-op safety + door/panel/lighting preservation + kitchen-row preservation).
- `tests/test_takeoff_t2_10_integration.py` (5 tests) — end-to-end kitchen+lab PDF through prepass + reconcile, kitchen+plumbing no-cross-suppress (the kitchen-sink-vs-lavatory case), T6.1 rough-in HAND_TAKEOFF banding, T7 PARAMETRIC tier math, empty schedule safety.

**Validation outcomes (per brief return-list):**
- **Header-helper audit:** LOCAL helpers KEPT; both extractors already route every collision-prone lookup through `header_index_excluding` via the two-pass picker, and the local helper is only used for the initial unrestricted tag/mark lookup (which has no collisions to resolve).  Documented in this section + in module docstrings on both `kitchen_schedule.py` and `lab_casework_schedule.py` (scaffold commit).
- **CSI mapping decisions:** Kitchen HOOD split-CSI rationale documented above (equipment in Div 11, rough-in in Div 23).  Lab EYEWASH cross-Division rationale documented above (`22 45 19` plumbing, not Div 11/12 lab).
- **Dedupe-regex breadth audit:** Confirmed conservative — no bare `fixtures?` / `casework` / `millwork` / `hood` / `sinks?` tokens; every alternative requires either an explicit schedule-section qualifier or a digit-suffixed tag form.
- **Confidence inheritance:** `inherit_with_haircut` from T6.1 used for every derived row (no hard-coded 0.8 / 0.85).  Trim rows apply `0.95 × 0.70` multiplier.
- **Trim conditional:** mfr+model both required; FUME_HOOD + EYEWASH_STATION exempt on lab side.
- **AV + Security:** explicitly NOT touched in this commit.

**Suggested next slices:**
- ~~**Phase T2.11 — AV + Security specialty schedules.** Last two T2.x specialty families: AV / low-voltage (`27 41 16`) and security (`28 13 16` access control, `28 16 33` intrusion detection, `28 23 16` video surveillance).  Scaffold schemas already in place from `d7a28c1`; same dispatcher shape as T2.10.  Natural continuation.~~ **SHIPPED** — see Phase T2.11 section below.
- **Phase T6.3 — Batch override from CSV.** The Streamlit T6.2 single-row override UI could ingest a CSV of `(takeoff_id, unit_cost, vendor, quote_ref)` rows to bulk-override a sub-quoted package (e.g. all kitchen equipment from one vendor's quote).  Pairs naturally with the T2.10 typed-record output — every kitchen / lab synthesis row carries a stable identity that CSV-keyed override can target.
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote PDF ingestion.** Real bid sets carry sub-quote markup ("see attached lavatory schedule from Ferguson", "kitchen equipment per ITW Food Equipment quote") — a vendor-quote-PDF ingestor that extracts unit prices and applies them as per-row MANUAL_OVERRIDE values would replace the synthesised parametric EA price with the real sub-quote price + markup.  Highest dollar-impact next slice for any project that bids out specialty work.

---

### Phase T2.11 — AV + Security specialty-schedule extraction + synthesis + dedupe

**Status:** SHIPPED — closes the **T2.x typed-extraction family entirely**.  This commit landed the AV-equipment-schedule (Division 27 Communications) + security-schedule (Division 28 Electronic Safety & Security) slices (extraction → schema → prepass wire-in → 1-to-3 synthesis fan-out → dedupe → reconcile wire-in) as the TENTH and ELEVENTH dispatchers on the door/window/finish/panel/lighting/HVAC/plumbing/kitchen/lab scaffold and the EIGHTH + NINTH downstream consumers of the promoted `header_index_excluding` helper.  Suite: 1747 → 1975 (+228 new tests across four files; 1 skipped unchanged).

**T2.x family closure stats:** **9 typed schedule families** (doors / windows / finishes & rooms / panels / lighting / HVAC / plumbing / kitchen / lab / AV / security — counting each T2.x slice's specialty families) across **6 MasterFormat Divisions** (08 doors+windows, 09 finishes, 22 plumbing, 23 HVAC, 26 panels+lighting, 11+12+22+23+26 cross-Division kitchen+lab rough-ins, 27 AV, 28 security).  Combined with the T1 door / T2.5 window / T2.6 panel / T2.7 lighting / T2.8 HVAC / T2.9 plumbing / T2.10 kitchen+lab work this represents the entire typed-extraction surface that the brief inventory ever called out.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **TWO-PASS header picker — eighth + ninth downstream uses.** Both `core/extraction/av_schedule.py:_av_indices` and `core/extraction/security_schedule.py:_security_indices` pin every long-form column first (`DESCRIPTION`, `MOUNTING`, `POWER`, `SIGNAL`, `CONNECTION`, `QUANTITY`, `NOTES`, …) with the union of prior long-form indices in the exclusion set, then run the short-form (`D`, `M`, `P`, `S`, `C`, `Q`, `W`) lookups with EVERY long-form excluded.  Collisions exercised in this commit: AV → `D` / `DISPLAY` / `DESCRIPTION` / `DEVICE`, `M` / `MIC` / `MODEL` / `MOUNTING` / `MARK`, `P` / `POWER` / `PROJECTOR`, `S` / `SIZE` / `SIGNAL` / `SPEAKER`, `W` / `WATTAGE`, `Q` / `QTY` / `QUANTITY`.  Security → `D` / `DOOR` / `DEVICE` / `DESCRIPTION`, `C` / `CAMERA` / `CARD` / `CONTACT` / `COM` / `CABLE` / `CONNECTION`, `M` / `MOTION` / `MODEL` / `MOUNTING` / `MARK`, `R` / `READER`, `P` / `POWER`, `Q` / `QTY` / `QUANTITY`.  All pinned by dedicated regression tests (`test_header_collision_*`).
- **AV CSI mapping decisions.** Nine families: DISPLAY → `27 41 16.51` (A-V Display Equipment); PROJECTOR → `27 41 16.31` (A-V Projection Equipment); CAMERA (AV / conferencing) → `27 41 16.49` (A-V Capture); MICROPHONE → `27 41 33.13` (Microphones); SPEAKER → `27 41 33.16` (Loudspeakers); RACK → `27 11 26` (Communications Racks); CONTROL_PROCESSOR → `27 41 19.13` (A-V Control); NETWORK_SWITCH → `27 21 33` (Data Communications Network Equipment); OTHER → `27 41 16` (generic Integrated AV).  Cabling rough-in routes to `27 15 13.13` (Communications Copper Backbone Cabling) and is emitted UNIVERSALLY (every AV device gets a cabling row).  Programming / commissioning labor routes to the SAME device CSI section and is gated to CONTROL_PROCESSOR / NETWORK_SWITCH OR any device with both `manufacturer` AND `model_number` populated.
- **NETWORK_SWITCH split-Division rationale.** A network switch on an AV/IT schedule routes to **Division 27** (`27 21 33` Data Communications Network Equipment), NOT Division 26 (electrical).  Rationale: the switch ships, is installed, programmed, and warrantied by the AV / IT integrator — it is procured and racked along with the rest of the audio-video / IT package, not the electrical subcontractor's panelboard / wiring scope.  Division 26 owns the *power* feeding the rack, but the active networking equipment itself belongs to Division 27.  This mirrors the kitchen HOOD split-CSI from T2.10 (equipment in one Division, MEP rough-in in another).
- **Security CSI mapping decisions.** Eight families: CARD_READER → `28 13 23.13` (Access Control Card Readers); CAMERA (security / surveillance) → `28 23 23` (Video Surveillance Cameras); MOTION_SENSOR → `28 16 13.13` (Passive Infrared Intrusion Detection); DOOR_CONTACT → `28 16 16.13` (Door Position Switches); KEYPAD → `28 13 23.16` (Access Control Keypads); REQUEST_TO_EXIT → `28 13 33.13` (Request-to-Exit Devices); MAGLOCK → `28 13 43.13` (Electromagnetic Locks); OTHER → `28 13 00` (generic Access Control).  Cabling rough-in routes to `28 05 13` (Conductors and Cables for Electronic Safety and Security) and is emitted for CARD_READER / CAMERA / MOTION_SENSOR / KEYPAD / REQUEST_TO_EXIT / MAGLOCK — **DOOR_CONTACT is excluded** because its wiring lives inside the door frame (no separate cabling pull).  Programming / commissioning labor routes to the SAME device CSI section and is gated to CARD_READER / MAGLOCK OR any device with both `manufacturer` AND `model_number` populated.
- **MAGLOCK Div-28-not-Div-8 rationale.** Maglocks are physically door hardware (they bolt to the door / frame) but route to **Division 28** (`28 13 43.13` Electromagnetic Locks), NOT Division 8 (architectural door hardware).  Rationale: a maglock is electrically energised, integrated into the access-control system, and procured + installed + programmed by the security / access-control subcontractor — the access-control panel must be programmed to release the maglock on REX, fire alarm, or credential events.  Phase T1's Division 8 door hardware dedupe never touches Division 28 rows (CSI prefix scopes are disjoint), so a synthesised maglock at `28 13 43.13` and a Phase T1 door hardware set at `08 71 00` coexist without cross-suppression even when the maglock and the door share the same opening.
- **CAM- cross-domain disambiguation strategy.** Both AV and Security schedules use the same `CAM-N` tag prefix.  Three-layer mitigation:
  1. **Schedule-level detection.** `detect_av_schedule_page` requires an AV-distinctive header token (DISPLAY / PROJECTOR / RESOLUTION / SIGNAL / SIZE / HDMI / SDI / SPEAKER / MICROPHONE / WATTAGE — MOUNTING and POWER alone are shared and DO NOT qualify) AND rejects any header carrying security-distinctive tokens (CONNECTION / CONTACT / READER / CARD / WIEGAND / SURVEILLANCE / CCTV).  `detect_security_schedule_page` mirrors this with security-distinctive tokens.  A CAM-1 row in an AV-headered schedule lands in AV synthesis; the same tag in a security-headered schedule lands in security synthesis.
  2. **Description-level disambiguation.** `_classify_item_type` in both extractors checks for opposing-domain keywords in the description: AV side REJECTS `CAM-N` to `OTHER` when the description carries SURVEILLANCE / CCTV / PTZ; Security side REJECTS to `OTHER` when the description carries CONFERENCE / LECTURE / WEBCAM / HUDDLE / VIDEO CONFERENCING / TELEPRESENCE / CAPTURE.  This catches edge-case schedules that mix both domains.
  3. **Dedupe-level mutual exclusion.** Both `av_dedupe.py` and `security_dedupe.py` INTENTIONALLY EXCLUDE the bare `cam-\d+` form from the legacy-aggregate regex.  Per-mark CAM- coverage relies on the description-mark anchor: AV synthesis writes `"AV device CAM-N — ..."` matched by `^av\s+device\s+...`; Security synthesis writes `"Security device CAM-N — ..."` matched by `^security\s+device\s+...`.  These anchors are mutually exclusive so AV dedupe never catches a security camera row and vice-versa.

  Test coverage: AV side has `test_classify_camera_av_context` + `test_classify_camera_rejected_when_security_context`; Security side has `test_classify_camera_security_context` + `test_classify_camera_rejected_when_av_context`; cross-domain dedupe pinned by `test_dedupe_av_does_not_catch_security_camera_rows`, `test_dedupe_av_does_not_catch_bare_cam_llm_row`, `test_dedupe_security_does_not_catch_av_camera_rows`, `test_dedupe_security_does_not_catch_bare_cam_llm_row`; end-to-end disambiguation in `test_cam_in_av_schedule_routes_to_div_27` + `test_cam_in_security_schedule_routes_to_div_28`.
- **DOOR HARDWARE SCHEDULE guard (Phase T1 cross-talk).** The brief includes `"DOOR HARDWARE SCHEDULE"` in `_SECURITY_SCHEDULE_KEYWORDS` because some access-control schedules use that title (electrified hardware, electric strikes, maglock packages).  Without a guard this would mis-claim every Phase T1 architectural door hardware schedule.  `detect_security_schedule_page` ACCEPTS that phrase **only** when the page also carries a security-context token (`SECURITY` / `ACCESS` / `CARD` / `READER` / `ELECTRIFIED` / `MAGLOCK` / `ELECTRIC STRIKE` / `REX` / `REQUEST TO EXIT` / `CCTV` / `SURVEILLANCE` / `WIEGAND`).  A pure Phase T1 schedule whose only signal is the literal title falls through and stays in Division 8.  Pinned by `test_detect_rejects_phase_t1_door_hardware_schedule` + `test_detect_accepts_door_hardware_with_security_context`.
- **Conservative dedupe regex breadth audit.** Both regexes require EITHER an unambiguous schedule-section phrase (AV → `av\s+`, `a/v\s+`, `audio[-\s]?(visual|video)\s+`, `video conferencing`, `display`, `projector`, `lecture capture`; Security → `security\s+`, `access\s+control\s+`, `card\s+reader`, `prox(?:imity)?\s+reader`, `cctv\s+`, `video\s+surveillance`, `motion\s+(sensors?|detectors?)`, `door\s+contact`, `keypad`, `request[-\s]?to[-\s]?exit`, `electromagnetic\s+lock`, `mag(?:netic)?\s+lock`) OR an explicit digit-suffixed tag form.  Bare `cam-\d+` (cross-domain CAM- guard) and bare `sw-\d+` (electrical switchgear collision guard) are INTENTIONALLY EXCLUDED from AV.  Bare `cam-\d+` and bare `dr-\d+` (Phase T1 door mark collision guard) are INTENTIONALLY EXCLUDED from Security — the bare `dr-\d+` exclusion is critical because `match_family_by_description=True` would otherwise wrap a Phase T1 row described `"DR-1"` into the security family and the per-mark whole-token search would dedupe it.
- **Mutual-exclusion matrix (audited).**  AV dedupe never catches: doors (08, Phase T1), windows (08 41 / 08 50 / 08 51 / 08 52 / 08 53, T2.5), finishes (09, T2.x), panels (26 24, T2.6), lighting (26 51, T2.7), HVAC (23, T2.8), plumbing (22, T2.9), kitchen (11 40, T2.10), lab (12 35 + 11 53, T2.10), security (28, T2.11).  Security dedupe never catches: doors (08, including bare `DR-1` description anchor — see `test_dedupe_security_dr_n_mark_only_fires_inside_28_scope`), windows, finishes, panels, lighting, HVAC, plumbing, kitchen, lab, AV (27).  Both AV and Security dedupes coexist on a single project without cross-domain false positives: `test_all_four_specialty_domains_independent_streams` exercises kitchen + lab + AV + security on a single PDF and confirms each family's primary row survives the other three families' dedupe passes.
- **Confidence inheritance — T6.1 hard requirement.** Every derived row (cabling + programming) uses `inherit_with_haircut(parent_confidence)` from T6.1; NO hard-coded 0.8 / 0.85 derived confidence anywhere in the AV or security synthesis.  Cabling rows apply the universal haircut multiplier `0.95 × 0.95` (parametric haircut × cabling-specific multiplier).  Programming rows apply the specialty-trim multiplier `0.95 × 0.70` (matches plumbing trim banding from T2.9 and kitchen / lab trim banding from T2.10).  Verified by `test_synthesize_av_cabling_inherits_haircut_from_parent`, `test_synthesize_av_programming_inherits_double_haircut`, `test_synthesize_security_cabling_inherits_haircut_from_parent`, `test_synthesize_security_programming_inherits_double_haircut`.
- **Wire-in.** `core/extraction/drawing_prepass.py` gains `_maybe_extract_av_schedule()` + `_maybe_extract_security_schedule()` orchestrated AFTER `_maybe_extract_lab_schedule()` in both `prepass_drawing_page` and `prepass_drawing_pdf`, plus two new dataclass fields (`av_schedule`, `security_schedule`) and two new `to_schema` bridge entries.  `core/takeoff.py:reconcile()` collects `synthesized_av_items` + `synthesized_security_items` after `synthesized_lab_items`, appends them to `all_takeoffs`, then runs `dedupe_av_against_synthesis(...)` + `dedupe_security_against_synthesis(...)` after `dedupe_lab_against_synthesis(...)`.  Pure additions; no refactor of existing T1–T2.10 paths.  **No edits to `core/schemas.py`** — the four T2.11 record / result pairs were already shipped by the T2.10 scaffold commit `d7a28c1`.

**Tests added (228 across four files):**
- `tests/test_av_schedule.py` (53 tests) — page detection (4 phrase variants + 2 negatives — security + lighting), full item-type classifier coverage (DISP / DSP / PROJ / PJ / MIC / SPK / SP / RACK / EQR / CTRL / SW + CAM AV-context + CAM security-context rejection + unknown + description fallback), cell parsers (resolution 4K / 1080p / inches / bare-diagonal / dash-none, wattage with/without unit, power 120V / PoE / PoE+ / 12VDC / USB-C, signal HDMI / SDI / IP / USB / DisplayPort, quantity, mounting), header heuristic (positive + 2 negatives), TWO-PASS header collision pin tests (D-vs-DESCRIPTION, D-vs-DISPLAY-vs-DESCRIPTION, M-vs-MODEL-vs-MOUNTING, P-vs-POWER-vs-PROJECTOR, S-vs-SIGNAL-vs-SIZE, W-vs-WATTAGE, Q-vs-QUANTITY, short-form-only fallback), end-to-end extraction (single display / multi-device / control + switch / CAM AV-context / CAM rejected when security-context), `to_schema` round-trip, empty result safety.
- `tests/test_security_schedule.py` (53 tests) — page detection (5 phrase variants + AV / lighting / pure-Phase-T1-DOOR-HARDWARE rejections + electrified-hardware acceptance), classifier (DR / RDR / CR / CAM security + CAM AV rejection / MS / MOT / PIR / DC / KP / RTE / ML / MAG + description fallback), cell parsers (power PoE / 12VDC / 24VDC / Wiegand-power / dash-none, connection Cat6 / RS-485 / Wiegand, quantity, mounting), header heuristic (positive + door-hardware / AV / lighting rejection), TWO-PASS header collision pin tests, end-to-end extraction (single reader / multi-device / CAM security-context / CAM rejected when AV-context / QTY-aware / no-QTY-column), `to_schema` round-trip, empty result safety.
- `tests/test_av_security_synthesis_dedupe.py` (57 tests) — AV synthesis shape (empty / display 2-row / display 3-row with mfr+model / projector CSI / control processor always-3-rows / network switch always-3-rows-Div27 / microphone CSI / speaker CSI / rack CSI / camera CSI / OTHER fallback / blank-tag skip / no-QTY HAND_TAKEOFF / QTY AUTO_APPROVE), AV confidence inheritance (cabling haircut + programming double haircut), AV notes / description / sheet_id wiring; Security synthesis shape (empty / card reader 3-row / camera 2-row / camera 3-row with mfr+model / motion / door-contact-1-row-no-cabling / keypad CSI / RTE CSI / maglock 3-row-Div28 / OTHER fallback / blank-tag skip / QTY band / no-QTY band), Security confidence inheritance; AV dedupe (AV-equipment aggregate suppression + per-mark suppression + no-op safety + cross-domain CAM- safety + bare-CAM safety + door / panel / lighting / plumbing / kitchen / lab preservation); Security dedupe (security-equipment aggregate + per-mark + no-op safety + cross-domain CAM- safety + bare-CAM safety + Phase T1 door hardware preservation + panel / lighting / AV preservation + DR-1 Phase-T1 mark-only-fires-inside-28-scope).
- `tests/test_takeoff_t2_11_integration.py` (7 tests) — end-to-end AV+Security PDF through prepass + reconcile, all-four-domains (kitchen + lab + AV + security) independent streams, T6.1 AV cabling rough-in HAND_TAKEOFF banding, T7 PARAMETRIC tier math for security cabling, CAM- end-to-end disambiguation (AV schedule → Div 27 41 16.49 vs Security schedule → Div 28 23 23), empty schedule safety.

**Validation outcomes (per brief return-list):**
- **`header_index_excluding` eighth + ninth uses:** Both `av_schedule.py:_av_indices` and `security_schedule.py:_security_indices` use the TWO-PASS pattern.  AV collisions fired: `D`/`DISPLAY`/`DESCRIPTION`, `M`/`MODEL`/`MOUNTING`, `P`/`POWER`, `S`/`SIGNAL`/`SIZE`, `W`/`WATTAGE`, `Q`/`QUANTITY`.  Security collisions fired: `D`/`DESCRIPTION`/`DOOR`, `C`/`CONNECTION`/`CABLE`, `M`/`MODEL`/`MOUNTING`, `P`/`POWER`, `Q`/`QUANTITY`.
- **TWO-PASS pattern:** Used in both modules.
- **CSI mapping decisions:** Documented above — MAGLOCK → Div 28 (security electronics, not architectural); NETWORK_SWITCH (in AV schedule) → Div 27 (communications, not Div 26 electrical).
- **CAM disambiguation strategy:** Three-layer (schedule detection + description classifier + dedupe regex exclusion + mutually-exclusive description anchors).  Test coverage spans unit + integration.
- **Dedupe regex breadth audit:** AV regex requires AV-section phrase OR digit-suffixed AV tag (excludes bare `cam-\d+`, bare `sw-\d+`).  Security regex requires security-section phrase OR digit-suffixed security tag (excludes bare `cam-\d+`, bare `dr-\d+`).  Mutual exclusion confirmed by integration test + 10 cross-family preservation tests.
- **Confidence inheritance:** `inherit_with_haircut` from T6.1 used for every derived row.  Cabling: parent × 0.95 × 0.95.  Programming: parent × 0.95 × 0.70.
- **T2.x family closure stats:** 9 typed schedule families (doors / windows / finishes & rooms / panels / lighting / HVAC / plumbing / kitchen / lab / AV / security) across 6 MasterFormat Divisions (08, 09, 11+12, 22, 23, 26, 27, 28).

**Suggested next slices:**
- **Phase T8 — Sub-quote PDF ingestion.** **Highest dollar-leverage next slice.** Now that nine typed schedule families generate parametric per-row prices, the marginal accuracy improvement from replacing a synthesised parametric EA price with a real vendor sub-quote price + markup dominates the marginal value of any new typed-extraction family.  Real bid sets routinely carry per-package sub-quotes ("see attached lavatory schedule from Ferguson", "kitchen equipment per ITW Food Equipment quote", "AV per AVI-SPL quote") whose unit prices are 20-40% off-catalog.  A vendor-quote-PDF ingestor that extracts unit prices and applies them as per-row MANUAL_OVERRIDE values is the natural completion of the typed-extraction work.
- **Phase T9 — Alternates pricing.** Orthogonal feature: spec sections 01 23 00 (Alternates) list bid alternates that the GC must price as add / deduct values from the base bid.  A typed Alternates extractor + per-alternate cost rollup would close the last major scope-of-work classification gap.
- **Phase T6.x — Finishing.** Confidence-propagation cleanup for any remaining legacy paths, override UX polish, queue tuning.  Lower dollar-impact than T8 / T9 but tightens the auto-approve / hand-takeoff queues for real-world projects.

---

### Phase T3.5 — Generalise the dedupe-by-source-tag pattern

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit lifts the common skeleton out of `door_dedupe.py` (T3) and `window_dedupe.py` (T2.5) into a single parametrised scaffold. Both existing callers reduce to thin wrappers; the 53 pre-existing door + window dedupe tests pass byte-identical against the refactored modules. Suite: 386 → 397 passed (+11 new generic-scaffold tests; 1 skipped unchanged).

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **New module.** `core/extraction/dedupe.py` exports `dedupe_against_synthesis()` and `extract_mark_from_synthesized()`. The final signature is `dedupe_against_synthesis(items, *, source_tag: str, section_prefixes: tuple[str, ...], legacy_aggregate_patterns: tuple[re.Pattern[str], ...], family_label: str, mark_pattern: re.Pattern[str] | None = None, section_field: Literal["csi_division", "csi_section"] = "csi_section", match_family_by_description: bool = False) -> list[TakeoffItem]`. The proposed signature in the T3.5 brief gained two extra parameters and shed one — see *Asymmetries reconciled* below.
- **Asymmetries reconciled.** Doors and windows differed in three non-trivial ways that the scaffold now exposes as parameters: (1) **family field** — doors discriminate on `csi_division` (Division 08 catches everything), windows discriminate on `csi_section` (narrower `08 41`/`08 44`/`08 5*` prefixes). Encoded via `section_field: Literal["csi_division", "csi_section"]`. (2) **Description-based family fallback** — windows treat a row as in-family when its description matches the legacy-aggregate regex OR the mark regex, even with an empty/uncategorised section; doors do not. Encoded via `match_family_by_description: bool` (default False, doors's behaviour). (3) **Legacy-aggregate regex count** — doors carry two regexes (`<material> doors` + `Doors (type unspecified)`); windows carry one. Encoded as `legacy_aggregate_patterns: tuple[re.Pattern[str], ...]` so callers pass however many they need.
- **`mark_pattern` is optional.** When `None`, per-mark dedupe is disabled and only the legacy-aggregate path fires. Pinned by `test_mark_pattern_none_disables_per_mark_dedupe`. The doors and windows wrappers both pass it; this knob exists for future callers (e.g. site-utility aggregates where no mark exists per row).
- **`family_label` is reserved.** Currently informational only; the scaffold does not log or raise. Threaded through for future error attribution.
- **Wrappers preserved by name.** `dedupe_doors_against_synthesis(items)` and `dedupe_windows_against_synthesis(items)` keep their signatures unchanged — `core/takeoff.py` imports them by name and was not touched.
- **LOC delta.** Combined production code +60 lines (door_dedupe 179 → 82, window_dedupe 212 → 94, new dedupe.py 275; net `-97 - 118 + 275 = +60`). Smaller than the brief's "-100 LOC" prediction because the new module carries the consolidated module-level docstring + reconciliation notes for both families; offset by the same documentation being lifted out of the two wrappers. Net **logic** LOC is meaningfully smaller; the test surface gains 14 tests (~190 lines after stripping helpers) that pin the generic behaviour directly.
- **No third-party deps.** Pure-stdlib (`re`, `typing.Literal`).

**Subtle behaviours reconciled by the refactor:**
- Door dedupe checks `csi_division.startswith("08")` while window dedupe checks `csi_section.startswith(prefix)`. The unified scaffold runs the prefix match against the configured `section_field` only — it does NOT OR the two fields together. This is intentional: OR-ing would introduce *new* dedupe coverage on rows like `csi_division="", csi_section="08 11 13"` (which the legacy door code would have missed), changing behaviour in production paths that the test suite doesn't exercise. Strict per-field matching preserves byte-identical behaviour.
- The `extract_mark_from_synthesized` helper is guarded by the notes-prefix check (`item.notes.startswith(f"source={source_tag}")`). Callers can apply it indiscriminately to any item; non-synth rows return `None`. The original modules gated externally via `_is_synthesised(it)` before calling `_extract_synthesised_mark(it)`; the guard moves into the helper without changing the caller's behaviour.

**Tests added (`tests/test_dedupe_generic.py`):** 14 tests against a synthetic "fixture_schedule_prepass" family (made-up CSI Division 22 sections, made-up "Fixture <MARK>" description shape) so the generic surface is pinned without touching the door- or window-specific contracts:
1. Empty input → empty output.
2. No synth rows → input unchanged (identity preserved).
3. Synth row + matching legacy aggregate → aggregate dropped.
4. Synth row + matching same-mark LLM row → LLM row dropped.
5. Synth + non-matching items → all preserved, original order intact.
6. Out-of-family rows untouched regardless of dedupe state (both modes: with and without an active synth row).
7. Custom `source_tag` — the scaffold is tag-agnostic; using the wrong tag against the same items is a no-op.
8. `mark_pattern=None` disables per-mark dedupe; legacy-aggregate dropping still fires.
9. Row matching both aggregate regex AND a synthesised mark — dropped exactly once.
10. Multiple aggregate patterns — every supplied pattern is honoured.
11. `extract_mark_from_synthesized` helper — four unit tests (notes wins over desc; desc fallback when notes lack `mark=`; source_tag guard rejects mismatches; None notes + no mark_pattern → None).

The 53 pre-existing door + window tests (`tests/test_door_dedupe.py` + `tests/test_window_dedupe.py`) are byte-identical and untouched.

**Phase T4 readiness:** wiring a third family (finish schedule, panel schedule, RTU schedule, plumbing fixture schedule) is now a 5-line wrapper plus a synthesiser update. The `tests/test_dedupe_generic.py` fixture-schedule shape is a working template — a future T4 worker can copy it, swap the keywords + CSI prefixes, and ship.

---

### Phase T4 — Finish-schedule extraction + per-surface synthesis + dedupe

**Status:** SHIPPED — this commit landed the full finish slice (extraction → schema → prepass wire-in → per-surface synthesis → dedupe → reconcile wire-in) as the THIRD dispatcher on the door/window scaffold, mirroring the T1+T2+T2.5+T3+T3.5 pattern. Suite: 480 → 624 passed (+144 new tests; 1 skipped unchanged). Finish schedules are the highest-leverage T-phase deliverable so far because each `FinishRecord` fans out into 3-7 ``TakeoffItem``s (one per finished surface — floor, base, walls, ceiling) instead of the 1:1 mapping doors and windows use.

**Implementation notes (this commit):**
- **Module structure.** Three new modules: `core/extraction/finish_schedule.py` (T1-shape extractor, dataclasses + `to_schema()` bridge), `core/extraction/finish_dedupe.py` (THIN wrapper over the T3.5 scaffold, 80 LOC vs ~94 of post-refactor window_dedupe — see *T3.5 leverage realized* below), plus an extension of `core/extraction/takeoff_synthesis.py` adding `synthesize_finish_takeoff_items()` and `SYNTHESIS_SOURCE_TAG_FINISH = "finish_schedule_prepass"`. `core/schemas.py` gains `FinishRecord` + `FinishScheduleResult` Pydantic models and a new optional `DrawingPrepassResult.finish_schedule` field alongside the existing `door_schedule` + `window_schedule`.
- **Per-room expansion shape (the structural difference vs. T2/T2.5).** Each `FinishRecord` fans out:
  - **1 Floor** item when `floor_finish` is set
  - **1 Base** item when `base_finish` is set
  - **1 Wall** item when `wall_finishes == {"ALL": code}` OR all compass walls share a code; **N Wall** items (one per direction in stable `N → S → E → W` order) when codes differ
  - **1 Ceiling** item when `ceiling_finish` is set; `EXPOSED` / `OPEN` ceilings emit a marker row at `09 00 00` so the audit trail survives even if Phase T6 suppresses it from pricing
  - Typical commercial schedule: 1 record → **4 items** (uniform walls); a record with 4 distinct compass walls → **7 items** (1 floor + 1 base + 4 walls + 1 ceiling). A record with no finishes emits zero items.
- **Quantity = 0.0, unit = "SF".** Phase T6 will compute SF from a room area cross-reference (Phase T5 work). T4 emits the line with a unit, confidence, description, and notes so the takeoff sheet shows it and Phase T6 can fill the quantity.
- **CSI mapping decisions (per-surface family tables).**
  - **Floor (`_FLOOR_CSI_MAPPING`):** VCT / VINYL / LVT / LVP → `09 65 19`; SHEET VINYL / SHT VINYL → `09 65 16`; CPT / CARPET → `09 68 13`; TILE / CT / CER / PORC → `09 30 13`; HW / WD / WOOD → `09 64 29`; POL CONC / POL-CONC / POLISHED / SEAL CONC / SEAL-CONC / SEALED / SC / POL → **`03 35 43`** (cross-division). Unknown → `09 60 00`.
